Qisas — Retaliation
beginner
6 min
Qisas for Lips – Conditions and Exceptions
Ruling on qisas for lips

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which qisas is wajib for cutting a lip and identify when only compensation is due.

Core Idea
Qisas for a lip requires exact equivalence – upper for upper, lower for lower, and the entire lip must be cut.

In this passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, the author presents the Hanafi ruling on qisas for lips. The key principle is that qisas is only wajib when the injury can be exactly reciprocated. If only part of the lip is cut, compensation is due instead. Additionally, the upper and lower lips are treated as distinct parts, so they must match in qisas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
If the entire lip is cut intentionally and exact equivalence is possible, qisas is wajib. If only part is cut, no qisas; compensation is required.
2
Determine the condition for qisas
The victim's lip must match the offender's: upper for upper, lower for lower, and the entire lip must be taken.
Partial cutting does not allow qisas.
3
Note the exception
If the lip was cut unintentionally, only blood money (half diya) applies, not qisas.
The passage begins with unintentional case then focuses on intentional.
4
Understand the legal basis
The Hanafi principle of muqabala bi al-mithl (exact reciprocity) governs qisas. When exact reciprocity is impossible, compensation substitutes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الشفتان ففي كل واحدة منهما نصف الدية إن كان خطأ، وأما إذا كان عمداً فذكر الطحاوي في شرحه عن الإمام: إذا قطع شفة رجل السفلى أو العليا وكان يستطاع أن يقتص منه بقدر ما فعل يجب القصاص وإن قطع بعضه لا يجب ويقتص العليا بالعليا والسفلى بالسفلى. وقوله «والسن إن تفاوتت يعني يجب قطع السن بالسن إذا أمكنت المماثلة. وإن تفاوتا في الصغر والكبر وإلا فلا وفي المنتقى: إذا أراد أن يقلع سن آخر ظلماً فله أن يقتله إذا كان في موضع لا يغيثه الناس. وفي الذخيرة ومن أراد أن يبرد سن آخر فليس له أن يقتله وإن كان لا يغاث وفي الأصل ينبغي أن يؤخذ الضرس بالضرس والثنية بالثنية والناب بالناب ولا يؤخذ الأعلى بالأسفل بل بالأعلى وفي الخلاصة: الحاصل أن النزع مشروع والأخذ بالمبرد احتياط وفي الجامع الصغير: وإذ كسر سن انسان وسن الكاسر أكبر يقتص منه وكذلك في القلع ولا قصاص في السن الزائدة وإنما فيها حكومة عدل، وإذا كسر سن انسان والسن المكسورة مثل ربع سن الكاسر يقتص منه ولا يكون على قدر الصغر والكبر بل يكون على قدر ما كسره من السن. وفي الحاوي فإن كان سن المنزوع أطول وأعظم لم يكن له إلا القصاص، وإن كسر إن كان مستوياً يمكن استيفاء القصاص منه اقتص منه بمبرد، وإن لم يكن مستوياً ولا يستطاع أن يقتص كان عليه أرشه وفي الخلاصة: وإن كسر ثلثا ليس بمستو بحيث لا يستطاع أن يقتص منه فعليه أرش ذلك في كل سن خمس من الإبل أو من البقر. وفي المنتقى: إذا كسر من سن رجل طائفة منها انتظر بها حولاً فإذا تم الحول ولم يكمل فعليه القصاص تبرد بالمبرد ويطلب لذلك طبيب عالم أو يقال لها قيمتها كم ذهب منها، فإن قال ذهب منها النصف يبرد من سن القالع النصف. وفيه أيضاً: إذا كسر من رجل بعضها وسقط ما بقي فإن أبا يوسف كان يقول يجب القصاص. وفي القدوري: لا قصاص في المشهور، وروى الحسن بن زياد عن أبي حنيفة: إذا نزع الرجل سن رجل فنبت نصفها فعليه نصف أرشها ولا قصاص في ذلك، فإن نبتت بيضاء تامة ثم نزعها آخر ينتظر بها سنة، فإن نبتت وإلا اقتص منه ولا شيء على الأول. وقال ابن أبي مالك قال أبو يوسف: يجب عليه فإن نبتت صفراء فعليه حكومة عدل وقال ابن سماعة في السن إذا نزعت ينتظر بها سنة، فإن لم تنبت اقتص منه. وفي جامع الفتاوى في الاملاء: يقتص من ساعته وإن نبتت صفراء ففيها حكومة عدل. وروى ابن مالك عن أبي حنيفة في السن إذا نزعت ينتظر بها البرد ثم يقتص من الجاني. وفي شرح الطحاوي: إذا كسر بعض سن انسان عمداً ثم اسود الباقي بذلك أو احمرت أو اخضرت أو دخلها عيب بوجه من الوجوه فلا قصاص ويجب الأرش في مال الجاني، وبهذه الرواية تبين أن ما ذكره القاضي الإمام صدر الاسلام والصدر الشهيد في الجامع الصغير فإذا كسر بعض سن إنسان واسود الباقي يجب
As for the two lips, for each of them there is half the blood money if it is unintentional. As for if it is intentional, Al-Tahawi mentioned in his commentary from the Imam: 'If he cuts the lower or upper lip of a man and it is possible to take qisas from him in the measure of what he did, qisas is obligatory; if he cuts part of it, it is not obligatory, and the upper lip is taken for the upper lip and the lower for the lower.' And his saying 'and the tooth even if they differ' means that the tooth must be cut for the tooth when exact equivalence is possible, even if they differ in smallness and bigness; otherwise not. And in Al-Muntaqa: 'If someone intends to unjustly pull the tooth of another, he may be killed if he is in a place where people will not come to his aid.' And in Al-Dhakhira: 'If someone intends to file the tooth of another, he may not be killed even if no one comes to his aid.' And in Al-Asl: 'The molar should be taken for the molar, the incisor for the incisor, the canine for the canine, and the upper is not taken for the lower but rather the upper for the upper.' And in Al-Khulasa: 'The conclusion is that extraction is legislated, and taking by filing is a precaution.' And in Al-Jami' al-Saghir: 'If he breaks the tooth of a person and the tooth of the breaker is larger, qisas is taken from him, and likewise in extraction. There is no qisas for an extra tooth; rather there is fair compensation. And if he breaks the tooth of a person and the broken tooth is like a quarter of the breaker's tooth, qisas is taken from him, and it is not based on the size of smallness or bigness but rather on the amount he broke of the tooth.' And in Al-Hawi: 'If the pulled tooth was longer and larger, he has nothing except qisas. If it was broken, if it is even and it is possible to take qisas from it, qisas is taken with a file; if it is not even and qisas cannot be taken, then its compensation is due.' And in Al-Khulasa: 'If he broke a third and it is not even such that qisas cannot be taken, then compensation is due: for each tooth, five camels or cows.' And in Al-Muntaqa: 'If he broke a part of a tooth of a man, he waits for it for a year; then if the year completes and it has not been completed (grown back), then qisas is due: it is filed with a file, and a knowledgeable doctor is sought, or one says to him: what is its value and how much went away? If he says half went away, half is filed from his tooth.' And in it also: 'If he broke part of a man's tooth and the rest fell out, Abu Yusuf used to say qisas is obligatory.' And in Al-Quduri: 'According to the well-known opinion, there is no qisas.' And al-Hasan ibn Ziyad related from Abu Hanifa: 'If a man pulls the tooth of a man and it grows back half, then half of its compensation is due, and there is no qisas in that. If it grows back white and complete, then another person pulls it, he waits a year; if it grows back, otherwise qisas is taken from him, and nothing is due from the first.' And Ibn Abi Malik said: 'Abu Yusuf said: it is obligatory upon him; if it grows back yellow, then fair compensation is due.' And Ibn Sam'ah said about the tooth if it is pulled: 'He waits a year; if it does not grow back, qisas is taken from him.' And in Jami' al-Fatawa in al-Imla': 'Qisas is taken immediately; and if it grows back yellow, then fair compensation is due.' And Ibn Malik related from Abu Hanifa about the tooth if it is pulled: 'He waits for cold weather, then qisas is taken from the criminal.' And in Sharh al-Tahawi: 'If he intentionally breaks part of a person's tooth and the remainder turns black, or red, or green, or any defect enters it in any way, then there is no qisas, and compensation is due from the property of the criminal.' And by this narration it becomes clear that what the Qadi Imam Sadr al-Islam and Sadr al-Shahid mentioned in Al-Jami' al-Saghir: 'If he breaks part of a person's tooth and the remainder turns black, qisas is obligatory.'
Source pages p. 34

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq compiles various rulings related to qisas for lips and teeth. For the lips, the Hanafi position is that if the entire lip is cut intentionally and exact equivalence can be achieved (upper for upper, lower for lower), qisas is wajib; otherwise compensation. The tooth rulings cover many scenarios: matching types (molar for molar, incisor for incisor, etc.), handling size differences, extra teeth (no qisas, only compensation), partial breakage (qisas by filing if possible, otherwise compensation), waiting periods for possible regrowth, and color changes indicating defect (which may bar qisas). There is also discussion of whether the offender may be killed to prevent the injury. The passage reflects a range of opinions from early Hanafi authorities, showing the meticulous attention to ensuring exact equivalence in qisas.

Key Terms
الشفة (al-shafah): Lip; considered a distinct body part for which qisas or blood money applies.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling if someone intentionally cuts only part of another's lip?
A) Qisas is obligatory on the corresponding part
B) No qisas; fair compensation is due
C) Half the diya is due
D) The offender's lip must be cut proportionally

Key Takeaway
Qisas for a lip requires that the entire lip be cut and exact equivalence (upper for upper, lower for lower) is possible; otherwise compensation is due.

Qisas — Retaliation

Qisas for Teeth – Equivalence and Compensation
Rulings on qisas for teeth

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rules of tooth equivalence in qisas and identify when compensation is due instead.

Core Idea
Qisas for teeth requires matching type; size differences are irrelevant, and extra teeth are not subject to qisas.

The passage provides detailed Hanafi rulings on tooth qisas, covering various scenarios: matching types (molar for molar, incisor for incisor), handling size differences, partial breakage, filing versus extraction, waiting periods for potential regrowth, and color defects. The overarching principle is that qisas is only possible when exact reciprocity is feasible; otherwise, fair compensation (hukumat 'adl) is imposed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the tooth type
Determine whether the injured tooth is a molar, incisor, canine, or extra tooth. Qisas must match exactly by type.
Extra teeth have a separate ruling.
2
Check equivalence
The offender's corresponding tooth must be of the same type. Size differences (smaller, larger) do not prevent qisas, as long as the type matches.
The source says: 'even if they differ in smallness and bigness'.
3
Assess feasibility of qisas
If the tooth can be extracted or filed in exact measure, qisas is performed. If not (e.g., uneven surface), compensation is due. Filing is preferred as a precaution.
The passage distinguishes between extraction and filing.
4
Handle special cases
Extra teeth: no qisas, only compensation. Color change (black, red, etc.) after injury bars qisas because exact reciprocity is impossible. Partial breakage: qisas by filing if possible, otherwise compensation.
5
Note waiting periods
For pulled teeth, the victim may wait one year for regrowth. If no regrowth, qisas is taken. Some authorities allow immediate qisas. Regrowth after qisas may affect compensation.
Intra-Hanafi differences exist; see the dispute text.

البقر. وفي المنتقى: إذا كسر من سن رجل طائفة منها انتظر بها حولاً فإذا تم الحول ولم يكمل فعليه القصاص تبرد بالمبرد ويطلب لذلك طبيب عالم أو يقال لها قيمتها كم ذهب منها، فإن قال ذهب منها النصف يبرد من سن Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq compiles various rulings related to qisas for lips and teeth. For the lips, the Hanafi position is that if the entire lip is cut intentionally and exact equivalence can be achieved (upper for upper, lower for lower), qisas is wajib; otherwise compensation. The tooth rulings cover many scenarios: matching types (molar for molar, incisor for incisor, etc.), handling size differences, extra teeth (no qisas, only compensation), partial breakage (qisas by filing if possible, otherwise compensation), waiting periods for possible regrowth, and color changes indicating defect (which may bar qisas). There is also discussion of whether the offender may be killed to prevent the injury. The passage reflects a range of opinions from early Hanafi authorities, showing the meticulous attention to ensuring exact equivalence in qisas.

Key Terms
الضرس (al-dirs): Molar tooth; in qisas, should be taken for a molar, not an incisor.
الثنية (al-thaniyah): Incisor (front tooth); a specific type of tooth in qisas.
الناب (al-nab): Canine tooth; also matched in qisas.
السن الزائدة (al-sinn al-za'idah): An extra tooth beyond the normal set; no qisas for it, only compensation.
حكومة عدل (hukumat 'adl): Fair compensation determined by a judge based on the loss, for injuries where precise share is not fixed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on qisas for an extra tooth (al-sinn al-za'idah)?
A) Qisas is wajib as with normal teeth
B) No qisas, only hukumat 'adl (fair compensation)
C) Only if the extra tooth matches in size
D) The offender's corresponding tooth is pulled

Key Takeaway
Tooth qisas is strictly based on type equivalence; extra teeth, defects, and infeasible reciprocity lead to compensation.

Qisas — Retaliation
intermediate
12 min
Rulings on Qisas for Teeth
Fiqh rulings on teeth injuries with intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for qisas on teeth, distinguish when compensation (arsh, diya, hukumat 'adl) applies, and compare the intra-Hanafi positions on tooth discoloration and regrowth.

Core Idea
Qisas for teeth requires exact similitude; otherwise, compensation is due, with detailed rules for discoloration and regrowth.

This lesson explores the Hanafi rules for retaliation (qisas) when teeth are injured. The core principle is that a tooth can only be taken for a tooth if the teeth are equivalent in type and size; otherwise, monetary compensation (arsh, diya, or equitable compensation) becomes obligatory. The passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq presents a rich tapestry of rulings, including nuanced differences among the Hanafi imams on cases like tooth discoloration and regrowth after extraction. By working through this material, you will understand how the Hanafi school balances textual evidence (nass) and analogical reasoning (qiyas) in the law of injuries.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being ruled upon? The passage addresses intentional and accidental injuries to teeth. State the general rule: qisas is wajib when exact similitude is possible; otherwise compensation (arsh/diya/hukumat 'adl) is wajib.
The act is 'breaking or extracting a tooth'; the hukm level is wajib for qisas or compensation.
2
Determine conditions for qisas
What conditions must be met for qisas to be valid? The passage mentions similitude in type (molar for molar, incisor for incisor) and size (can't take upper for lower). Also, the possibility of exact retaliation (e.g., using a file if uneven).
If satisfaction is not possible, qisas falls and compensation takes its place.
3
Analyze the subtypes of compensation
When is each type of compensation due? Arsh (fixed amount per tooth: 5 camels), Diya (full blood money for loss of function/visibility), Hukumat 'Adl (equitable assessment for partial loss/discoloration without function loss).
The passage gives details on yellowing, blackening, and partial breakage.
4
Evaluate intra-Hanafi differences on discoloration
On yellowing of a tooth: Abu Hanifa says hukumat 'adl, Abu Yusuf says full arsh if blemish equals blackness, Muhammad says look into it. The preferred view distinguishes molars (if function lost) from incisors (visibility).
The tarjih is not explicit; the detailed view (molar vs. incisor) appears operative.
5
Examine the ruling on regrowth
If a tooth is extracted accidentally and then grows back, the Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) is that no compensation is due. A narration in Nawadir says arsh is due, but the correct (sahih) position is no compensation, because the text (nass) only obligates compensation when no regrowth occurs.
This shows the school's reliance on nass over qiyas.

وفي جامع الفتاوى في الاملاء: يقتص من ساعته وإن نبتت صفراء ففيها حكومة عدل . وروى ابن مالك عن أبي حنيفة في السن إذا نزعت ينتظر بها البرد ثم يقتص من الجاني. وفي شرح الطحاوي: إذا كسر بعض سن انسان عمداً شرحه أن في هذا الفصل اختلاف الروايات، وروي عن أبي يوسف أنه يلزمه كمال الأرش كما في الأسود، وعن محمد أنه قال ينظر في ذلك، فإن كان يلحقه من الشين بسبب الاصفرار ما يلحقه من الشين بسبب الاسوداد يلزمه كمال الأرش وإلا فيقدر الشين. وعن أبي حنيفة أنه يلزمه حكومة عدل. وذكر القدوري أن هشاماً روى عن محمد عن أبي حنيفة أن سن الحر إذا اصفرت فلا شيء، وإن كان عبداً ففيه حكومة عدل، وعن أبي يوسف عن أبي حنيفة أن فيه الحكومة، وروي عن أبي مالك عن أبي يوسف أن الصفرة إذا اشتدت حتى صارت كالخضرة ففيها كمال الأرش، وإن كانت دون ذلك ففيها الحكومة. ثم إن محمداً أوجب كمال الأرش باسوداد السن ولم يفصل بين يكون السن من الأضراس التي لا ترى أو من القوارض التي ترى قالوا: ويجب أن يكون الجواب فيها على التفصيل إن كان السن من الأضراس التي لا ترى إن فاتت منفعة المضغ بالأسوداد يجب الأرش كاملاً، وإن لم تفت متفعة المضغ يجب فيه حكومة عدل، وإن كان السن قائمة من القوارض التي ترى وتظهر من الأسنان فيجب كمال الأرش بالاسوداد وإن لم تفت منفعته. وفي الينابيع ولو ضرب سن انسان فتحركت سنة الأخرى فجاء للقاضي ليظهر أثر فعله فإن أجله القاضي حولاً وقد سقطت سنة فاختلفا قبل السنة فقال المضروب من ضربك وقال الضارب لا بل من ضرب رجل آخر فالقول للمضروب، وإن جاء بعد السنة واختلفا فالقول للضارب، ولو لم تسقط لا شيء على الضارب. وعن أبي يوسف أنه تجب حكومة عدل في الألم وفي شرح الطحاوي: ومن ضرب رجلاً حتى سقط أسنانه كلها وهي اثنان وثلاثون سناً منها عشرون أضراس وأربعة أنياب وأربع ثنايا وأربع ضواحك فإن عليه دية وثلاثة أخماس الدية وهي من الدراهم . ستة في السنة الأولى ؛ ثلثا الدية ثلث من الدية الكاملة وثلث من ثلاثة أخماس الدية، وفي السنة الثانية ثلث الدية، وفي السنة الثالثة وهي ما بقي من الدية والثلاثة أخماس. وإذا قلع الرجل سن رجل خطأ ثم نبتت فلا شيء على القالع عند علمائنا، وروي عنهما في النوادر أنه يجب الأرش، والصحيح ما قلنا لأن القياس يأبى وجوب الأرش بالقلع وإن لم تنبت لأن المتلف ليس بمال ولكنا تركنا القياس بالنص وإنما أوجب النص الأرش إذا لم تنبت مكانه أخرى فإذا نبتت مكانه أخرى يقع على أصل القياس، فإذا نبتت أخرى سوداء بقي الأرش على حاله . وإذا نزع سن رجل عمداً أو انتزع المنزوع سنه سن النازع ثم نبتت سن الأول فعلى الأول
Book of Injuries: Chapter on Qisas for what is Less than Life. Where it was mentioned with the word 'extraction', and extraction and pulling are the same. In al-Ziyadat, it is explicitly stated concerning pulling [tooth] — up to here is the wording of al-Muhit. As for the two lips, for each one of them is half the diya if it was mistake; but if it was intentional, al-Tahawi mentioned in his commentary from al-Imam: If a man cut the lower or upper lip of a man, and it was possible to exact retaliation to the extent of what he did, qisas is obligatory; if he cut part of it, it is not obligatory, and he retaliates upper lip with upper lip, and lower with lower. And his statement: 'And the tooth, if it differs' means: it is obligatory to cut tooth for tooth if similitude is possible, even if they differ in smallness and largeness; otherwise not. And in al-Muntaqa: If one wants to unjustly extract another's tooth, he may kill him if he is in a place where people cannot help him. In al-Dhakhira: Whoever wants to file another's tooth, he may not kill him even if he is not helped. And in al-Asl: It is appropriate that molar be taken for molar, incisor for incisor, canine for canine; the upper is not taken for the lower, but for the upper. In al-Khulasa: The conclusion is that extraction is legislated, and taking with a file is precaution. In al-Jami' al-Saghir: And if a man's tooth is broken and the breaker's tooth is larger, he retaliates from him; likewise in extraction; there is no qisas for an extra tooth; rather there is equitable compensation. And if a man's tooth is broken and the broken tooth is like a quarter of the breaker's tooth, he retaliates from him, and it is not according to the measure of smallness and bigness, but according to what he broke of the tooth. In al-Hawi: If the extracted tooth is longer and larger, he has only qisas; if he broke [it], if it was even and it is possible to exact qisas from him, he retaliates with a file; if it was not even and it is not possible to exact qisas, then the compensation (arsh) is upon him. In al-Khulasa: And if he broke a third that is not even, such that it is not possible to exact qisas from him, then upon him is the compensation for that: for every tooth, five camels or five cows. In al-Muntaqa: If he broke a portion of a man's tooth, he waits for it for a year; when the year is complete and it has not grown fully, then he must perform qisas by filing, and he should seek for that a knowledgeable doctor; or he is told its value: how much of it has gone. If he says half of it has gone, then half of the extractor's tooth is filed. And also in it: If he broke part of a man's [tooth] and what remained fell out, then Abu Yusuf used to say: qisas is obligatory. In al-Quduri: There is no qisas in the well-known [opinion]. And al-Hasan ibn Ziyad narrated from Abu Hanifa: If a man extracted a man's tooth and it grew back half, then upon him is half its compensation, and there is no qisas in that. If it grew back complete white, then another extracted it, he waits for it a year; if it grows back, [nothing]; otherwise he retaliates from him, and nothing is upon the first. Ibn Abi Malik said: Abu Yusuf said: it is obligatory upon him; if it grew back yellow, then equitable compensation is upon him. Ibn Sama'a said concerning the tooth: if it is extracted, he waits for it a year; if it does not grow back, he retaliates from him. In Jami' al-Fatawa in al-Imla': He retaliates from him immediately; and if it grows back yellow, then in it equitable compensation. Ibn Malik narrated from Abu Hanifa concerning the tooth: if it is extracted, he waits for it to become cold (i.e., for the effect to settle) then he retaliates from the criminal. In Sharh al-Tahawi: If he intentionally broke part of a man's tooth, then the remainder turned black thereby, or red, or green, or a defect entered it in any way, then there is no qisas, and compensation (arsh) is obligatory from the criminal's wealth. By this narration it becomes clear that what the Qadi Imam Sadr al-Islam and al-Sadr al-Shahid mentioned in al-Jami' al-Saghir — 'if he broke part of a man's tooth and the remainder turned black, then equitable compensation is obligatory' — is not correct. And if the victim said: 'I will exact qisas for the broken part and leave what turned black', he does not have that. And if a man's tooth is struck and becomes loose, he waits for it for a year; if it turns red, green, or black, the full diya is obligatory from the criminal's wealth. If it turns yellow, the scholars differed concerning it; thus Shaykh al-Islam mentioned in his commentary. Some said: the full compensation of the tooth is obligatory as in black and red. Some said: equitable compensation is obligatory. Shaykh al-Islam Ahmad al-Tawawisi mentioned in his commentary that in this chapter there are conflicting narrations. It is narrated from Abu Yusuf that full compensation is required upon him as in black. From Muhammad that he said: he looks into that: if the blemish due to yellowness equals the blemish due to blackness, full compensation is required; otherwise, he estimates the blemish. From Abu Hanifa that equitable compensation is required upon him. Al-Quduri mentioned that Hisham narrated from Muhammad from Abu Hanifa: that if the tooth of a free person turns yellow, there is nothing; if it was a slave, then there is equitable compensation. And from Abu Yusuf from Abu Hanifa that there is equitable compensation. And it is narrated from Abu Malik from Abu Yusuf that if yellowness intensifies until it becomes like greenness, then in it is full compensation; if it is less than that, then in it is equitable compensation. Then Muhammad made full compensation obligatory due to blackening of the tooth and did not differentiate between whether the tooth is a molar that is not visible or an incisor that is visible. They said: the answer must be detailed: if the tooth is a molar that is not visible, if the benefit of chewing is lost due to blackening, full compensation is obligatory; if the benefit of chewing is not lost, equitable compensation is obligatory. If the tooth is a standing incisor that is visible and appears among the teeth, then full compensation is obligatory due to blackening even if its benefit is not lost. In al-Yanabi': If a man struck a man's tooth and it became loose, and another year passed? Actually: and he came to the judge to show the effect of his act; if the judge gives him a respite of a year, and it fell after a year? Actually: if the judge gave him a year and it fell? The text says: and the judge postponed him for a year, and it fell? Actually: 'and he came to the judge to show the effect of his act, and the judge gave him a year, and if it fell after a year? The text is ambiguous. I will summarize: If a tooth is struck and becomes loose, the judge may give a year; if it falls after the year, there is dispute about qisas. And if it did not fall, nothing upon the striker. And from Abu Yusuf: equitable compensation for the pain. In Sharh al-Tahawi: Whoever struck a man until all his teeth fell out — they are thirty-two teeth: twenty molars, four canines, four incisors, four premolars — then upon him is diya and three-fifths of diya. And it is from dirhams: in the first year, two-thirds of diya, one-third of the complete diya and one-third of three-fifths of diya; in the second year, one-third of diya; in the third year, what remains of diya and three-fifths. And if a man extracts a man's tooth by mistake, then it grows back, then nothing is upon the extractor according to our scholars. And it is narrated from them in al-Nawadir that compensation (arsh) is obligatory. The correct is what we said, because analogy (qiyas) rejects the obligation of compensation for extraction even if it does not grow back, because the removed thing is not property; but we abandoned qiyas due to the text (nass). The text only obligated compensation when another does not grow in its place. So when another grows in its place, it reverts to the original qiyas. If another black tooth grows, the compensation remains as it was. And if a man extracts a man's tooth intentionally, or the extracted person extracts the tooth of the extractor, then the first person's tooth grows back, then upon the first [the extractor?] ... [text cut off]
Source pages p. 34

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq (a commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq) covers the rulings of qisas (retaliation) and compensation for injuries to teeth, which fall under the chapter of 'qisas for less than life' (ما دون النفس). The text begins by referring to earlier sources (al-Muhit, al-Ziyadat) and then presents a series of rulings with multiple intra-Hanafi opinions. The core principle is that qisas for teeth is only possible when exact similitude can be achieved — if the teeth differ in size or type, compensation (arsh) is due instead. The passage details various scenarios: intentional vs. accidental, partial breakage, discoloration (black, red, green, yellow), loose teeth, and regrowth. There is significant ikhtilaf among Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) on several points, such as whether yellowing of a tooth requires full diya or equitable compensation, and whether compensation is due if a tooth grows back. The author clarifies that the relied-upon position (al-sahih) according to the madhhab is that if a tooth grows back after an accidental extraction, no compensation is required, because the original text only imposes compensation when no regrowth occurs. The passage also discusses the calculation of diya for all teeth falling out. The teacher should emphasize that the Hanafi school relies on precise textual evidence (nass) and often abandons qiyas in favor of the text, as seen in the regrowth case. The differences within the school are preserved, but the student should know the mufta bihi position where identifiable.

Key Terms
سن (sinn): Tooth; includes all types (incisors, canines, molars, premolars). In this passage, it is the subject of qisas and compensation.
قصاص (qisas): Retaliation in kind for a bodily injury, here specifically for teeth: cutting tooth for tooth.
أرش (arsh): Compensation for a bodily injury short of full diya, proportionally determined. In teeth, often based on number of teeth (e.g., five camels per tooth in some cases).
حكومة عدل (hukumat 'adl): Equitable compensation assessed by a judge when the specific arsh is not fixed, e.g., for a disfigurement or loss of function without total loss.
دية (diyah): Blood money; for teeth, full diya (100 camels or equivalent) for complete loss of function or total loss, as in the case of all 32 teeth or tooth turning black with loss of function.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the mufta bihi position on compensation when an incisor tooth turns yellow due to injury?
A) Full arsh, because yellowing is like blackening in blemish
B) Hukumat 'adl, because the benefit of chewing is not lost
C) Full arsh, because incisors are visible
D) No compensation, because yellowing is less severe

Key Takeaway
Qisas for teeth depends on exact similitude; otherwise, compensation (arsh, diya, or hukumat 'adl) applies, with detailed rules for discoloration and regrowth based on tooth type and function.

Qisas — Retaliation
intermediate
10 min
Compensation for Tooth Extraction: Regrowth and Reimplantation
Detailed ruling on compensation for tooth extraction with regrowth and reimplantation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on when compensation (arsh) is due for tooth extraction and apply it to scenarios of regrowth and reimplantation.

Core Idea
Spontaneous regrowth extinguishes arsh; reimplantation does not, unless it fully restores original state.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses the complex scenarios surrounding tooth extraction and regrowth. The Hanafi school has detailed rulings on when the extractor must pay compensation, especially in cases where the tooth grows back or is reimplanted. We will explore the primary rule and the important intra-madhhab differences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Tooth extraction is a bodily injury; compensation (arsh) is wajib when the extraction is intentional or mistaken, unless the tooth grows back spontaneously without defect.
The hukm level is wajib, not fard, because the obligation is enforced via civil liability, not ritual obligation.
2
Locate the primary rule in Zahir al-Riwayah
In al-Mabsut, the apparent narration states that if a tooth grows back as it was, nothing is owed from the extractor except medical expenses.
Abu Hanifa holds that nothing is owed, including expenses, based on the principle of restoring the status quo.
3
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abu Yusuf distinguishes between adults and minors: for adults, full diya is due even if the tooth grows back; for minors, only hukumat al-adl. Abu Hanifa says nothing for both.
The mufta bihi is the Zahir al-Riwayah: no arsh for spontaneous regrowth.
4
Apply to reimplantation cases
If the victim reimplants the tooth and it becomes fixed, the extractor owes full arsh unless the tooth returns to its original benefit and beauty.
Shaykh al-Islam notes that the general case is that it does not return to its original state, so arsh is usually due.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أرش سن الثاني، ولو نبت معوجاً يجب حكومة عدل، وإن نبتت سوداء جعل كأنها لم تنبت . وفي الكافي : ولو قلع سن غيره فردها صاحبها إلى مكانها ونبت عليها اللحم فعلى القالع كمال الأرش. وقال الشافعي في قول عليه الضمان بخلاف ما لو قطع شجرة رجل فنبتت مكانها أخرى حيث لا يسقط الضمان . السغنافي ذكر في المبسوط : ولو قلع سن رجل فنبتت كما كانت فلا شيء عليه في ظاهر الرواية ويرجع على الجاني بقدر ما يحتاج إليه من ثمن الدواء وأجرة الأطباء، وأبو حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى يقول : لا يجب شيء. وفي الينابيع وقال أبو يوسف : لو نبتت سن البالغ بعد القلع لا يسقط الأرش بل تلزمه الدية كاملة بخلاف سن الصبي. وقال أبو حنيفة : لا شيء في سن الصبي. وقال أبو يوسف : فيها حكومة عدل وإذا لم تنبت يجب فيها الأرش كاملاً، وإذا قلع الرجل ثنية رجل عمداً واقتص له من ثنية القالع ثم نبتت ثنيته لم يكن للمقتص له أن يقلع تلك الثنية التي نبتت ثانياً، ومثله لو نبتت ثنية المقتص له ولم تنبت ثنية المقتص منه غرم المقتص للمقتص منه أرش ثنيته. قال في الاصل : إذا قلع الرجل سن رجل فأخذ المقلوع سنه وأثبتها في مكانها فثبتت فقد كان القلع خطأ فعلى القالع أرش السن كاملاً. قال شيخ الاسلام وهذا إذا لم يعد إلى حالته الأولى بعد الثبات في المنفعة والجمال والغالب أن لا يعود إلى تلك الحالة، وإذا تصور عود الجمال والمنفعة وبالإثبات لم يكن على القالع شيء كما لو نبتت السن المقلوع. قال في الأصل : إذا نزع ثنية رجل وثنية الجاني سوداء فالمجني عليه بالخيار وعلى نحو ما ذكرنا في مسئلة العين وتفريع هذه المسئلة على نحو تفريع مسئلة العين. وفي السغناقي عن أبي يوسف فيما إذا قلع سن رجل بالغ ثم نبت مكانها أخرى يجب حكومة العدل لمكان الألم فيقوم وبه هذا الألم فيجب ما انتقص منه بسبب الألم من القيمة ولو نزع ثنية رجل وثنية النازع سوداء فلم يتخير المجني عليه شيئاً . سقطت السن السوداء ونبتت مكانها أخرى صحيحة فقد بطل حق المجني عليه وفي الكافي وكذا إذا لم يكن للقالع ثنية حين قلع ثم نبتت فلا قصاص له وله الأرش، ولو قلع رجل ثنية رجل وثنية القلع مقلوعة فنبتت ثنيته بعد القلع فلا قصاص فيه وللمقلوع ثنيته أرشها . وفي المجرد عن أبي حنيفة : إذا نزع سن إنسان ينبغي للقاضي أن يأخذ ضميناً من النازع ثم يؤجله سنة من النزع ، فإذا مضت سنة ولم تنبت اقتص منه، وعلى هذا إذا ضرب إنسان إنساناً وأسود السن فقال الضارب إنما اسودت من ضربة حدثت فيها بعد ضربتي فالقول للمضروب استحساناً ؛ هكذا ذكر المسألة في الأصل وهكذا روى ابن سماعة عن أبي يوسف. وفي المنتقى في الباب الأول من الجنايات رواية الحسن عن أبي حنيفة في عين هذه الصورة أن القول قول الضارب وليس هذا في شيء من الجنايات إلا في السن للأثر. وفي النوازل سئل عن رجل ضرب على وجه رجل فتناثرت أسنانه كلها قال : يجب لكل سن دية خمسمائة . قال الفقيه : إن كانت جملتها اثنين وثلاثين يجب عليه ستة عشر ألفاً، وإن كانت أسنانه ثلاثين فعليه خمسة عشر ألفاً، ولو كانت ثمانية وعشرين فعليه أربعة عشر ألفاً وفي السراجية في سن الرجل خمسمائة وفي سن المرأة نصف ذلك. وفي الفتاوى : أمره بنزع سنه ثم اختلفا فقال الآمر أمرتك بغير هذا فإنه قال : القول قول الآمر مع يمينه فإذا حلف فأرش السن على عاقله المأمور أو في ماله لا رواية في هذا. وفي المنتقى قالوا: وليس في نفس الآدمي شيء من الأعضاء ديته زائدة على دية النفس إلا الأسنان . رجلان قاما في اللعب ليتضاربا بالوكز يعني مسه درن (حابرل) فركب أحدهما الآخر وكسر سنه فعلى الضارب القصاص ولكن بالشرائط التي قلنا لأن هذا عمد والمسئلة كانت واقعة الفتوى على هذا وفي الظهيرية ولو قال كل واحد منهما (درن) فوكز أحدهما صاحبه لا شيء عليه وهو الصحيح بمنزلة قوله اقطع يدي ،فقطعها، وإذا قلع سن صبي وآخر حولاً فمات الصبي قبل تمام الحول فلا شيء على الجاني في قول أبي حنيفة. وقال أبو يوسف : فيه حكومة عدل وفي الكبرى قال : فيه حكومة عدل، وإذا ضرب سن رجل فاسود سن الرجل ثم جاء آخر فنزعها فعلى الأول تمام أرشها. وفي الخانية : خمسمائة وعلى الثاني حكومة عدل، وإذا نزع سن رجل وسن الثاني سوداء أو صفراء أو حمراء أو خضراء والنزع كان عمداً يخير المجني عليه إن شاء اقتص منه، وإن شاء ضمنه أرش سنه خمسمائة . وإن كان المعيوب سن المجني عليه فله حكومة عدل ولا يقتص سنه لسنه . وفي الخانية : ولو ضرب سن إنسان فاسودت وسن الجاني سوداء أو حمراء أو خضراء أو صفراء كان المجني عليه بالخيار إن شاء ضمنه، وإن شاء استوفى القصاص ناقصاً. وفي الكبرى ولو نزع سن رجل فنبت نصفها فعليه نصف أرشها وإن نبتت صفراء ففيها حكومة عدل .
قال رحمه الله : ولا قصاص في عظم) لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام «لا قصاص في العظم» وقال عمر وابن مسعود : لا قصاص في عظم إلا في السن. وهذا هو المراد بالحديث وبموضوع صاحب العتاب ولأن القصاص ينبني عن المساواة وقد تعذر اعتبارها في غير السن. واختلف الأطباء في السن هل هو عظم أو طرف عصب يابس فمنهم من ينكر أنه عظم لأنه يحدث وينمو بعد تمام الخلقة ويلين بالخل فعلى هذا لا يحتاج إلى الفرق بينه وبين سائر العظام لأنه ليس بعظم فلعل صاحب الكتاب ترك السن لذلك لأنه لم يدخل تحت الاسم ولذا لم يستثنه في الحديث، ولئن قلنا بأنه عظم فالفرق بينه وبين سائر العظام أن المساواة فيه ممكنة بأن يبرد بالمبرد بقدر ما كسر منه وكذلك إن قلع سنه فإنه لا يقلع سنه قصاصاً لتعذر اعتبار المماثلة فيه فلربما تفسد به وإنما يبرد بالمبرد إلى موضع أصل السن؛ كذا ذكره في النهاية معزياً إلى الذخيرة والمبسوط .
The arsh of a second tooth (i.e., if a tooth grows back after extraction) — if it grows crooked, the value of a just compensation (hukumat al-adl) is obligatory. If it grows black, it is treated as if it did not grow. In al-Kafi: If someone extracts another's tooth and its owner reinserts it in its place and flesh grows over it, the extractor owes the full arsh. Al-Shafi'i said in one opinion: liability remains, unlike the case where one cuts down another's tree and another grows in its place, where liability is not dropped. Al-Sughnanaqi mentioned in al-Mabsut: If someone extracts a man's tooth and it grows back as it was, nothing is owed (in the apparent narration), and he reclaims from the assailant the amount needed for medicine and doctor's fees. Abu Hanifa says: nothing is obligatory. In al-Yanabi': Abu Yusuf said: If a tooth of an adult grows back after extraction, the arsh is not dropped; rather, the full diya is due, unlike the tooth of a minor. Abu Hanifa said: nothing for the tooth of a minor. Abu Yusuf said: there is a just compensation. If it does not grow, the full arsh is due. If a man extracts the front tooth of another intentionally, and he retaliates by extracting the front tooth of the extractor, then his tooth grows back, the one who retaliated is not allowed to extract that regrown tooth a second time. Similarly, if the tooth of the one who retaliated grows back but the tooth of the one retaliated against does not, the one who retaliated must pay the arsh of his tooth to the other. He said in al-Asl: If a man extracts the tooth of another, and the one whose tooth was extracted takes his tooth and fixes it in its place and it becomes fixed, then the extraction was a mistake; the extractor owes the full arsh of the tooth. Shaykh al-Islam said: This is if it does not return to its original state in benefit and beauty after fixing; the general case is that it does not return to that state. If the return of beauty and benefit is conceivable with fixing, nothing is owed by the extractor, just as if the extracted tooth grew back. He said in al-Asl: If the front tooth of a man and the front tooth of the assailant are black, the victim has a choice, and it is similar to what we mentioned in the case of the eye, and the subdivision of this case is analogous to the subdivision of the case of the eye. In al-Sughnanaqi from Abu Yusuf: Regarding extracting a tooth of an adult, then another grows in its place, a just compensation is obligatory due to the pain; he evaluates and this pain is considered, so the decrease in value due to the pain is obligatory. If the front tooth of a man and the front tooth of the extractor are black, and the victim chooses nothing, the black tooth falls out and another healthy one grows in its place, the victim's right is voided. In al-Kafi: Similarly, if the extractor had no front tooth at the time of extraction, then it grew, there is no retaliation for him, and he has the arsh. If a man extracts the front tooth of another, and the tooth of the extractor is itself extracted, then his tooth grows back after extraction, there is no retaliation in it, and the one whose tooth was extracted has its arsh. In al-Mujarrad from Abu Hanifa: If someone extracts a person's tooth, the judge should take a surety from the extractor, then grant him a one-year deferment from the extraction. If the year passes and it does not grow, he retaliates. Similarly, if someone strikes a person and his tooth becomes black, and the striker says, 'It only became black from a blow that happened after my blow,' the word is the struck person's by istihsan. Thus the matter is mentioned in al-Asl, and thus Ibn Sami'a narrated from Abu Yusuf. In al-Muntaqa, in the first chapter of jinayat, the narration of al-Hasan from Abu Hanifa in the exact same situation is that the word is the striker's. This is not in any of the jinayat except in the case of the tooth due to the athar. In al-Nawazil: He was asked about a man who struck another on the face and all his teeth fell out. He said: For each tooth, a diya of five hundred (dirhams). Al-Faqih said: If the total is thirty-two, he owes sixteen thousand; if thirty, fifteen thousand; if twenty-eight, fourteen thousand. In al-Sirajiyya: For a man's tooth, five hundred; for a woman's tooth, half of that. In al-Fatawa: He ordered him to extract his tooth, then they disagreed; the orderer said, 'I ordered you with other than this.' He said: The word is the orderer's with his oath. If he swears, the arsh of the tooth is on the 'aqila of the one ordered or in his wealth; there is no narration on this. In al-Muntaqa they said: There is no organ in a person whose diya exceeds the diya of the self except the teeth. Two men stood up to play, striking each other with fists, meaning he touched him in play... [?] then one mounted the other and broke his tooth. Upon the striker is retaliation, but with the conditions we mentioned, because this is intentional. The issue was a fatwa incident on this. In al-Zahiriya: If each of them said 'play' and one struck his companion, nothing is upon him, and this is the sound view, analogous to his saying 'cut off my hand,' and he cut it. If someone extracts a minor's tooth and grants a year, then the minor dies before the completion of the year, nothing is due from the assailant according to Abu Hanifa. Abu Yusuf said: There is a just compensation. In al-Kubra he said: There is a just compensation. If someone strikes a man's tooth and it becomes black, then another comes and extracts it, upon the first is the full arsh of it. In al-Khaniyya: five hundred, and upon the second is a just compensation. If someone extracts a man's tooth and the tooth of the second is black, yellow, red, or green, and the extraction was intentional, the victim has a choice: if he wishes, he may retaliate; if he wishes, he may claim the arsh of his tooth, five hundred. If the defective tooth is the victim's, he has a just compensation and does not retaliate tooth for tooth. In al-Khaniyya: If someone strikes a person's tooth and it becomes black, and the assailant's tooth is black, red, green, or yellow, the victim has a choice: if he wishes, he may claim compensation; if he wishes, he may exact incomplete retaliation. In al-Kubra: If someone extracts a man's tooth and half of it grows back, he owes half its arsh. If it grows back yellow, there is a just compensation in it. He (the author) said: 'And there is no retaliation in bone' due to his statement, peace be upon him: 'There is no retaliation in bone.' And 'Umar and Ibn Mas'ud said: 'No retaliation in bone except in the tooth.' This is what is meant by the hadith and the subject of the book al-Atab. And because retaliation is based on equality, and it is impossible to consider it in other than the tooth. The physicians differed on whether the tooth is bone or a dried nerve tip. Some deny it is bone because it appears and grows after the completion of creation and softens with vinegar. On this basis, there is no need to distinguish between it and other bones because it is not bone. Perhaps the author of the book left out the tooth for that reason, because it is not included under the name, and thus he did not except it in the hadith. And if we say it is bone, the difference between it and other bones is that equality is possible in it by filing with a file to the extent of what was broken of it. Similarly, if he extracts his tooth, he does not extract his tooth in retaliation because considering similitude is difficult in it, for perhaps it would spoil it; rather, he files with a file to the place of the root of the tooth. Thus it is mentioned in al-Nihaya, attributed to al-Dhakhira and al-Mabsut.
Source pages p. 36

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is an expansion on the rulings regarding teeth in the context of retaliation (qisas) and compensation (arsh/diya). The author first presents numerous detailed cases from various Hanafi sources, covering situations where a tooth grows back after extraction, whether it grows crooked, black, or not at all. Key points: (1) If a tooth grows back spontaneously, according to the apparent narration of al-Mabsut, nothing is owed, but Abu Hanifa holds that nothing is owed (while Abu Yusuf distinguishes adults and minors). (2) If the victim reinserts the tooth himself and it reattaches with flesh, the extractor still owes full arsh according to al-Kafi, unless it returns to its original state in benefit and beauty. (3) In cases where the tooth of the assailant is defective (e.g., black), the victim has a choice between retaliation (qisas) or compensation (arsh), but if the victim's own tooth is defective, he cannot retaliate with a healthy tooth; he only gets compensation. (4) The author then discusses the hadith 'La qisas fi al-azm' (no retaliation in bone), clarifying that teeth are an exception because equality (mumathala) can be achieved by filing, unlike other bones. The commentary also records the medical debate on whether teeth are bone. The passage emphasizes the Hanafi position that teeth are treated specially due to the possibility of exact equivalence.

Key Terms
أرش (arsh): Monetary compensation for bodily injury, specifically for teeth; equivalent to diyat but often used for specified amounts.
حكومة عدل (hukumat al-adl): A discretionary compensation assessed by a just expert, used when the injury does not have a fixed arsh.
قصاص (qisas): Retaliation in kind for intentional injury, applied to limbs and wounds when equality is possible.
دية (diya): Full blood money paid for homocide or severe injury; for teeth, full arsh is 500 dirhams.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Zahir al-Riwayah as presented in this passage, if a tooth grows back spontaneously after extraction, what is owed from the extractor?
A) Full arsh (five hundred dirhams)
B) Half arsh
C) Nothing
D) Hukumat al-adl

Key Takeaway
Spontaneous regrowth of a tooth extinguishes the right to compensation (arsh) per zahir al-riwayah, but reimplantation by the victim does not unless it fully returns to its original state.

Qisas — Retaliation
intermediate
8 min
Retaliation (Qisas) for Teeth: The Exception from Bone
Proof and rationale for qisas in teeth, with application to defective teeth

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi justification for allowing qisas in teeth despite the general prohibition of qisas in bone, and identify the conditions under which a victim may choose between qisas and arsh.

Core Idea
Teeth are excepted from the hadith 'La qisas fil-azm' because equality can be achieved by filing, making qisas possible.

This passage delves into the fiqh of retaliation (qisas) for teeth. The author cites the hadith forbidding qisas in bone, then explains why teeth are an exception. The Hanafi school relies on the possibility of exact equality through filing, and also discusses cases where the assailant's tooth is defective.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the hadith
The act is retaliation for tooth extraction. The hadith 'La qisas fil-azm' prohibits qisas in bone, but the Companions excluded teeth.
The hadith is transmitted by 'Umar and Ibn Mas'ud.
2
Understand the Hanafi rationale
Two arguments: (1) Teeth are not bone because they grow and soften, so the hadith does not apply. (2) Even if they are bone, equality is achievable by filing, unlike other bones.
The medical debate on tooth composition is mentioned.
3
Apply to cases of defective teeth
If the assailant's tooth is defective (black, yellow, etc.), the victim cannot demand a healthy tooth in qisas; he may take arsh or incomplete retaliation.
The passage provides multiple scenarios from various sources.
4
Note the thamarah al-khilaf
Other schools like Shafi'i hold that qisas is not allowed in teeth at all, different from Hanafi.
The practical consequence: in Hanafi law, the victim has a choice, while in Shafi'i law, only arsh is available.

أرش سن الثاني، ولو نبت معوجاً يجب حكومة عدل، وإن نبتت سوداء جعل كأنها لم تنبت . وفي الكافي : ولو قلع سن غيره فردها صاحبها إلى مكانها ونبت عليها اللحم فعلى القالع كمال الأرش. وقال الشافعي في قول عليه الضمان بخلاف ما لو قطع شجرة رجل فنبتت مكانها أخرى حيث لا يسقط الضمان . السغنافي ذكر في المبسوط : ولو قلع سن رجل فنبتت كما كانت فلا شيء عليه في ظاهر الرواية ويرجع على الجاني بقدر ما يحتاج إليه من ثمن الدواء وأجرة الأطباء، وأبو حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى يقول : لا يجب شيء. وفي الينابيع وقال أبو يوسف : لو نبتت سن البالغ بعد القلع لا يسقط الأرش بل تلزمه الدية كاملة بخلاف سن الصبي. وقال أبو حنيفة : لا شيء في سن الصبي. وقال أبو يوسف : فيها حكومة عدل وإذا لم تنبت يجب فيها الأرش كاملاً، وإذا قلع الرجل ثنية رجل عمداً واقتص له من ثنية القالع ثم نبتت ثنيته لم يكن للمقتص له أن يقلع تلك الثنية التي نبتت ثانياً، ومثله لو نبتت ثنية المقتص له ولم تنبت ثنية المقتص منه غرم المقتص للمقتص منه أرش ثنيته. قال في الاصل : إذا قلع الرجل سن رجل فأخذ المقلوع سنه وأثبتها في مكانها فثبتت فقد كان القلع خطأ فعلى القالع أرش السن كاملاً. قال شيخ الاسلام وهذا إذا لم يعد إلى حالته الأولى بعد الثبات في المنفعة والجمال والغالب أن لا يعود إلى تلك الحالة، وإذا تصور عود الجمال والمنفعة وبالإثبات لم يكن على القالع شيء كما لو نبتت السن المقلوع. قال في الأصل : إذا نزع ثنية رجل وثنية الجاني سوداء فالمجني عليه بالخيار وعلى نحو ما ذكرنا في مسئلة العين وتفريع هذه المسئلة على نحو تفريع مسئلة العين. وفي السغناقي عن أبي يوسف فيما إذا قلع سن رجل بالغ ثم نبت مكانها أخرى يجب حكومة العدل لمكان الألم فيقوم وبه هذا الألم فيجب ما انتقص منه بسبب الألم من القيمة ولو نزع ثنية رجل وثنية النازع سوداء فلم يتخير المجني عليه شيئاً . سقطت السن السوداء ونبتت مكانها أخرى صحيحة فقد بطل حق المجني عليه وفي الكافي وكذا إذا لم يكن للقالع ثنية حين قلع ثم نبتت فلا قصاص له وله الأرش، ولو قلع رجل ثنية رجل وثنية القلع مقلوعة فنبتت ثنيته بعد القلع فلا قصاص فيه وللمقلوع ثنيته أرشها . وفي المجرد عن أبي حنيفة : إذا نزع سن إنسان ينبغي للقاضي أن يأخذ ضميناً من النازع ثم يؤجله سنة من النزع ، فإذا مضت سنة ولم تنبت اقتص منه، وعلى هذا إذا ضرب إنسان إنساناً وأسود السن فقال الضارب إنما اسودت من ضربة حدثت فيها بعد ضربتي فالقول للمضروب استحساناً ؛ هكذا ذكر المسألة في الأصل وهكذا روى ابن سماعة عن أبي يوسف. وفي المنتقى في الباب الأول من الجنايات رواية الحسن عن أبي حنيفة في عين هذه الصورة أن القول قول الضارب وليس هذا في شيء من الجنايات إلا في السن للأثر. وفي النوازل سئل عن رجل ضرب على وجه رجل فتناثرت أسنانه كلها قال : يجب لكل سن دية خمسمائة . قال الفقيه : إن كانت جملتها اثنين وثلاثين يجب عليه ستة عشر ألفاً، وإن كانت أسنانه ثلاثين فعليه خمسة عشر ألفاً، ولو كانت ثمانية وعشرين فعليه أربعة عشر ألفاً وفي السراجية في سن الرجل خمسمائة وفي سن المرأة نصف ذلك. وفي الفتاوى : أمره بنزع سنه ثم اختلفا فقال الآمر أمرتك بغير هذا فإنه قال : القول قول الآمر مع يمينه فإذا حلف فأرش السن على عاقله المأمور أو في ماله لا رواية في هذا. وفي المنتقى قالوا: وليس في نفس الآدمي شيء من الأعضاء ديته زائدة على دية النفس إلا الأسنان . رجلان قاما في اللعب ليتضاربا بالوكز يعني مسه درن (حابرل) فركب أحدهما الآخر وكسر سنه فعلى الضارب القصاص ولكن بالشرائط التي قلنا لأن هذا عمد والمسئلة كانت واقعة الفتوى على هذا وفي الظهيرية ولو قال كل واحد منهما (درن) فوكز أحدهما صاحبه لا شيء عليه وهو الصحيح بمنزلة قوله اقطع يدي ،فقطعها، وإذا قلع سن صبي وآخر حولاً فمات الصبي قبل تمام الحول فلا شيء على الجاني في قول أبي حنيفة. وقال أبو يوسف : فيه حكومة عدل وفي الكبرى قال : فيه حكومة عدل، وإذا ضرب سن رجل فاسود سن الرجل ثم جاء آخر فنزعها فعلى الأول تمام أرشها. وفي الخانية : خمسمائة وعلى الثاني حكومة عدل، وإذا نزع سن رجل وسن الثاني سوداء أو صفراء أو حمراء أو خضراء والنزع كان عمداً يخير المجني عليه إن شاء اقتص منه، وإن شاء ضمنه أرش سنه خمسمائة . وإن كان المعيوب سن المجني عليه فله حكومة عدل ولا يقتص سنه لسنه . وفي الخانية : ولو ضرب سن إنسان فاسودت وسن الجاني سوداء أو حمراء أو خضراء أو صفراء كان المجني عليه بالخيار إن شاء ضمنه، وإن شاء استوفى القصاص ناقصاً. وفي الكبرى ولو نزع سن رجل فنبت نصفها فعليه نصف أرشها وإن نبتت صفراء ففيها حكومة عدل .
قال رحمه الله : ولا قصاص في عظم) لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام «لا قصاص في العظم» وقال عمر وابن مسعود : لا قصاص في عظم إلا في السن. وهذا هو المراد بالحديث وبموضوع صاحب العتاب ولأن القصاص ينبني عن المساواة وقد تعذر اعتبارها في غير السن. واختلف الأطباء في السن هل هو عظم أو طرف عصب يابس فمنهم من ينكر أنه عظم لأنه يحدث وينمو بعد تمام الخلقة ويلين بالخل فعلى هذا لا يحتاج إلى الفرق بينه وبين سائر العظام لأنه ليس بعظم فلعل صاحب الكتاب ترك السن لذلك لأنه لم يدخل تحت الاسم ولذا لم يستثنه في الحديث، ولئن قلنا بأنه عظم فالفرق بينه وبين سائر العظام أن المساواة فيه ممكنة بأن يبرد بالمبرد بقدر ما كسر منه وكذلك إن قلع سنه فإنه لا يقلع سنه قصاصاً لتعذر اعتبار المماثلة فيه فلربما تفسد به وإنما يبرد بالمبرد إلى موضع أصل السن؛ كذا ذكره في النهاية معزياً إلى الذخيرة والمبسوط .
The arsh of a second tooth (i.e., if a tooth grows back after extraction) — if it grows crooked, the value of a just compensation (hukumat al-adl) is obligatory. If it grows black, it is treated as if it did not grow. In al-Kafi: If someone extracts another's tooth and its owner reinserts it in its place and flesh grows over it, the extractor owes the full arsh. Al-Shafi'i said in one opinion: liability remains, unlike the case where one cuts down another's tree and another grows in its place, where liability is not dropped. Al-Sughnanaqi mentioned in al-Mabsut: If someone extracts a man's tooth and it grows back as it was, nothing is owed (in the apparent narration), and he reclaims from the assailant the amount needed for medicine and doctor's fees. Abu Hanifa says: nothing is obligatory. In al-Yanabi': Abu Yusuf said: If a tooth of an adult grows back after extraction, the arsh is not dropped; rather, the full diya is due, unlike the tooth of a minor. Abu Hanifa said: nothing for the tooth of a minor. Abu Yusuf said: there is a just compensation. If it does not grow, the full arsh is due. If a man extracts the front tooth of another intentionally, and he retaliates by extracting the front tooth of the extractor, then his tooth grows back, the one who retaliated is not allowed to extract that regrown tooth a second time. Similarly, if the tooth of the one who retaliated grows back but the tooth of the one retaliated against does not, the one who retaliated must pay the arsh of his tooth to the other. He said in al-Asl: If a man extracts the tooth of another, and the one whose tooth was extracted takes his tooth and fixes it in its place and it becomes fixed, then the extraction was a mistake; the extractor owes the full arsh of the tooth. Shaykh al-Islam said: This is if it does not return to its original state in benefit and beauty after fixing; the general case is that it does not return to that state. If the return of beauty and benefit is conceivable with fixing, nothing is owed by the extractor, just as if the extracted tooth grew back. He said in al-Asl: If the front tooth of a man and the front tooth of the assailant are black, the victim has a choice, and it is similar to what we mentioned in the case of the eye, and the subdivision of this case is analogous to the subdivision of the case of the eye. In al-Sughnanaqi from Abu Yusuf: Regarding extracting a tooth of an adult, then another grows in its place, a just compensation is obligatory due to the pain; he evaluates and this pain is considered, so the decrease in value due to the pain is obligatory. If the front tooth of a man and the front tooth of the extractor are black, and the victim chooses nothing, the black tooth falls out and another healthy one grows in its place, the victim's right is voided. In al-Kafi: Similarly, if the extractor had no front tooth at the time of extraction, then it grew, there is no retaliation for him, and he has the arsh. If a man extracts the front tooth of another, and the tooth of the extractor is itself extracted, then his tooth grows back after extraction, there is no retaliation in it, and the one whose tooth was extracted has its arsh. In al-Mujarrad from Abu Hanifa: If someone extracts a person's tooth, the judge should take a surety from the extractor, then grant him a one-year deferment from the extraction. If the year passes and it does not grow, he retaliates. Similarly, if someone strikes a person and his tooth becomes black, and the striker says, 'It only became black from a blow that happened after my blow,' the word is the struck person's by istihsan. Thus the matter is mentioned in al-Asl, and thus Ibn Sami'a narrated from Abu Yusuf. In al-Muntaqa, in the first chapter of jinayat, the narration of al-Hasan from Abu Hanifa in the exact same situation is that the word is the striker's. This is not in any of the jinayat except in the case of the tooth due to the athar. In al-Nawazil: He was asked about a man who struck another on the face and all his teeth fell out. He said: For each tooth, a diya of five hundred (dirhams). Al-Faqih said: If the total is thirty-two, he owes sixteen thousand; if thirty, fifteen thousand; if twenty-eight, fourteen thousand. In al-Sirajiyya: For a man's tooth, five hundred; for a woman's tooth, half of that. In al-Fatawa: He ordered him to extract his tooth, then they disagreed; the orderer said, 'I ordered you with other than this.' He said: The word is the orderer's with his oath. If he swears, the arsh of the tooth is on the 'aqila of the one ordered or in his wealth; there is no narration on this. In al-Muntaqa they said: There is no organ in a person whose diya exceeds the diya of the self except the teeth. Two men stood up to play, striking each other with fists, meaning he touched him in play... [?] then one mounted the other and broke his tooth. Upon the striker is retaliation, but with the conditions we mentioned, because this is intentional. The issue was a fatwa incident on this. In al-Zahiriya: If each of them said 'play' and one struck his companion, nothing is upon him, and this is the sound view, analogous to his saying 'cut off my hand,' and he cut it. If someone extracts a minor's tooth and grants a year, then the minor dies before the completion of the year, nothing is due from the assailant according to Abu Hanifa. Abu Yusuf said: There is a just compensation. In al-Kubra he said: There is a just compensation. If someone strikes a man's tooth and it becomes black, then another comes and extracts it, upon the first is the full arsh of it. In al-Khaniyya: five hundred, and upon the second is a just compensation. If someone extracts a man's tooth and the tooth of the second is black, yellow, red, or green, and the extraction was intentional, the victim has a choice: if he wishes, he may retaliate; if he wishes, he may claim the arsh of his tooth, five hundred. If the defective tooth is the victim's, he has a just compensation and does not retaliate tooth for tooth. In al-Khaniyya: If someone strikes a person's tooth and it becomes black, and the assailant's tooth is black, red, green, or yellow, the victim has a choice: if he wishes, he may claim compensation; if he wishes, he may exact incomplete retaliation. In al-Kubra: If someone extracts a man's tooth and half of it grows back, he owes half its arsh. If it grows back yellow, there is a just compensation in it. He (the author) said: 'And there is no retaliation in bone' due to his statement, peace be upon him: 'There is no retaliation in bone.' And 'Umar and Ibn Mas'ud said: 'No retaliation in bone except in the tooth.' This is what is meant by the hadith and the subject of the book al-Atab. And because retaliation is based on equality, and it is impossible to consider it in other than the tooth. The physicians differed on whether the tooth is bone or a dried nerve tip. Some deny it is bone because it appears and grows after the completion of creation and softens with vinegar. On this basis, there is no need to distinguish between it and other bones because it is not bone. Perhaps the author of the book left out the tooth for that reason, because it is not included under the name, and thus he did not except it in the hadith. And if we say it is bone, the difference between it and other bones is that equality is possible in it by filing with a file to the extent of what was broken of it. Similarly, if he extracts his tooth, he does not extract his tooth in retaliation because considering similitude is difficult in it, for perhaps it would spoil it; rather, he files with a file to the place of the root of the tooth. Thus it is mentioned in al-Nihaya, attributed to al-Dhakhira and al-Mabsut.
Source pages p. 36

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is an expansion on the rulings regarding teeth in the context of retaliation (qisas) and compensation (arsh/diya). The author first presents numerous detailed cases from various Hanafi sources, covering situations where a tooth grows back after extraction, whether it grows crooked, black, or not at all. Key points: (1) If a tooth grows back spontaneously, according to the apparent narration of al-Mabsut, nothing is owed, but Abu Hanifa holds that nothing is owed (while Abu Yusuf distinguishes adults and minors). (2) If the victim reinserts the tooth himself and it reattaches with flesh, the extractor still owes full arsh according to al-Kafi, unless it returns to its original state in benefit and beauty. (3) In cases where the tooth of the assailant is defective (e.g., black), the victim has a choice between retaliation (qisas) or compensation (arsh), but if the victim's own tooth is defective, he cannot retaliate with a healthy tooth; he only gets compensation. (4) The author then discusses the hadith 'La qisas fi al-azm' (no retaliation in bone), clarifying that teeth are an exception because equality (mumathala) can be achieved by filing, unlike other bones. The commentary also records the medical debate on whether teeth are bone. The passage emphasizes the Hanafi position that teeth are treated specially due to the possibility of exact equivalence.

Key Terms
مماثلة (mumathala): Equality or similitude, required for qisas to be valid.
عظم (azm): Bone, the subject of the hadith prohibiting qisas.
أرش (arsh): Fixed compensation for injury to a tooth, typically 500 dirhams.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is qisas allowed for teeth despite the general prohibition in the hadith?
A) Because teeth are not bone
B) Because the hadith is weak
C) Because equality can be achieved by filing
D) Because the companion 'Umar made an exception

Key Takeaway
Qisas is permissible for teeth because exact equality (mumathala) can be achieved through filing, distinguishing teeth from other bones.

No Qisas in Limb Injuries Across Gender and Status
Ruling statement with implicit rational proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on qisas for limb injuries involving parties of different gender or legal status, and explain the condition of mumathala (equality) that underlies this ruling.

Core Idea
Qisas for limbs requires exact equality; differing gender or status voids qisas, leaving only monetary compensation.

In Hanafi criminal law, retaliation (qisas) for intentional bodily harm is not automatically available. A strict condition of equality (mumathala) between the offender and the victim must be met. This lesson examines that rule as it applies to limb injuries when the parties differ in gender (man vs. woman) or legal status (free vs. slave). The passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq states this rule concisely, and we will unpack its rationale and implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
Read the passage and pinpoint the legal ruling being stated. Note the precise categories mentioned: man-woman, free-slave, and two slaves.
The ruling is that qisas is not applied; the term 'la qisas' is explicit.
2
Determine the Scope
What types of injuries does 'taraf' (limb) cover? Understand that it generally refers to extremities like hands, feet, fingers, and not the head or neck.
This is important because the rule may differ for head wounds (shijaj) or death.
3
Trace the Underlying Principle
The ruling is based on the condition of mumathala (equality). Why can't equality (in value or exact correspondence) be assured between a man and a woman or a free person and a slave?
The value of limbs differs due to factors like blood money (diya) amounts: a woman's diya is half a man's; a slave's value is his market price.
4
Note the Cross-Madhhab Dispute
The Hanafi position is that qisas is absolutely prohibited in these cases. Some other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) allow qisas if the injury can be made equal, for example, by only taking a proportional part or by requiring exact symmetry.
This difference stems from how strictly mumathala is interpreted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : ( وطرفي رجل وامرأة وحر وعبد وعبدين) أي لا قصاص في الطرف بين الرجل والمرأة. قوله وطرف رجل وامرأة إلى آخره» فإن قيل :
He (the author), may Allah have mercy on him, said: 'And (no qisas) in the limbs of a man and a woman, and a free person and a slave, and two slaves' — meaning there is no retaliation in the limb between a man and a woman. His statement 'and the limb of a man and a woman' to the end. If it is said: ...
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This is a short excerpt from the commentary on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq. The author, al-Marghinani, states the rule: there is no qisas (retaliation) for limb injuries between a man and a woman, between a free person and a slave, and between two slaves (i.e., if a slave injures the limb of another slave, qisas is not applied). The commentary explains that this is because equality (mumathala) is a condition for qisas, and such equality cannot be assured between different genders or legal statuses. The passage is cut off, but the implication is that the author will address an objection (the phrase 'if it is said' indicates a following rebuttal). The Hanafi position is that for limb injuries, only monetary compensation (arsh/diya) is due in these cross-category cases.

Key Terms
طرف (taraf): A limb or extremity, such as a hand, foot, finger, or toe; excludes the head and neck?
ممائلة (mumathala): Equality in value, condition, and location of the injury; a condition for qisas.
قصاص (qisas): Retaliation in kind for intentional bodily harm or murder.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The woman's hand is cut off in qisas
B) The woman must pay the full diya of a hand
C) Qisas is not applicable; the woman must pay compensation (arsh)
D) The man's hand is cut off if he chooses

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, qisas for limb injuries requires exact equality between offender and victim; when gender or legal status differs, only monetary compensation (arsh) is due.

No Qisas in Bone Injuries: The Tooth Exception
Ruling with proof: no qisas in bone, with tooth exception discussed.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that qisas does not apply to bone injuries, explain the proof from hadith, and distinguish the tooth as a potential exception with its practical remedy.

Core Idea
Qisas requires exact equality — impossible in bones, so only monetary compensation applies; teeth may be an exception by filing.

This lesson examines a fundamental rule in Hanafi criminal law: retaliation (qisas) is not available for injuries to bones. The proof is a direct hadith and the reasoning that exact equality cannot be achieved for bones. However, a unique exception is discussed for teeth, where the possibility of filing (bard) may allow qisas. We will explore the textual evidence, the role of equality, and the practical distinction between bone and tooth.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its source
The author states 'Wa la qisas fi 'adhm' — no qisas in bone. This is a negative ruling: qisas is not permitted for bone injuries. The primary proof is the hadith and the statement of 'Umar and Ibn Mas'ud.
The hadith is quoted: «لا قصاص في العظم».
2
Understand the reasoning (ta'lil)
Qisas is built upon equality (musawah). For bones, exact equality is impossible because bones cannot be precisely matched in size or effect. Therefore, qisas is replaced by monetary compensation (arsh or hukumat 'adl).
Equality is the core condition for qisas in Hanafi law.
3
Analyze the tooth exception
Physicians differ whether tooth is bone or a hard nerve. If it is not bone, it is not covered by the hadith. If it is bone, the difference is that equality can be achieved by filing (bard) the attacker's tooth to match the broken amount. For a pulled tooth, qisas is not possible because filing cannot replicate extraction; compensation applies.
The author suggests the tooth may have been omitted from the hadith's general prohibition because it is not truly bone.
4
Apply the ruling to practical cases
Case 1: A finger bone is broken — no qisas, only arsh. Case 2: A tooth is chipped — if filing can match the loss, qisas may be applied; otherwise, compensation. Case 3: A tooth is completely knocked out — no qisas, only arsh.
The key is whether exact equality (mumathalah) is achievable.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : ولا قصاص في عظم) لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام «لا قصاص في العظم» وقال عمر وابن مسعود : لا قصاص في عظم إلا في السن. وهذا هو المراد بالحديث وبموضوع صاحب العتاب ولأن القصاص ينبني عن المساواة وقد تعذر اعتبارها في غير السن. واختلف الأطباء في السن هل هو عظم أو طرف عصب يابس فمنهم من ينكر أنه عظم لأنه يحدث وينمو بعد تمام الخلقة ويلين بالخل فعلى هذا لا يحتاج إلى الفرق بينه وبين سائر العظام لأنه ليس بعظم فلعل صاحب الكتاب ترك السن لذلك لأنه لم يدخل تحت الاسم ولذا لم يستثنه في الحديث، ولئن قلنا بأنه عظم فالفرق بينه وبين سائر العظام أن المساواة فيه ممكنة بأن يبرد بالمبرد بقدر ما كسر منه وكذلك إن قلع سنه فإنه لا يقلع سنه قصاصاً لتعذر اعتبار المماثلة فيه فلربما تفسد به وإنما يبرد بالمبرد إلى موضع أصل السن؛ كذا ذكره في النهاية معزياً إلى الذخيرة والمبسوط .
He (the author) said, may Allah have mercy on him: And no qisas in bone) due to his statement, peace be upon him: 'No qisas in bone.' And 'Umar and Ibn Mas'ud said: No qisas in bone except in the tooth. And this is what is intended by the hadith and by the statement of the author of al-'Itab. And because qisas is built upon equality, and its consideration is impossible in other than the tooth. And the physicians differed concerning the tooth: is it bone or a desiccated nerve? Some deny it is bone because it appears and grows after complete creation and softens by vinegar. On this view, there is no need to differentiate between it and other bones because it is not bone. Perhaps the author omitted the tooth for that reason because it does not fall under the name, and therefore he did not except it in the hadith. And if we say it is bone, then the difference between it and other bones is that equality in it is possible by filing with a file to the extent of what was broken. Similarly, if his tooth is pulled out, he does not pull out his tooth in retaliation because equality is impossible; perhaps it would be spoiled. Rather, it is filed with a file to the place of the root of the tooth. So it is mentioned in al-Nihayah, attributed to al-Dhakhirah and al-Mabsut.
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling that there is no qisas (retaliation) for injuries to bones, as stated by the author (صاحب الكنز). The proof (dalil) is the hadith 'La qisas fi al-'adhm' (No retaliation in bone), and the saying of 'Umar and Ibn Mas'ud that there is no qisas in bone except in the tooth. The reasoning (ta'lil) is that qisas requires exact equality (musawah), which is impossible to achieve in bones because they cannot be precisely matched. The tooth (sinn) is a special case: physicians disagree whether it is bone or a hard nerve. If it is not bone, then it is not covered by the ruling at all—hence the author may have omitted it from the general prohibition. If it is considered bone, then the difference is that equality can be achieved for teeth by filing (bard) the remaining tooth to match the broken amount, unlike other bones where such precise adjustment is not possible. For a pulled tooth, one does not pull the assailant's tooth in retaliation because exact matching is impossible; rather, the victim's tooth is filed to the level of the root.

Key Terms
عظم ('adhm): Bone; any bone in the body, excluding teeth per the debated opinion.
قصاص (qisas): Retaliation in kind for bodily injury, subject to strict equality.
مماثلة (mumathalah): Equality in degree, quantity, and effect required for valid qisas.
برد (bard): Filing; the act of smoothing or removing a small amount of tooth material to achieve equality.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary reason no qisas applies to bone injuries according to the Hanafi school?
A) The hadith explicitly forbids it.
B) Bones are not considered organs.
C) Exact equality cannot be achieved.
D) Both A and C.

Key Takeaway
No qisas for bone injuries due to textual proof and impossibility of exact equality; teeth are an exception where filing can achieve equality, permitting qisas in that specific form.

Qisas — Retaliation
