No Qisas in Limbs Between Man/Woman, Free/Slave, Two Slaves
Ruling that qisas is not applicable for limbs between parties of different legal status due to value disparity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school denies qisas for limbs between persons of different legal status and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument based on the general verse.

Core Idea
Qisas for limbs requires exact value equality; gender and status disparities create legal doubt (shubhah) that bars retaliation.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses a critical point of disagreement between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools: whether qisas (retaliation) applies when a limb is injured between a man and a woman, a free person and a slave, or two slaves. The Hanafi position holds that it does not, due to inherent value differences. However, the commentator presents and critiques the proof offered by earlier Hanafi scholars, leaving the reader with an unresolved challenge. In this lesson, we will unpack the legal reasoning and the debate surrounding the Hanafi reliance on the hadith of 'Imran ibn Husayn.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling: no qisas for limbs between man/woman, free/slave, or two slaves, because limbs are treated as wealth (mal) and value disparity prevents exact equality (mumathalah).
The Hanafi view is based on the principle that qisas requires precise equivalence; any doubt (shubhah) in equality bars it.
2
Identify the opponent and their proof
The Shafi'i school (implied) argues from the general Quranic verse 'The eye for the eye, the ear for the ear' (5:45), which appears to demand qisas in all cases of limb injury regardless of status.
The opponent also raises an analogy: if a paralyzed limb is cut off, qisas is done with a healthy limb, so why not cut a woman's limb for a man's?
3
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response uses two arguments: (1) Limbs are like wealth, so absolute value disparity matters, unlike functional deficiency (paralysis). (2) The general verse is specified by the hadith of 'Imran ibn Husayn, where the Prophet did not apply qisas between two slaves.
The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq then critiques this specification: the hadith only covers slaves, and the verse remains qat'i (definitive) because its specification for harbi/musta'min is by separate, unconnected speech, so it cannot be specified by ahad hadith.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Under Hanafi fiqh, a woman cutting a man's hand pays diyah (half a man's diyah) or arsh; under Shafi'i, qisas would be applied if the injury is equivalent.
This affects legal outcomes in real cases, especially in jurisdictions applying classical fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : ( وطرفي رجل وامرأة وحر وعبد وعبدين) أي لا قصاص في الطرف بين الرجل والمرأة. قوله وطرف رجل وامرأة إلى آخره» فإن قيل : سلمنا وجود التفاوت في القيمة في الأطراف وأنه يمنع الاستيفاء لكن المعقول منه منع استيفاء الأكمل بالأنقص دون العكس فإن الشلاء نقطع بالصحيحة وأنتم لا تقطعون يد المرأة بيد الرجل ولا يد عبد بحر والجواب أنا قد ذكرنا أن الأطراف يسلك بها مسلك الأموال لأنها خلقت وقاية للأنفس كالمال فالواجب أن يعتبر التفاوت المالي شائعاً مطلقاً والشلل ليس منه فيعتبر من جهتة الأكمل؛ كذا في العناية. ولا مماثلة بين طرفي الذكر والأنثى المماثلة مانعاً للتفاوت وبينهما في القيمة بتقسيم الشارع ولا بين الحر والعبد ولا بين العبدين للتفاوت في القيمة، وإن تساويا فيها بالظن فصار شبهة منع القصاص فإن قيل : إن استقام عدم في الحر والعبد لم يستقم بين العبدين لإمكان تساوي قيمتهما بتقويم المقومين أجيب بأن التساوي إنما يكون بالحزر والظن والمماثلة المشروطة شرعاً لا تثبت بذلك كالمماثلة في الأموال الربوية بخلاف طرفي الحرين لأن استوائهما متيقن بتقويم الشرع، وبخلاف الأنفس لأن الخلاف فيها متعلق بإزهاق الروح ولا تفاوت فيه قال صاحب الكفاية : فإن قيل قوله تعالى والعين بالعين والاذن بالاذن ﴾ [المائدة : ٤٥] مطلق يتناول موضع النزاع فيكون حجة عليكم قلنا : قد خص منه الحربي والمستأمن والعام إذا خص منه شيء يجوز تخصيصه بخبر الواحد فخصصناه بما روي عن عمران بن حصين أنه قال : قطع عبد لقوم فقراء أذن عبد لقوم أغنياء فاختصموا إلى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فلم يقض بالقصاص اهـ. أقول : فيه نظر؛ أما أولاً فلأنه قد نقرر في علم الأحوال أن النص العام إذا خص منه شيء بكلام مستقل موصول به يكون ذلك العام المخصص منه البعض ظنياً في الباقي فيجوز تخصيصه بخبر الواحد، وأما إذا خرج من النص العام شيء مما هو مفصول عنه غير موصول به فلا يكون ذلك ظنياً في الباقي بل يكون باقياً على حالته الأولى، ولا شك أن مخرج الحربي والمستأمن من الآية المذكورة ليس بكلام موصول بها فتكون باقية على قطيعتها الأصلية فلا يجوز تخصيصها بخبر الواحد، وقد مر منا غير مرة نظير هذا النظر في محاله. وأما ثانياً فلأن حديث عمران بن حصين إنما يفيد عدم جريان القصاص في الأطراف بين العبدين ولا يفيد عدم جريانه فيما بين الرجل والمرأة ولا بين الحر والعبد فبقي الاعتراض بإطلاق الآية المذكورة في هاتين الصورتين ولم يتم الجواب .
He (the author) said, may Allah have mercy on him: And (no qisas in) the limbs of a man and a woman, and a free and a slave, and two slaves) i.e., no qisas in the limb between a man and a woman. His statement: 'And limb of a man and a woman' etc. Then it is said: We accept that there exists disparity in value in limbs and that it prevents extraction, but what is understood from it is the prevention of extracting the more complete for the less complete, not the opposite, for we cut the paralyzed with the healthy, but you do not cut a woman's hand for a man's hand nor a slave's hand for a free person's hand. The answer: We have mentioned that limbs are treated like wealth because they are created as a protection for lives like wealth, so it is necessary to consider financial disparity absolutely, and paralysis is not from that, so it is considered from the side of the more complete. Thus in al-'Inayah. And there is no similitude between the limbs of male and female; similitude is prevented by disparity, and between them in value by the division of the Lawgiver, nor between free and slave, nor between two slaves due to disparity in value, even if they are equal in estimation, so it becomes a doubt that prevents qisas. Then it is said: If the lack of qisas is consistent in the free and slave, it is not consistent between two slaves because their values can be equal by the estimation of valuers. The answer: Equality is only by conjecture and estimation, and the similitude required by the Law is not established by that, like similitude in ribawi properties; unlike the limbs of two free men because their equality is certain by the lawgiver's estimation, and unlike lives because the dispute there concerns taking life and there is no disparity in it. The author of al-Kifayah said: Then it is said: The verse of Allah 'The eye for the eye, and the ear for the ear' (5:45) is general, including the place of dispute, so it is an argument against you. We say: It has been specified by excluding the harbi and musta'min, and a general text when something is specified from it, it becomes permissible to specify it by khabar wahid. So we specified it by what is narrated from 'Imran ibn Husayn that he said: A slave of poor people cut the ear of a slave of rich people, and they brought the case to the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, and he did not rule qisas. I say: There is consideration; first, because we have established in the science of conditions that a general text from which something is specified by an independent connected speech becomes zanni in the remainder, so it is permissible to specify it by khabar wahid. But if something is removed from the general text in a separate, unconnected speech, then it does not become zanni in the remainder but remains in its original state. No doubt that the exclusion of the harbi and musta'min from the mentioned verse is not by connected speech, so it remains in its original certainty, so it is not permissible to specify it by khabar wahid. And we have repeatedly passed similar consideration in its place. Secondly, the hadith of 'Imran ibn Husayn only indicates the absence of qisas in limbs between slaves, and does not indicate its absence between a man and a woman or between free and slave. So the objection with the generality of the verse in these two cases remains, and the answer is not complete.
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute (between Hanafi and Shafi'i, and also within Hanafi) concerning the applicability of qisas for limbs (atraf) between persons of different legal status: man vs. woman, free vs. slave, and two slaves. The Hanafi position holds that no qisas applies because qisas requires exact equality (mumathalah), which is lacking due to differences in value. The Shafi'i argument cites the Quranic verse (5:45) which seems general (the verse 'the eye for the eye, etc.') and thus would include all these cases. The Hanafi response attempts to specify the verse by the hadith of 'Imran ibn Husayn where the Prophet did not apply qisas between two slaves. However, the author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq (the commentator) critiques this response: the specification of the verse for harbi and musta'min is not connected to the verse, so the verse remains qat'i (definitive) and cannot be specified by ahad hadith. Moreover, the hadith of 'Imran only covers qisas between two slaves, not between man/woman or free/slave, so the objection remains unanswered. The passage also discusses a hypothetical: if a paralyzed limb is cut off, qisas is done by cutting the healthy limb because the deficiency is not in value but in function; but for gender and freedom status, the value disparity is inherent.

Key Terms
طرف (taraf): Limb; any extremity of the body (hand, foot, finger, etc.) - subject to specific rulings for qisas and diyah.
شبهة (shubhah): Legal doubt that prevents the application of qisas; here, the possibility of value equality creates a doubt (shubhah) that bars retaliation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi school deny qisas between a free man and a slave for a limb injury?
A) Because the slave is considered property, not a person.
B) Because the value (diyah) differs between free and slave, preventing exact equality.
C) Because the hadith explicitly exempts slaves from qisas.
D) Because the verse 'eye for an eye' does not cover slaves.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school conditions qisas for limbs on exact value equality; any legally established value disparity (by gender or status) creates a shubhah that bars retaliation, substituting diyah or arsh.

Qisas — Retaliation

Qisas for Limbs: Equality Between Muslim and Kafir
Ruling with inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that qisas applies for limbs between a Muslim and a kafir, and identify the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf) with the Shafi'i school.

Core Idea
Equality in arsh for limbs makes qisas valid between Muslim and kafir in the Hanafi school.

This passage presents a clear Hanafi ruling that the limb of a kafir and a Muslim are considered equal for the purpose of qisas (retaliation), based on the equality of their monetary compensation (arsh). The author contrasts this with the Shafi'i position, which denies qisas for limbs between a Muslim and a kafir. Understanding this dispute requires analysing the underlying reasoning and its practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the specific ruling: the limb of a kafir and a Muslim are equal, so qisas is executed between them.
The text explicitly states: 'wa taraf al-kafir wa al-muslim siyan'.
2
Identify the opponent's view
Note that Imam al-Shafi'i holds the opposite: qisas does not apply for limbs between a Muslim and a kafir.
The text says: 'Wa qala al-Shafi'i: la yajri'.
3
Follow the Hanafi proof
The Hanafi proof is based on equality in arsh (monetary compensation) – since the financial value of a limb is the same for a Muslim and a kafir, the requisite equality for qisas is satisfied.
This is a talil (reasoning) from the equality of arsh.
4
Follow the Shafi'i proof
The text does not elaborate, but refers to 'his principle' – likely that a Muslim is not executed for a kafir in cases of homicide, and this analogy extends to limbs.
We fill the gap from the broader madhhab context.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: under Hanafi, if a kafir cuts off a Muslim's hand, the Muslim can demand qisas (cutting the kafir's hand). Under Shafi'i, only diyah (financial compensation) is owed.
This shows the real-world impact of the ikhtilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : وطرف الكافر والمسلم سيان) أي مثلان فيجري القصاص بينهما للتساوي في الأرش. وقال الشافعي : لا يجري لما ذكرنا من أصله .
He (the author) said, may Allah have mercy on him: And the limb of the kafir and the Muslim are equal i.e., they are similar, so qisas is executed between them due to equality in arsh. And al-Shafi'i said: It does not apply, due to his principle we mentioned.
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This is a brief ruling that in the Hanafi school, the limb (taraf) of a Muslim and a kafir (non-Muslim) are considered equal for the purpose of qisas (retaliation). The reason (ta'lil) is that the arsh (monetary compensation) for a limb is the same for both—i.e., there is no disparity in value. In contrast, Imam al-Shafi'i holds that qisas does not apply between Muslim and kafir for limbs, based on his earlier principle (which the text does not elaborate here; presumably the principle that a Muslim is not killed for a kafir in qatl, and similarly limbs are treated). The Hanafi position relies on the equality of arsh for limbs across faiths, so the required equality (musawah) for qisas is present.

Key Terms
كافر (kafir): Non-Muslim who is not a harbi (warring) or musta'min (protected); for limbs, the arsh is equal to a Muslim's.
أرش (arsh): Monetary compensation for a limb; for a Muslim it is fixed, and for a kafir it is equal (in Hanafi view).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, can a Muslim demand qisas for his limb from a kafir who injured him?
A) Yes, because the arsh for limbs is equal.
B) No, because a Muslim is superior.
C) Yes, but only if the kafir is a dhimmi.
D) No, because the kafir's limb is not equal in value.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the equality of arsh for limbs means a Muslim can demand qisas against a kafir for limb injuries.

Qisas — Retaliation
intermediate
7 min
When Qisas is Not Possible: Half Forearm, Healed Ja'ifah, Tongue, and Penis
Ruling with reasoning (talil) on qisas exclusion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four cases where qisas does not apply and explain the legal reasoning (ta'lil) behind each, including the exception for the glans.

Core Idea
Qisas requires exact equality; where precise similitude is impossible, retaliation is replaced by compensation.

In the law of qisas (retaliation), the principle of equality (mumathalah) is paramount. This passage from the Hanafi tradition identifies specific injuries where exact replication is unattainable, whether due to anatomical complexity, healing uncertainty, or variable dimensions. The author explains why cutting a hand from mid-forearm, a healed penetrating wound, the tongue, and the penis all fall outside qisas, with one critical exception: the glans of the penis, because it can be precisely measured.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four prohibited qisas cases
List the four injuries mentioned in the passage: cutting a hand from half the forearm, a healed ja'ifah (wound reaching the body cavity), the tongue, and the penis (except the glans).
The exception for the glans is also part of the ruling.
2
Extract the ta'lil (legal reason) for each
For each case, identify why exact equality is impossible: (1) forearm: breaking bone with no control over precise replication; (2) ja'ifah: healing is rare, so a similar wound might not heal and could kill; (3) tongue and penis: they contract and expand, so equal measure cannot be assured.
Ta'lil is the reasoning that connects the ruling to its cause.
3
Recognize the exception and its rationale
The glans (hashafah) of the penis is excluded from the general prohibition because it is a fixed, measurable part, allowing exact equality.
This exception shows that qisas remains possible where precise similitude can be achieved.
4
Apply the principle to a hypothetical
Consider cutting a finger joint versus the whole finger. Which could be subject to qisas? The joint, like the glans, is a defined, measurable part; the whole finger might involve bone and variability.
Use analogy to test understanding of the ta'lil.
5
Note the consequence of qisas denial
When qisas is not available, the victim is entitled to financial compensation: arsh (fixed amount) for defined injuries or hukumat 'adl (equitable assessment) for injuries without fixed arsh.
This compensation ensures justice despite the impossibility of retaliation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : وقطع يد من نصف ساعد وجائفة برىء منها ولسان وذكر إلا أن تقطع الحشفة) أي لا قصاص في هذه الأشياء لعدم المماثلة فيها لأن في القطع من نصف الساعد كسر العظم ويتعذر التساوي فيها إذا لا ضابط له، وفي الجائفة البرء نادر فلا يمكن أن يخرج الثاني جائفة على وجه يبرأ منه فيكون إهلاكاً فلا يجوز والذكر للسان ينقبضان وينبسطان فلا
He (the author) said, may Allah have mercy on him: And cutting a hand from half the forearm, and a jai'fah (wound reaching the body cavity) that has healed, and the tongue, and the penis, except if the glans is cut) i.e., there is no qisas in these things due to lack of similitude, because in cutting from half the forearm there is breaking of bone, and equality is impossible since there is no control over it. And in the jai'fah, healing is rare, so it is not possible for the second (perpetrator) to produce a jai'fah in a way that it would heal; it would be destruction, so it is not permissible. And the penis and tongue contract and expand, so...
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This passage lists specific injuries for which qisas (retaliation) is not applicable. The reason (ta'lil) for each is the impossibility of achieving exact equality (mumathalah). Cutting from the halfway point of the forearm (nisf sa'id) involves breaking a bone, and there is no precise way to replicate exactly the same fracture. A jai'fah is a wound that penetrates into the body cavity (e.g., abdomen); if it heals, it is rare, so the perpetrator cannot inflict a similar wound that would also heal—it would likely cause death, and thus qisas would not be permissible as it would be excessive. The tongue and penis are not subject to qisas because they can contract and expand (e.g., the tongue can be extended or retracted), making exact equality impossible. However, there is an exception: if the glans (hashafah) of the penis is cut, qisas may apply because it is a defined, measurable part.

Key Terms
جائفة (ja'ifah): A wound that reaches the body cavity (jawf), such as the abdomen or thorax; considered dangerous.
حشفة (hashafah): The glans of the penis; a defined part that can be precisely cut, thus qisas is possible.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is qisas not applied for cutting a hand from half the forearm (nisf sa'id)?
A) Because the hand is not a limb.
B) Because it would require breaking a bone, which cannot be precisely equal.
C) Because it is considered a minor injury.
D) Because the victim has no right to qisas if the wound heals.

Key Takeaway
Qisas is only applicable when exact equality can be achieved; for injuries involving bones, variable organs, or uncertain healing, financial compensation is prescribed.

Qisas — Retaliation
intermediate
12 min
No Qisas Between Male/Female and Free/Slave Limbs
Ruling and proof that limbs of male/female and free/slave are not equal in qisas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school denies qisas between male and female, free and slave in limb injuries, and evaluate the proof from the general verse and the hadith of 'Imran.

Core Idea
Qisas in limbs requires exact equality; value disparity creates doubt (shubhah) that prevents retribution.

This passage tackles a key dispute in qisas (retributive justice): can a woman's limb be taken for a man's, or a slave's for a free person's? The Hanafi school says no, because the Lawgiver has fixed different values for these limbs. The passage provides a rational argument based on property analogy, addresses an objection from the absolute quranic verse, and includes a critical analysis of the hadith used to specify it.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi ruling on qisas between different genders and statuses
Identify the core ruling: no qisas between male/female, free/slave, or even two slaves due to potential value disparity. Understand the rationale: equality (mumathala) is a prerequisite for qisas.
The ruling is derived from the Lawgiver's division of diyah (blood money).
2
Trace the qiyas argument on property analogy
The text analogizes limbs to ribawi goods: just as inequality prevents exchange, value disparity in limbs prevents qisas. Notice the distinction between two free persons (certain equality by Law) and others (uncertain equality by estimation).
This qiyas is aqli (rational) but rooted in textual values.
3
Analyze the objection from the general verse and the hadith of 'Imran
The opponent (Shafi'i) cites the absolute verse (Q 5:45). The Hanafi response specifies it with the hadith of 'Imran. But the author critiques this: the exclusion of warriors and protected persons from the verse is disconnected, so the verse remains qat'i and cannot be specified by a solitary hadith. Also, the hadith only covers two slaves, not male/female or free/slave.
This critique is from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, showing intra-Hanafi refinement.
4
Evaluate the strength of the Hanafi position
Despite the critique, the Hanafi ruling stands on the value disparity principle. The passage shows that even if the hadith specification is flawed, the aqli argument (qiyas on riba) supports the ruling.
The thamarah al-khilaf: in practice, a woman who cuts a man's hand pays diyah, not qisas.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا مماثلة بين طرفي الذكر والأنثى المماثلة مانعاً للتفاوت وبينهما في القيمة بتقسيم الشارع ولا بين الحر والعبد ولا بين العبدين للتفاوت في القيمة، وإن تساويا فيها بالظن فصار شبهة منع القصاص فإن قيل : إن استقام عدم في الحر والعبد لم يستقم بين العبدين لإمكان تساوي قيمتهما بتقويم المقومين أجيب بأن التساوي إنما يكون بالحزر والظن والمماثلة المشروطة شرعاً لا تثبت بذلك كالمماثلة في الأموال الربوية بخلاف طرفي الحرين لأن استوائهما متيقن بتقويم الشرع، وبخلاف الأنفس لأن الخلاف فيها متعلق بإزهاق الروح ولا تفاوت فيه قال صاحب الكفاية : فإن قيل قوله تعالى والعين بالعين والاذن بالاذن ﴾ [المائدة : ٤٥] مطلق يتناول موضع النزاع فيكون حجة عليكم قلنا : قد خص منه الحربي والمستأمن والعام إذا خص منه شيء يجوز تخصيصه بخبر الواحد فخصصناه بما روي عن عمران بن حصين أنه قال : قطع عبد لقوم فقراء أذن عبد لقوم أغنياء فاختصموا إلى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فلم يقض بالقصاص اهـ. أقول : فيه نظر؛ أما أولاً فلأنه قد نقرر في علم الأحوال أن النص العام إذا خص منه شيء بكلام مستقل موصول به يكون ذلك العام المخصص منه البعض ظنياً في الباقي فيجوز تخصيصه بخبر الواحد، وأما إذا خرج من النص العام شيء مما هو مفصول عنه غير موصول به فلا يكون ذلك ظنياً في الباقي بل يكون باقياً على حالته الأولى، ولا شك أن مخرج الحربي والمستأمن من الآية المذكورة ليس بكلام موصول بها فتكون باقية على قطيعتها الأصلية فلا يجوز تخصيصها بخبر الواحد، وقد مر منا غير مرة نظير هذا النظر في محاله. وأما ثانياً فلأن حديث عمران بن حصين إنما يفيد عدم جريان القصاص في الأطراف بين العبدين ولا يفيد عدم جريانه فيما بين الرجل والمرأة ولا بين الحر والعبد فبقي الاعتراض بإطلاق الآية المذكورة في هاتين الصورتين ولم يتم الجواب.
And there is no equality between the limb of the male and the female, equality preventing disparity, and between them is disparity in value due to the division of the Lawgiver. Nor between free and slave, nor between two slaves due to disparity in value, even if they are equal by estimation, so it becomes a doubt preventing qisas. If it is said: If the negation is established for free and slave, it is not established for two slaves because their values can be equal by the estimation of valuers. The answer is that equality is only by guess and estimation, and the required legal equality is not established thereby, like equality in ribawi properties, unlike the limbs of two free persons because their equality is certain by the estimation of the Law. And unlike lives because the dispute therein pertains to taking the soul and there is no disparity therein. The author of al-Kifāyah said: If it is said: His statement 'The eye for the eye and the ear for the ear' is absolute and includes the disputed cases, thus it is proof against you. We respond: It excludes the harbi and musta'min; when a general text is excluded from it by an independent connected statement, that general text becomes zanni in the remainder, so it is allowed to specify it with a khabar wahid. Thus we specify it with the hadith of 'Imran ibn Husayn that a slave belonging to poor people cut the ear of a slave belonging to rich people, and they referred to the Prophet ﷺ and he did not judge qisas. I say: There is consideration: First, because it is established in the science of legal theory that when a general text is excluded from something by an independent connected statement, that general text becomes zanni in the remainder, so specifying it with a khabar wahid is allowed. But if something is excluded from the general text by what is disconnected, then it does not become zanni in the remainder but remains in its original state. There is no doubt that the exclusion of the harbi and musta'min from the said verse is not by a connected statement, so it remains in its original certainty, so it is not permissible to specify it with a khabar wahid. Second, the hadith of 'Imran ibn Husayn only indicates the non-application of qisas in limbs between two slaves, not between a man and a woman nor between free and slave, so the objection based on the absolute meaning of the verse remains in these two cases, and the answer is incomplete.
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It first states that there is no equality between limbs of male and female, free and slave, and even between two slaves if their values are estimated equal by guesswork, because that uncertainty creates a doubt (shubhah) preventing qisas. Then an objection is raised: if we accept inequality between free and slave, why not between two slaves when their values may be equal? The answer is that equality by estimation is not legally sufficient, unlike the certainty of equality between free persons established by Law. Then a larger objection comes from the general verse on qisas. The commentator (author of al-Kifāyah) attempts to specify it with the hadith of 'Imran, but the author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq critiques this, arguing that the exclusion of certain categories from the verse was not done by a connected statement, so the verse remains qat'i and cannot be specified by a solitary hadith. Also, the hadith only covers slaves, not the other cases, so the objection remains unanswered.

Key Terms
شبهة (shubhah): Doubt or ambiguity that prevents the application of hudud or qisas.
مقطوع (maqṭūʿ): Text that is certain in transmission and meaning, cannot be specified by khabar wahid.
خبر الواحد (khabar al-wahid): A solitary hadith, which is zanni in transmission.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary reason the Hanafi school denies qisas between a man and a woman for limb injuries?
A) The hadith of 'Imran only covers slaves.
B) The man's limb is considered more valuable by the Lawgiver.
C) The Quranic verse on qisas is abrogated.
D) There is a consensus among all schools.

Key Takeaway
Qisas in limbs requires exact value equality; when the Lawgiver has fixed a disparity (as between male/female, free/slave), qisas is replaced by diyah due to the doubt created by inequality.

Qisas — Retaliation

12 min
Limbs Where Qisas Is Not Applicable
Rulings on specific injuries where qisas is precluded

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the specific injuries where qisas is precluded, explain the rationale of lack of exact equivalence, and distinguish the compensatory rules (diyah vs. ḥukūmat al-ʿadl) that apply.

Core Idea
Qisas requires exact equality; where impossible, diyah or arbitrated compensation (ḥukūmat al-ʿadl) replaces it.

This passage from al-Baḥr al-Rāʾiq explains that qisas is not applicable for certain injuries due to the impossibility of exact reciprocation. The injuries listed include amputation at half the forearm, a penetrating wound (jāʾifah) that heals, the tongue, and the penis except for the glans. The commentator elucidates the rationale behind each exception and also notes the intra-Hanafi disagreement regarding the extent of qisas for the penis and the determination of compensation for amputations at different joints.

Guided Path
1
Identify the listed injuries
From the text, enumerate the injuries where qisas is excluded: cutting hand from half forearm, jāʾifah (penetrating wound) that heals, tongue, penis – with the exception of cutting the glans.
Note the exception for the glans: qisas is applicable there because the boundary is clear.
2
Understand the rationale for each
For each, state why exact equality is impossible: half forearm involves bone breakage and variable healing; jāʾifah healing is rare and unpredictable; tongue and penis are contractile and cannot be measured precisely.
The text uses 'taʿadhdhur al-mumāthalah' (lack of equality).
3
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abū Yūsuf holds that if the penis is cut from the base, qisas is obligatory, contradicting the general view. Recognize that this difference stems from the possibility of exact measurement at the base.
The other two (Abū Ḥanīfa and Muḥammad) reject qisas for any part of the penis except the glans.
4
Distinguish the compensatory rulings
When qisas is excluded, compensation is either full diyah or ḥukūmat al-ʿadl. The text from al-Yanābīʿ specifies: cutting at the joint (wrist, knee) incurs full diyah; cutting above the joint incurs ḥukūmat al-ʿadl. Abū Yūsuf differs on the ankle.
Remember: diyah is fixed; ḥukūmat al-ʿadl is assessed by a just arbitrator.
5
Apply the rule to similar cases
Consider other injuries like cutting a finger near the palm vs. at the joint. The same principle applies: Qisas requires identical placement and healing characteristics.
You can test with the practice tasks.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : وقطع يد من نصف ساعد وجائفة برىء منها ولسان وذكر إلا أن تقطع الحشفة) أي لا قصاص في هذه الأشياء لعدم المماثلة فيها لأن في القطع من نصف الساعد كسر العظم ويتعذر التساوي فيها إذا لا ضابط له، وفي الجائفة البرء نادر فلا يمكن أن يخرج الثاني جائفة على وجه يبرأ منه فيكون إهلاكاً فلا يجوز والذكر للسان ينقبضان وينبسطان فلا يمكن اعتبار المماثلة فيهما إلا أن يقطع من الحشفة لأن موضع القطع معلوم فيصار إليه . وعن أبي يوسف أنه إذا قطع من أصلها يجب بخلاف ما إذا قطع بعضها لتعذر اعتبار المماثلة فيه. قال في الينابيع : إذا قطع اليد من العضو والرجل من الفخذ فعندهما فيه الدية، وما فوق الكتف والقدم ففيه حكومة عدل، وعند أبي يوسف : ما فوق الكعب والقدم مع الأصابع .
He said, may Allah have mercy on him: And cutting a hand from half the forearm, and a penetrating wound that heals, and the tongue, and the penis unless the glans is cut. That is, no qisas in these things due to lack of equality because cutting from half the forearm involves bone fracture and equality is impossible since there is no standard. In a penetrating wound, healing is rare, so it is not possible for the second person to produce a similar wound that heals; thus it would be destruction, so it is not permitted. The penis and tongue contract and expand, so equality cannot be considered unless the glans is cut because the place of cutting is known, so resort is made to it. And from Abu Yusuf: if he cuts from its base, qisas is obligatory, unlike if he cuts part of it due to difficulty in considering equality. It is said in al-Yanābīʿ: if he cuts the hand from the joint and the leg from the thigh, according to both (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) there is full diyah; what is above the shoulder and foot, there is ḥukūmat al-ʿadl. According to Abu Yusuf: what is above the ankle and foot [is considered] with the fingers.
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This passage is a parsing exercise of multiple rulings. The matn lists specific injuries where qisas is not applied because exact equality is impossible. For half-forearm amputation: bone breakage occurs and cannot be replicated precisely. For a penetrating wound that heals: such healing is rare, so a second wound cannot be guaranteed to heal similarly; therefore, it would be tantamount to manslaughter. For tongue and penis: these organs contract and expand, making identical amputation impossible, except for the glans of the penis, which has a clear boundary. Abu Yusuf adds that cutting the penis from its base requires qisas, but not if only part is cut, due to lack of precision. Al-Yanābīʿ further distinguishes: cutting from the joint (wrist or knee) incurs full diyah; cutting above the joint incurs ḥukūmat al-ʿadl; Abu Yusuf has a different view on the ankle.

Key Terms
جائفة (jā'ifah): A penetrating wound that reaches the body cavity (belly, chest, etc.).
حكومة عدل (ḥukūmat al-ʿadl): Arbitrated compensation assessed by a just arbitrator, used when no fixed diyah exists.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is qisas not applicable for a jāʾifah (penetrating wound) that heals?
A) Because the wound is too deep.
B) Because healing from such a wound is rare, and the second wound cannot be guaranteed to heal similarly, risking death.
C) Because the victim cannot survive the retaliation.
D) Because jāʾifah is not considered a crime.

Key Takeaway
Qisas is precluded when exact equality is impossible; the default compensation is full diyah for joint-level amputations and ḥukūmat al-ʿadl for others.

Diyah for Hand, Slave Injuries, and Supernumerary Fingers
Rulings on hand diyah payment schedule, slave injury compensation delay, and supernumerary finger qisas exemption.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on diyah for a hand (deferred over two years), the ruling on a slave's broken limb (no immediate payment), and the consensus on a supernumerary finger with a counterpart (no qisas).

Core Idea
Hand diyah is paid in two-year installments; slave bone breaks incur no immediate liability; an extra finger with matching counterpart triggers no qisas.

This passage from al-Khulāṣah presents three specific rulings on diyah and qisas. The first establishes the payment schedule for a hand's diyah. The second addresses the delayed liability for injuries to a slave's bones. The third clarifies the consensus on supernumerary fingers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage states that the diyah for the hand is wajib and deferred over two years, with two-thirds in the first year and the remainder in the second.
This applies to a free person's hand.
2
Analyze the slave's bone injury
Breaking a slave's hand or leg does not mandate immediate compensation; nothing is obligatory in the present.
The obligation may arise later upon freeing or sale.
3
Examine the supernumerary finger case
Cutting an extra finger that has a counterpart (a similar extra finger on the other hand) incurs no qisas by consensus.
Consensus here means within the Hanafi school or broader? The text says 'bil-ijmāʿ'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي الخلاصة : دية اليد تجب مؤجلة في سنتين ثلثاها في السنة الأولى والباقي في الثانية، وإذا كسر يد عبد رجل أو رجله لا يجب في الحال شيء، ولو قطع أصبعاً زائدة وفي يده مثلها لا قصاص بالإجماع. وقال أبو حنيفة في الاقطعين والأشلين إنه لا قصاص هو قول أبي يوسف في رواية الحسن عنه، وكذلك مقطوع الإبهام أو الأصابع كلها إذا قطع إنسان يده فلا قصاص في قول أبي حنيفة أنه لا قصاص فيه وفيه حكومة عدل. ولو كسر عظماً ساعد أو ساق أو غيره ففيه حكومة عدل، وفي ثدي المرأة دية كاملة ولا ذكر له في الكتب. وفي كسر الصلب دية كاملة إن منعه عن الجماع وأحد به فأما إذا لم يحد به ولم يمنعه عن الجماع فهذا على نوعين : إما أن يبقى للجراحة أثر ففيه حكومة عدل ولم يجب كمال الدية، وأما إذا لم يبق لها أثر لم يجب فيه شيء وقد مر هذا فيما تقدم .
And in al-Khulāṣah: the diyah for the hand is obligatory deferred over two years, two-thirds in the first year and the remainder in the second. And if the hand of a man's slave is broken or his leg, nothing is obligatory immediately. And if he cuts a supernumerary finger while having a similar one on the other hand, there is no qisas by consensus. Abu Hanifa said regarding those with missing limbs and the paralyzed: there is no qisas; this is the statement of Abu Yusuf in the narration from al-Hasan from him. Similarly, if a person whose thumb or all fingers are cut, cuts someone else's hand, there is no qisas according to Abu Hanifa, and there is ḥukūmat al-ʿadl. And if he breaks a bone of the forearm or shin or other, there is ḥukūmat al-ʿadl. And in the breast of a woman, full diyah is obligatory, though not mentioned in the books. And in breaking the back, full diyah is obligatory if it prevents him from intercourse and makes him hunched. But if it does not make him hunched and does not prevent him from intercourse, then it is of two types: either an effect of the wound remains, then there is ḥukūmat al-ʿadl and full diyah is not obligatory; or if no effect remains, then nothing is obligatory, and this has preceded earlier.
Source pages p. 39

Commentary
This passage collects various rulings on diyah. The diyah for a hand is paid in installments over two years. For a slave's broken bones, no immediate payment is due; the owner's liability is deferred. A supernumerary finger with a counterpart: consensus no qisas. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf agree that a person missing a limb or paralyzed cannot have qisas from the other; instead, ḥukūmat al-ʿadl applies. Similarly, a person with missing fingers: no qisas. Fractures of major bones require ḥukūmat al-ʿadl. A woman's breast has full diyah (500 dinars). Breaking the back has full diyah if it causes hunching and impotence; lesser injuries may require ḥukūmat al-ʿadl or nothing if healed completely.

Key Terms
أصبع زائدة (iṣbaʿ zā'idah): An extra finger, supernumerary digit.
شلاء (shallā'): Paralyzed limb, crippled hand.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Khulāṣah, when is the diyah for a hand paid?
A) Immediately in one lump sum.
B) Over two years: two-thirds in first year, remainder in second.
C) Over three years in equal installments.
D) It is not specified.

Key Takeaway
The diyah for a hand is paid in two-year installments; slave bone injuries have no immediate compensation; a supernumerary finger with a counterpart incurs no qisas by consensus.

Diyah for Amputees, Fractures, and Special Cases (Breast, Back)
Rulings on qisas exemption for amputees/paralyzed, diyah for fractures, woman's breast, and back injuries.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on qisas for amputees and paralyzed persons (no qisas, only ḥukūmat al-ʿadl), the diyah for fractures (ḥukūmat al-ʿadl), the woman's breast (full diyah), and the back break (full diyah if hunchback and impotence).

Core Idea
Amputees and paralyzed cannot have qisas from them; bone fractures require ḥukūmat al-ʿadl; a woman's breast has full diyah; a back break causing hunchback and impotence has full diyah.

This continuation of the passage addresses special cases: persons with missing limbs or paralysis, fractures of major bones, the woman's breast, and back injuries. Each case has a specific ruling on whether qisas applies or diyah is full or reduced.

Guided Path
1
Identify the amputee/paralyzed ruling
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf state that there is no qisas for persons with missing limbs or paralysis; instead, ḥukūmat al-ʿadl is applied.
Ḥukūmat al-ʿadl is estimation by just experts of the value of the lost function.
2
Analyze the fracture ruling
Breaking a bone of the forearm, shin, or other requires ḥukūmat al-ʿadl, not full diyah.
This applies even if the bone heals but had an effect.
3
Examine the woman's breast
Loss of a woman's breast incurs full diyah (complete blood money).
This is unusual as normally partial limbs have fractional diyah.
4
Differentiate back break
If breaking the back causes hunchback and prevents intercourse, full diyah; if no permanent effect, either ḥukūmat al-ʿadl (if effect remains) or nothing (if healed completely).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي الخلاصة : دية اليد تجب مؤجلة في سنتين ثلثاها في السنة الأولى والباقي في الثانية، وإذا كسر يد عبد رجل أو رجله لا يجب في الحال شيء، ولو قطع أصبعاً زائدة وفي يده مثلها لا قصاص بالإجماع. وقال أبو حنيفة في الاقطعين والأشلين إنه لا قصاص هو قول أبي يوسف في رواية الحسن عنه، وكذلك مقطوع الإبهام أو الأصابع كلها إذا قطع إنسان يده فلا قصاص في قول أبي حنيفة أنه لا قصاص فيه وفيه حكومة عدل. ولو كسر عظماً ساعد أو ساق أو غيره ففيه حكومة عدل، وفي ثدي المرأة دية كاملة ولا ذكر له في الكتب. وفي كسر الصلب دية كاملة إن منعه عن الجماع وأحد به فأما إذا لم يحد به ولم يمنعه عن الجماع فهذا على نوعين : إما أن يبقى للجراحة أثر ففيه حكومة عدل ولم يجب كمال الدية، وأما إذا لم يبق لها أثر لم يجب فيه شيء وقد مر هذا فيما تقدم .
And in al-Khulāṣah: the diyah for the hand is obligatory deferred over two years, two-thirds in the first year and the remainder in the second. And if the hand of a man's slave is broken or his leg, nothing is obligatory immediately. And if he cuts a supernumerary finger while having a similar one on the other hand, there is no qisas by consensus. And in breaking the back, full diyah is obligatory if it prevents him from intercourse and makes him hunched. But if it does not make him hunched and does not prevent him from intercourse, then it is of two types: either an effect of the wound remains, then there is ḥukūmat al-ʿadl and full diyah is not obligatory; or if no effect remains, then nothing is obligatory, and this has preceded earlier.
Source pages p. 39

Commentary
This passage collects various rulings on diyah. The diyah for a hand is paid in installments over two years. For a slave's broken bones, no immediate payment is due; the owner's liability is deferred. A supernumerary finger with a counterpart: consensus no qisas. A) Full diyah.

Diyah for Injuries to the Breast, Spine, Penis, and Testicles
Catalogue of diyah rulings for specific injuries

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the diyah amounts for specific injuries to the breast, spine, penis, and testicles, and distinguish between full diyah and ḥukūmat al-ʿadl based on functional impairment.

Core Idea
Full diyah is for loss of function; partial or no compensation when function remains.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq details various rulings on diyah for injuries to the breast, backbone, penis, and testicles. The amounts depend on whether the injury causes functional loss as described in the text. You will learn the specific rules for each body part and the intra-Hanafi disagreement regarding the doctor's fee for spinal injuries that heal without a mark.

Guided Path
1
Identify the injured body part and type of injury
The passage covers breast fracture with fluid leakage, spinal crush with or without hunchback/impotence, penis cuts (glans vs. rest, eunuch), testicles, and mufḍāh (woman with loss of control).
Each case has a specific ruling.
2
Determine if functional loss occurred
Full diyah is due when function is lost (e.g., inability to copulate, incontinence). If function remains, only ḥukūmat al-ʿadl or nothing is due.
For spine: full diyah only if hunchback and impotence.
3
Apply the appropriate diyah or ḥukūmat al-ʿadl
Full diyah for breast (500 dinars), penis (1000 dinars), both testicles (1000 dinars), mufḍāh (1000 dinars). For eunuch's penis: ḥukūmat al-ʿadl. For glans cut separately: full diyah; if rest of penis cut with healing between: diyah for glans + ḥukūmat for remainder.
If multiple limbs cut, order matters (see text).
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on doctor's fee for healed spinal injuries
Abu Hanifa says nothing is due if no mark remains; Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say doctor's fee is wajib.
The text does not specify which is mufta bihi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي الظهيرية : وكذا صدر المرأة إذا انكسر وانقطع الماء منه ففيه الدية، وفي الصلب إذا دق لكن يقدر على الجماع ففيه حكومة عدل وإن لم يقدر وصار أحدب فدية كاملة، وإن عاد إلى حبله ولم ينقص ولكن فيه أثر الضرب ففيه حكومة عدل وإن لم يقدر وصار أحدب فدية كاملة، وإن عاد إلى حبلة ولم ينقص ولكن فيه أثر الضرب ففيه حكومة عدل، وإن لم يكن فيه أثر فلا شيء فيه في قول أبي حنيفة وعندهما تجب أجرة الطبيب، وفي الذكر كمال الدية، وفي ذكر الخصي حكومة عدل سواء كان يتحرك أو لا يقدر الخصي على الوطء أو لا يقدر على هذا الخلاف ذكر العنين. وأما ذكر الشيخ الكبير إن كان يتحرك ولا يقدر على الوطء فالجواب فيه كالجواب في ذكر الخصي وذكر العنين. وفي التهذيب : وفي ذكر الخصي والعينين حكومة عدل وهو ما يرى القاضي بمشورة أهل البصيرة وقيل يقوم أن لو كان عبداً محبوباً وغيره فتجب نسبة النقصان من ديته كما لو نقص عشر القيمة يجب عشر الدية والأول أصح. وفي التجريد: المرأة إذا أفضاها فصارت لا تستمسك البول والغائط أو أحدهما ففيه دية كاملة، وفي الأنثيين كمال الدية. وإذا قطع الحشفة يجب كمال الدية فإن قطع باقي الذكر فإن كان قبل تخلل البرء تجب دية كاملة ويجعل كأنه قطع الذكر بدفعة واحدة، وإن تخلل بينهما برء فيجب كمال الدية في الحشفة وحكومة العدل في الباقي. وإذا قطع الذكر والأنثيين من الرجل الصحيح خطأ إن بدأ بقطع الذكر ففيه ديتان. وفي التجريد: وكذا إذا قطعها من جانب واحد ولو بدأ بقطع الأنثيين ثم بالذكر ففي الانثيين الدية كاملة وفي الذكر حكومة عدل، وإن قطعهما من جانب الفخذ معاً فعليه ديتان وفي التحفة : وفي الأنثيين إذا قطعهما
And in al-Ẓāhiriyyah: likewise the breast of a woman, if it breaks and water emerges from it, there is full diyah. And in the backbone, if it is crushed but he can still have intercourse, there is ḥukūmat al-ʿadl; if he cannot and becomes hunched, full diyah. If he returns to his original state without decrease but with a mark of the blow, there is ḥukūmat al-ʿadl. If there is no mark, then nothing is due according to Abu Hanifa, while according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), the doctor's fee is obligatory. In the penis, full diyah. In the penis of a eunuch, ḥukūmat al-ʿadl, whether it moves or not, whether the eunuch can copulate or not; this is the same difference as for the penis of an impotent man. As for the penis of a very old man, if it moves but he cannot copulate, the answer is the same as for the penis of a eunuch and impotent man. In al-Tahdhīb: Regarding the penis of a eunuch and both testicles, there is ḥukūmat al-ʿadl, which is what the judge determines with the advice of experts. And it is said that one estimates how much a valuable slave would be, then the proportion of decrease is fixed from his diyah, as if one-tenth of value is lost, one-tenth of diyah is due; the first view is more correct. In al-Tajrīd: If a woman is injured such that she cannot control urine and stool or one of them, full diyah is due. In both testicles, full diyah. If the glans is cut, full diyah is due. If the rest of the penis is cut, if the wound heals before full separation, full diyah is due and it is treated as if he cut the penis in one go. If healing occurs between them, then full diyah for the glans and ḥukūmat al-ʿadl for the remainder. If the penis and both testicles are cut from a healthy man by mistake: if he began with cutting the penis, then two diyahs are due. In al-Tajrīd: likewise if he cuts them from one side; and if he began with the testicles then the penis, then for the testicles full diyah and for the penis ḥukūmat al-ʿadl. If he cuts both from the side of the thigh together, two diyahs are due. And in al-Tuḥfah: regarding the testicles if he cuts them...
Source pages p. 39

Commentary
This passage is an expansion probe containing a catalogue of rulings from various sources. For a woman's breast that breaks and leaks fluid: full diyah (500 dinars). For spinal injuries: full diyah if it causes hunching and impotence; otherwise ḥukūmat al-ʿadl or nothing. The doctor's fee is disputed between Abu Hanifa and the two companions. For the penis: full diyah. For a eunuch's penis: ḥukūmat al-ʿadl due to decreased function. The method of calculating ḥukūmat al-ʿadl is described: judge’s estimate or proportional valuation. For a mufḍāh (woman with uncontrolled excretion): full diyah. For testicles: full diyah. If glans only is cut: full diyah; if rest of penis cut with healing between: separate diyah for glans and ḥukūmat al-ʿadl for rest. Multiple limb injuries: if both penis and testicles are cut, the order matters for the total diyah.

Key Terms
أفضى (afdā): A woman who has lost control over urine or stool due to injury.
خصي (khaṣī): A eunuch, castrated male.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, how many diyahs are due if the penis and both testicles are cut unintentionally, starting with the penis?
A) One diyah
B) Two diyahs
C) One and a half diyahs
D) Ḥukūmat al-ʿadl for both

Key Takeaway
Full diyah is due only when the injury causes complete loss of function; otherwise, ḥukūmat al-ʿadl or nothing.

Qisas — Retaliation

Option Between Arsh and Qisas for Defective Limbs and Larger Wounds
Commentary on Kanz matn: victim's option when cutter's hand is withered/missing fingers or the head wound is larger

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the victim's option when the offender's limb is defective or the head wound is larger, and explain the proof and the Shafi'i disagreement.

Core Idea
When identical retaliation is impossible due to a defect, the victim may choose either full compensation or deficient retaliation — and once he chooses retaliation, no further claim remains.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq addresses a specific situation in qisas: what happens if the offender's hand is withered or missing fingers, or if the head wound he inflicted is larger than the victim's? The matn states that the victim is given a choice (khiyar) between taking full monetary compensation (arsh) or exacting retaliation (qisas) with a deficiency. The commentary explains the Hanafi position and refutes Imam al-Shafi'i's contrary view. Understanding this ruling helps clarify the boundaries of qisas when exact equivalence is impossible.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the victim's option when the offender's limb is defective or the head wound is larger. The ruling is that the victim may choose between arsh (full compensation) or qisas (retaliation) even if retaliation is deficient.
The option exists only if the defect was present at the time of the cutting.
2
Locate the dalil
The Hanafi proof is based on qiyas (analogy) to accepting inferior goods in a sale. Just as a buyer who accepts defective goods cannot later claim the price difference, the victim who chooses deficient retaliation forfeits any claim for the deficiency.
The analogy is to the principle that a description (wasf) attached to a thing is not separately compensable.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The deficiency in the limb is considered a description (wasf) of the limb, not a separate entity. Therefore, when the victim retaliates against the defective limb, he receives the limb itself and the deficiency is not an additional right.
This is why the analogy to accepting inferior goods works: the buyer accepts the goods 'as is' and has no further claim.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that since full retaliation is impossible, the victim should receive compensation for the deficiency after retaliation. He analogizes to cases where partial retaliation is possible and the remainder is compensated.
The practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) is that in the Shafi'i school, the offender must pay for the deficiency, while in the Hanafi school, no further payment is due.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The commentator favours the Hanafi position, supported by the principle that the victim's right is in the same limb, and once he chooses retaliation, he waives any claim to the difference.
The authority is zahir al-riwayah and the mufta bihi is the Hanafi view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (وخير بين الأرش والقود إن كان القاطع أشل أو ناقص الاصابع أو كان رأس الشاج أكبر) قيد بحالة القطع فجعلها قيداً في التخيير لأنها لو تغيرت بعد القطع لا يخير كما سيأتي بيانه. وأطلق في الشلاء فشمل ما إذا كان ينتفع بها أو لا فلو قيد في الشلاء فقال شلاء ينتفع بها لكان أولى كما سنبينه أيضاً. أما الأول فهو ما إذا كانت يد القاطع شلاء أو ناقصة الأصابع ويد المقطوع صحيحة كاملة الأصابع فلأن استيفاء حقه متعذر فيخير بين أن يتجوز بدون حقه في القطع وبين أن يأخذ الأرش كاملاً ثم إذا استوفى القصاص سقط حقه في الزيادة. وقال الشافعي : يضمنه النقصان لأنه قدر على استيفاء البعض فيستوفي ما قدر عليه وما تعذر استيفاؤه ويضمنه. ولنا أن الباقي وصف فلا يضمن بانفراده فصار كما لو تجوز بالرديء مكان الجيد، ولو سقطت يده المعيبة قبل اختيار المجني عليه بطل حقه ولا شيء له عليه فإن حقه تعين في القصاص لما مر أن العمد القود عيناً وحقه ثابت فيه قبل اختياره بخلاف ما إذا قطعت موجب بقود أو سرقة حيث يجب عليه الأرش. وقال الشافعي : يجب عليه الأرش في الموضعين لأنه لما تعذر استيفاء الحق طهر أنه كان مستحقاً عليه بخلاف النفس إذا وجبت على القاتل فقتل بجناية أخرى حيث لا يضمن وأما الثاني وهو ما إذا كانت رأس الشاج أكبر بأن كانت استوعبت ما بين قرني المشجوج وفي استيفاء ما بين قرني الشاج زيادة على ما فعل، وفي استيفاء قدر حقه لا يلحق الشاج من الشين مثل ما يلحق المشجوج فيتخير، ثم لو اختار القود يبدأ من أي الجانبين شاء لأنه حقه في ذلك المحل فكان له أن يتخير، ولو كانت رأس المشجوج أكبر تخير أيضاً لتقرير الاستيفاء كملاً.
The author (may Allah have mercy on him) said: (And he is given choice between compensation and retaliation if the cutter was withered or missing fingers, or if the head of the wound [of the striker] is larger). This is restricted to the state at the time of cutting, so that if it changes after cutting, he is not given choice, as will be explained. The term 'withered' is absolute, including whether it is useful or not; it would have been preferable to restrict it to 'a withered hand that is still useful', as we will also explain. As for the first: that is when the cutter's hand is withered or missing fingers, and the victim's hand is healthy and complete in fingers, because exacting his right is impossible; so he is given choice between taking less than his right in retaliation or taking full compensation. Then if he exacts retaliation, his right to any surplus is forfeited. Al-Shafi'i said: he is liable for the deficiency because he is able to exact some, so he exacts what he can and is liable for what is impossible to exact. Our proof: the remainder is a description, so it is not separately liable; it is like accepting inferior goods in place of good ones. And if the defective hand falls off before the victim makes his choice, his right is nullified and he has nothing against him, because his right is fixed in retaliation; as per the earlier principle that intentional aggression specifically fixes retaliation, and his right is established in it before his choice – unlike the case where it is cut due to retaliation or theft, where compensation is obligatory. Al-Shafi'i said: compensation is obligatory in both cases because since exacting the right is impossible, it becomes clear that it was due upon him – unlike the case of a life when a killer is liable for another crime, where he is not liable. As for the second: that is when the head of the wound [of the striker] is larger, meaning it extends between the two horns of the wounded person; exacting the same between the two horns of the striker would be more than was done, and exacting his exact right would not cause the striker the same disfigurement as the victim, so he is given choice. Then if he chooses retaliation, he may start from either side he wishes, because his right is in that place, so he may choose. And if the head of the victim's wound is larger, he is also given choice to ensure complete exaction.
Source pages p. 41

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on a matn from Kanz al-Daqaiq. It explains the ruling that when a person commits a retaliatory injury but his own limb is defective (withered or missing fingers) or his head wound is larger than the victim's, the victim is given an option: either accept full monetary compensation (arsh) or exact retaliation with a deficiency (i.e., accept a lesser retaliation). The reason is that exacting identical retaliation is impossible due to the defect. The commentator then refutes Imam al-Shafi'i's view that the offender must also compensate for the deficiency if the victim chooses retaliation. The Hanafi position is that once retaliation is chosen, all rights are satisfied because the deficiency is part of the limb's description, not a separate loss. The passage also covers the special case of a larger head wound (ras al-shaj akbar), where the striker's wound is larger than the victim's; here the victim may still choose retaliation but must be careful not to exceed. The option exists when the condition exists at the time of cutting; if it changes later, the option vanishes.

Key Terms
شلاء (shallāʾ): A withered/paralyzed hand that has no function.
رأس الشاج (raʾs al-shājj): The head of the wound on the striker himself (the one who inflicted the wound).
التجوز (al-tajawwuz): Accepting less than the full right, i.e., tolerating a deficiency.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a victim retaliates against a person with a withered hand, what happens to his claim for the deficiency?
A) He may claim compensation for the deficiency after retaliation
B) He forfeits any claim for the deficiency
C) He must first receive compensation before retaliating
D) He is not allowed to retaliate at all

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, when identical retaliation is impossible due to a defect, the victim may choose either full compensation or deficient retaliation, and once retaliation is chosen, all rights are satisfied.

Qisas for Hands with Black Nails and Missing Fingers
Rules for qisas when the hand has a black nail or missing fingers, including distinction between divine and human-caused deficiency

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rules for qisas when the victim's hand has a black nail or missing fingers, and distinguish between deficiencies caused by divine affliction versus human action.

Core Idea
A black nail does not affect qisas; only functional impairment does. Option between qisas and arsh depends on the nature of the deficiency.

In this passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, the Hanafi school clarifies the rules of qisas when the victim's hand has a cosmetic defect (black nail) or a quantitative deficiency (missing fingers). The key distinction is between defects that affect function and those that do not, and whether the deficiency was caused by a divine act or human action. We will work through the ruling and its underlying reasoning, including a comparison with the Shafi'i school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what is being ruled upon: qisas for a hand with a black nail. The text states that qisas is obligatory even if the cutter's hand has no black nail.
2
Locate the dalil
Imam Muhammad's statement in al-Asl provides the proof: blackness does not impair utility (grasping). The analogy with accidental cutting confirms this.
The dalil is aqli (rational analogy) based on function.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The reasoning is that since blackness does not reduce diya (half diya is due for accidental cutting regardless), it does not affect qisas. The existence of a defect is compared to a withered hand that is still useful.
If the deficiency impairs function, it becomes like a useless withered hand, and qisas is not allowed.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that if the victim chooses qisas on a hand missing fingers, he is entitled to arsh for the missing part. The Hanafi school rejects this.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
Burhan al-A'imma restricts the victim's option to cases where the withered hand is useful. If not useful, full diya is due. This view is given fatwa.
Intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: Shams al-A'imma distinguishes between deficiency by qisas (option) and by injustice (no option).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي السراجية: ولا يقطع الإبهام بالسبابة ولا بالوسطى. والحاصل أنه لا يؤخذ شيء من الأعضاء إلا بمثله من القاطع. قال محمد في الأصل: وإذا قطع الرجل يد آخر وفيها ظفر سوداء يجب القصاص وإن لم يكن ظفر يد القاطع مسوداً لأن الأسوداد لا يوجب نقصاناً في منفعة اليد وهي البطش ألا ترى أنه لو قطع إنسان يده خطأ كان على عاقلة القاطع نصف الدية، وإذا لم يكن للاسوداد في الظفر أثر في نقصان دية اليد صار وجود هذا العيب وعدمه بمنزلة اليد الشلاء، وإن كان نقصاناً يوهن في البطش حتى يجب بقطعها حكومة عدل لا نصف الدية كان بمنزلة اليد الشلاء واليد الصحيحة لا تقطع بالشلاء. وإذا قطع الرجل يد رجل عمداً ويد القاطع ناقصة فهذا على وجهين : إما أن تكون ناقصة من حيث الصفة بأن كانت شلاء أو كانت ناقصة من حيث الأصابع بأن كانت ناقصة أصبع أو إصبعين فإن كان النقصان من حيث الصفة فالمقطوع يده بالخيار، فإن اختار القطع فلا شيء له مع القطع عندهم جميعاً، وإن شاء لم يقطع واحد يده حتى يصل إليه. بدل حقه على الكمال من ماله وكان الشهيد برهان الائمة يقول : إنما يثبت الخيار للمقطوعة يده في هذه الصورة إذا كانت اليد الشلاء مما ينتفع بها مع ذلك، فأما إذا كانت غير منتفع بها فهي ليست بمحل القصاص فلا يخير المجني عليه حينئذ بل له دية صحيحة كما لو لم يكن القاطع يد المسألة وبه يفتي، وتفريع بعد هذا على حسب ما ذكرنا في العين والسن الكبرى، وكذا لو كان القاطع صحيح اليد عند القطع فشلت يده بعد ذلك لا خيار للمجني عليه بين القصاص والأرش بل يقطع الشلاء أو يترك ولا شيء له، وإن كانت ناقصة فهذا على وجهين : إن كان النقصان حاصلاً لا بفعل أحد وإن كانت ناقصة من حيث القدر فكذلك يتخير، فإن اختار القطع فلا شيء له على القاطع أصلًا وقال الشافعي رحمه الله : أخذ منه أرض ما كان فائتاً من الأصابع. هذا إذا كانت ناقصة وقت القطع فأما إذا نتقصت بعد القطع فهذا على وجهين : إن كان النقصان حاصلاً لا بفعل أحد بأن سقط أصبح من أصابعه بآفة سماوية الجواب فيه كالجواب فيما إذا كانت ناقصة وقت القطع، وكل جواب عرفته ثم فهو الجواب هنا، وإن كان بفعل أحد بأن قطع أصبعاً من أصابعه ظلماً أو قطع القاطع أصبعاً أو قضى به حقاً واجباً عليه فالجواب فيه كالجواب في اليد؛ هكذا ذكر شيخ الإسلام في شرحه فهذا إشارة إلى أن للمقطوع يده الخيار في الفصول كلها غير أن النقصان إذا كان بآفة سماوية واختار قطع اليد لا شيء له من الأرش عنده، وذكر شمس الأئمة الحلواني في شرحه أنه إن قطع أصبعه بقصاص وجب عليه في الأصبح فللمقطوعة يده الخيار وإن قطع يده ظلماً فلا خيار للقطاع وليس له إلا القصاص. وأشار إلى الفرق فقال : إذا قطع أصبعه قصاصاً فقد قضى بها حقاً مستحقاً عليه فيصير متلفاً بعد حق صاحب الحق فيكون له الخيار ولا كذلك ما إذا قطع يده ظلماً، وهذا الفرق إشارة إلى أنها لو سقطت بآفة سماوية فلا خيار له ذكر الشيخ أحمد الطواويسي في شرحه أنها إذا قطعت
In al-Sirajiyya: The thumb is not cut with the index finger nor with the middle finger. The conclusion is that no organ is taken except its exact equivalent from the cutter. Muhammad said in al-Asl: If a man cuts the hand of another and in that hand there is a black nail, qisas is obligatory even if the cutter's hand does not have a black nail, because blackness does not cause a deficiency in the utility of the hand, which is grasping. Do you not see that if someone cuts a hand by mistake, the 'aqila pays half the diya. Since blackness of the nail has no effect in reducing the diya of the hand, the existence or absence of this defect is like a withered hand. But if it is a deficiency that weakens grasping, so that cutting it requires a just compensation rather than half diya, then it is like a withered hand, and a healthy hand is not cut with a withered one. If a man deliberately cuts the hand of another, and the cutter's hand is deficient, this is of two types: either deficient in description, i.e., withered, or deficient in quantity, i.e., missing one or two fingers. If the deficiency is in description, the victim has the option: if he chooses cutting, nothing is due to him along with the cutting according to all (Hanafis); if he wishes, he does not have his hand cut until he receives the full substitute from his property. Al-Shahid Burhan al-A'imma said: the option is established for the victim in this case only if the withered hand is still useful; but if it is not useful, it is not a place for qisas, so the victim is not given a choice; rather, he has a full diya as if the cutter had no hand—and this is what fatwa is given. The details after this are according to what we mentioned for the eye and the large tooth. Likewise, if the cutter's hand was healthy at the time of cutting but later became withered, the victim has no option between qisas and arsh; rather, he cuts the withered hand or leaves it and gets nothing. If it is deficient [in quantity], there are two types: if the deficiency occurred not by anyone's act [but by a divine affliction], and if it is deficient in quantity, then similarly he has an option; if he chooses cutting, he gets nothing from the cutter at all. Al-Shafi'i (may Allah have mercy on him) said: he takes from him the compensation for what was lost of the fingers. This applies if the deficiency existed at the time of cutting. If the deficiency occurred after cutting, there are two types: if the deficiency occurred not by anyone's act, e.g., a finger fell due to a divine affliction, the answer is the same as when it was deficient at the time of cutting; every answer you knew there is the answer here. If it was by someone's act, e.g., he cut a finger of his unjustly, or the cutter cut a finger, or it was taken due to an obligatory right, then the answer is the same as for the hand. Thus mentioned Sheikh al-Islam in his commentary. This indicates that the victim has the option in all sections, except that if the deficiency was by a divine affliction and he chooses to cut the hand, he gets no arsh according to him. Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani mentioned in his commentary that if he cut his finger by qisas, then that finger is obligatory upon him, so the victim has the option; but if he cut his hand unjustly, the cutter has no option and only qisas is upon him. He indicated the difference by saying: if he cut his finger by qisas, he has fulfilled a right due upon him, so he becomes an offender after the right of the owner has been considered, so he has an option; not so if he cut his hand unjustly. This difference indicates that if it falls due to a divine affliction, he has no option. Sheikh Ahmad al-Tawawisi mentioned in his commentary that if it is cut...
Source pages p. 42

Commentary
This passage concludes the discussion on qisas for bodily harm. It begins with a rule from al-Sirajiyya: the thumb cannot be cut for the index or middle finger; only exact equivalents are taken. Then it discusses the case of a hand with a black nail: qisas is valid because the blackness does not impair function (grasping). The analogy is drawn with accidental cutting, where half diya is due regardless of nail color. However, if the deficiency (like weakness) reduces function, it is treated like a withered hand, and a healthy hand is not cut for it. Next, when the cutter's hand is missing fingers, the victim has an option: choose qisas (and get no arsh) or wait for full arsh. But if the withered hand is completely useless, qisas is not possible, and the victim gets full diya. If the cutter's hand becomes defective after the act, the option is lost. For finger deficiency, the same rules apply: if the deficiency is by divine act, no arsh if qisas chosen; Shafi'i disagrees and says arsh for the missing part is due. The passage also cites later scholars: Burhan al-A'imma, Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani, and Ahmad al-Tawawisi, who refine the conditions. The key principle: the victim's option exists only when the deficiency is not by his own fault and when qisas is physically possible (i.e., the limb has some function). If the deficiency is by human act (like prior theft or qisas), the ruling differs.

Key Terms
ظفر سوداء (ẓufr sawdāʾ): A black nail on the hand, considered a cosmetic defect that does not affect function.
حكومة عدل (ḥukūmat ʿadl): A just compensation determined by a judge, used when the injury does not have a fixed diya.
آفة سماوية (āfa samāwiyya): A divine affliction, i.e., a natural cause not due to human action.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if the victim's hand has a black nail and the cutter's hand is healthy, what is the ruling on qisas?
A) Qisas is not valid because the hand is defective.
B) Qisas is valid because blackness does not affect function.
C) Only arsh is due; qisas is not an option.
D) The victim must choose between arsh and qisas, with arsh being preferred.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi qisas, cosmetic defects like black nail do not affect the validity of qisas; only functional impairment matters. The victim's option between qisas and arsh depends on the nature and usability of the deficient limb.

Qisas — Retaliation
intermediate
6 min
Victim's Choice When the Offender's Hand is Defective
Expands qisas rules with cases of defective offender limbs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi khiyar rule when the offender's hand is defective and distinguish between functional and non-functional defects.

Core Idea
If the offender's hand is defective but still functional, the victim may choose qisas or full diyah.

In Hanafi fiqh, qisas requires strict equivalence. But what happens when the offender's hand is already defective? This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains that the victim is given a choice: accept the defective hand in retaliation, or demand full blood-money. The key factor is whether the defect impairs the hand's function. We will unpack the ruling, its proof, and its practical application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the type of defect
Determine whether the defect is in quality (e.g., paralyzed hand) or quantity (missing fingers). This classification affects the ruling.
The text divides defects into two types: al-nuqsan min hayth al-sifa (quality) and al-nuqsan min hayth al-asabi' (quantity).
2
Assess functional impact
For a quality defect (paralysis), check if the hand is still useful (yuntafa‘u biha). If it is, qisas is valid; if not, only diyah is due. For quantity defects (missing fingers), the function of grasping (al-batsh) is presumed unaffected.
The Hanafi position uses functional benefit as the criterion, not mere appearance.
3
Apply the victim's choice
If qisas is valid, the victim has a choice (khiyar): take qisas (accept the defective hand) with no extra compensation, or forgo qisas and claim full diyah from the offender's property.
This choice applies only if the defect existed at the time of the injury; post-injury defects follow different rules.
4
Consider the mufta bihi refinement
According to Burhan al-A'imma (whose view is relied upon for fatwa), if the paralyzed hand is completely useless (ghayr muntafa‘ biha), the victim loses the choice and is entitled only to full diyah.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: the majority of earlier scholars gave the choice even for useless hands, but the fatwa follows Burhan al-A'imma.

وقال الشافعي رحمه الله : أخذ منه أرض ما كان فائتاً من الأصابع. هذا إذا كانت ناقصة وقت القطع فأما إذا نتقصت بعد القطع فهذا على وجهين : إن كان النقصان حاصلاً لا بفعل أحد بأن سقط أصبح من أصابعه بآفة سماوية الجواب فيه كالجواب فيما إذا كانت ناقصة وقت القطع، وكل جواب عرفته ثم فهو الجواب هنا، وإن كان بفعل أحد بأن قطع أصبعاً من أصابعه ظلماً أو قطع القاطع أصبعاً أو قضى به حقاً واجباً عليه فالجواب فيه كالجواب في اليد؛ هكذا ذكر شيخ الإسلام في شرحه فهذا إشارة إلى أن للمقطوع يده الخيار في الفصول كلها غير أن النقصان إذا كان بآفة سماوية واختار قطع اليد لا شيء له من الأرش عنده، وذكر شمس الأئمة الحلواني في شرحه أنه إن قطع أصبعه بقصاص وجب عليه في الأصبح فللمقطوعة يده الخيار وإن قطع يده ظلماً فلا خيار للقطاع وليس له إلا القصاص. وأشار إلى الفرق فقال : إذا قطع أصبعه قصاصاً فقد قضى بها حقاً مستحقاً عليه فيصير متلفاً بعد حق صاحب الحق فيكون له الخيار ولا كذلك ما إذا قطع يده ،ظلماً، وهذا الفرق إشارة إلى أنها لو سقطت بآفة سماوية فلا خيار له ذكر الشيخ أحمد الطواويسي في شرحه أنها إذا قطعت
