المفصل الأعلى
And not the middle finger. The conclusion is that no limb is taken except for its equivalent from the cutter. Muhammad said in al-Asl: If a man cuts off another's hand and it has a black nail, qisas is obligatory even if the cutter's hand's nail is not black, because blackness does not cause a deficiency in the benefit of the hand, which is grasping. Do you not see that if a person cuts off his hand by mistake, half the blood-money is upon the cutter's 'aqila? And when blackness in the nail has no effect in decreasing the blood-money of the hand, this defect's existence and non-existence is like a paralyzed hand. And if it is a deficiency that weakens grasping so that a just compensation (hukuma) is due for cutting it, not half the blood-money, it is like a paralyzed hand, and a healthy hand is not cut for a paralyzed one. And if a man cuts off another's hand intentionally and the cutter's hand is defective, this is in two ways: either it is defective in quality, being paralyzed, or defective in quantity, missing a finger or two fingers. If the deficiency is in quality, the victim has a choice: if he chooses qisas, he gets nothing with the qisas according to all of them; and if he wishes, he does not have his hand cut until he receives the full substitute of his right from the cutter's property. And al-Shahid Burhan al-A'imma said: The choice for the victim is only established in this form if the paralyzed hand is still useful. If it is not useful, then it is not a subject for qisas, so the victim is not given a choice; rather he has the blood-money of a healthy hand, as if the cutter had no hand in the matter, and this is the fatwa. And branching after this is according to what we mentioned regarding the eye and the large tooth. Likewise, if the cutter had a healthy hand at the time of cutting and then it became paralyzed after, the victim has no choice between qisas and compensation; rather he cuts the paralyzed hand or leaves it and gets nothing. And if the deficiency is in quantity, likewise he has a choice. If he chooses qisas, he gets nothing from the cutter. Al-Shafi'i (may Allah have mercy on him) said: He takes from him what is missing of the fingers. This is if it was defective at the time of cutting. But if it became defective after cutting, this is in two ways: if the deficiency occurred not by anyone's action, e.g. a finger fell off due to a divine affliction, the answer is the same as when it was defective at the time of cutting; and every answer you know there is the answer here. And if it was by someone's action, e.g. he cut a finger of his unjustly, or the cutter cut a finger, or he fulfilled an obligatory right upon him, the answer is like the hand. Thus Shaykh al-Islam mentioned in his commentary, indicating that the victim has a choice in all chapters, except that when the deficiency is by a divine affliction and he chooses to cut the hand, he gets no compensation according to him. And Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani mentioned in his commentary that if he cut his finger by qisas (as a right due to him), then the victim of the hand has a choice; but if he cut his hand unjustly, there is no choice for the victim and he only has qisas. He pointed to the difference: if he cut his finger as qisas, he fulfilled an obligatory right due upon him, so he becomes a destroyer after the right of the rightful claimant, so he has a choice; not so if he cut his hand unjustly. This difference indicates that if it fell due to a divine affliction, he has no choice. Shaykh Ahmad al-Tawawisi mentioned in his commentary that if it is cut by qisas, he has a choice; if it is cut unjustly or by divine affliction, he has no choice. This is if the cutter's hand existed at the time of cutting. But if it was missing at the time of cutting, e.g. he cut a man's right hand and the cutter has no right hand, then the victim's right is compensation from the cutter's property because he does not find his exact right, so he has a substitute for his right. And if the cutter's hand existed at the time of cutting and then was lost after, this is in two ways: either it was lost not by his action, by a divine affliction such as an ulcer that caused it to fall, or cut by another unjustly, or lost due to his action such as fulfilling an obligatory right, or he destroyed it himself by cutting his right hand. If it was lost after cutting not by his action, then the victim's right becomes void because the victim's right is in the specific object and it is lost with the loss of the object, like a slave who committed a crime if he dies, and like the property of zakat if it is destroyed, and the cutter does not guarantee. And if he cut the upper joint of a man's finger intentionally, or qisas was taken from him, then one of them later cuts the other's hand intentionally, there is no qisas between them. In al-Nawazil: One whose thumb of the right hand is cut off, if he cuts a forearm of someone like him, there is no qisas. And Muhammad said: If a man cuts a man's finger from the joint, then cuts another's hand and starts with the hand, then cuts the finger, all in one hand (meaning the right or left), and the owner of the finger and the owner of the hand are present and request qisas from the judge, the judge first cuts for the owner of the finger, then gives the owner of the hand a choice: if he wishes, he cuts the second for his sake and gets nothing for the compensation of the finger; if he wishes, he does not cut his hand and he gets the blood-money of the hand from the cutter's property. This is different from the case where he cuts the right hands of two men, then they come and request their rights from the judge: the judge does not start with one but gives them qisas in his right hand and blood-money from his property. This is what we mentioned if the owner of the finger and the owner of the hand are present. But if one is present and the other absent: if the present is the owner of the finger, the finger is not cut for him; if the present is the owner of the hand, then it is cut for him, and when the owner of the finger comes later, he takes the compensation of the finger from his property. And if a man cuts a man's finger from the upper joint, then another cuts from the middle joint, then another cuts another finger from the lower joint, all in one finger, this is in two ways: either the owners of the fingers are all present or some are absent. If all are present and request their right from the judge, the judge cuts from the upper joint for the owner of the upper joint, and the owners of the lower and middle have no right to cut the upper joint except by way of partnership, because the cutter did not place the knife on the joint of their fingers; he only placed it on the joint of the owner of the upper. The right of the owner of the upper is complete. Then he gives the owner of the middle joint a choice. And he only placed it on the owner of the middle joint completely because his right was in two joints, so with the loss of one, he has a choice, just like the owner of the hand after we cut the finger for the owner of the finger. If he wishes, he cuts the middle joint of the cutter and gets nothing of the blood-money of the finger; if he wishes, he does not cut and is guaranteed one-third of the blood-money of the finger because he caused the loss of two joints of the finger, so he guarantees one-third of the blood-money of the finger. And if only one of them is present and the other two are absent, and the present is the owner of the upper joint, then...
Source pages p. 42

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is an expansion (sharh) on the rulings of qisas for injuries to the hand when the offender's own hand is defective or missing parts. The author, Ibn Nujaym, explains the Hanafi position, primarily based on the statements of Imam Muhammad in al-Asl and later scholars. The central principle is that qisas is only due if the limb to be cut is equivalent in function and value to the limb cut off. If the offender's hand is paralyzed (shalla') or missing digits, the victim has a choice between taking qisas (accepting the defective hand) or claiming the full diyah (blood-money) from the offender's property. However, there is a dispute: according to Burhan al-A'imma, if the paralyzed hand is completely useless, qisas is not possible and only the full diyah is due. This is the relied-upon position (mufta bihi). The text also addresses cases where the deficiency occurs after the cut, distinguishing between acts of God and human actions. The Shafi'i opinion is mentioned, which allows taking compensation for missing digits, but the Hanafi response is that the victim's choice is retained. Later, the passage discusses scenarios with multiple claimants (finger owner and hand owner) and the order of qisas when the same offender has injured multiple victims. The judge must first execute qisas for the finger, then give the hand owner a choice. The text also covers the cutting of different joints of the same finger by different offenders, and the rights of each victim. Throughout, the commentary uses analogical reasoning (qiyas) to compare cases like the black nail with a paralyzed hand, and the loss of the hand after judgment with a runaway slave. The authority weight is from Zahir al-Riwayah, as the original rulings are from Muhammad's al-Asl, but later fatwa positions from Burhan al-A'imma and others are incorporated.

Key Terms
شلاء (shalla'): A paralyzed hand that is functionally impaired, but may still have some use.
قصاص (qisas): Retaliation by inflicting an equivalent injury on the offender.
أرش (arsh): Compensation for bodily injury, measured as a fraction of full diyah or estimated by the judge (hukuma).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a man intentionally cuts off another's hand, and the offender's hand is paralyzed (shalla') but still has some functional use, what is the victim's option according to the mufta bihi position?
A) The victim must take qisas and can demand no additional compensation.
B) The victim has the choice between qisas (accepting the paralyzed hand) and demanding full diyah.
C) The victim must take the full diyah and cannot take qisas.
D) The victim can only take compensation for the missing function.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a functional defect in the offender's hand gives the victim a choice between qisas (accepting the defect) and full diyah; only a useless hand removes that choice.

Qisas — Retaliation
intermediate
8 min
Rulings on Qisas When the Cutter's Limb is Missing or Lost Afterward
Exposition of qisas limb-cutting rules

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rules for qisas when the cutter's hand is missing at the time of cutting or is lost afterward, and identify the consequences of each scenario.

Core Idea
If the cutter's hand is missing at the time, only diya is due; if lost afterward without his action, the victim's right to qisas is void.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq outlines the conditions under which qisas for cutting a limb is valid. It handles two scenarios: (1) when the cutter does not have the same limb at the time of the crime, and (2) when the cutter's limb is present but is later lost. Understanding these distinctions is crucial for applying qisas correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the baseline ruling
When the cutter's hand is present at the time of cutting and the act is intentional, the victim has the choice between qisas and diya.
The passage mentions 'falahu al-khiyar' (he has the option) for the intentional case.
2
Case 1: Cutter's hand missing at time of cutting
If the cutter lacks the corresponding limb (e.g., cuts off a right hand but has no right hand), the victim cannot demand qisas because the exact object of retaliation does not exist. He is entitled only to diya (arsh) from the cutter's property.
This is based on the principle that qisas requires equality in the specific limb.
3
Case 2: Cutter's hand present but lost afterward
Two sub-cases: (a) lost not by the cutter's action (e.g., disease, third-party cutting) and (b) lost by the cutter's own action (e.g., fulfilling a necessary right or cutting it himself).
The distinction determines whether the victim's right to qisas remains valid.
4
Consequence of loss not by cutter's action
If the limb is lost without the cutter's direct involvement, the victim's right to qisas becomes void, analogous to a criminal slave dying before execution or complete zakat being destroyed. Only diya remains.
The analogy to the slave and zakat is explicitly mentioned in the text.
5
Note on loss by cutter's own action
If the cutter himself causes the loss (e.g., fulfills a necessary right or deliberately cuts off his own hand), the victim retains the option of qisas or diya. The passage hints at this by implying the opposite of the voiding rule.
The final line about cutting the finger joint and then one cuts the other's hand reinforces that intentional retaliatory acts may not invite further qisas.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فرق بين У بقصاص فله الخيار، وإذا قطعت ظلماً أو بآفة سماوية فلا خيار له هذا إذا كانت يد القاطع قائمة وقت القاطع، فأما إذا كانت فائتة وقت القطع بأن قطع يمين رجل ولا يمين للقاطع فحق المقطوع في الأرش في ماله لأنه لا يجد عين حقه وكان له بدل حقه، وإن كانت يد القاطع قائمة وقت القطع ثم فاتت بعد ذلك فهذا على وجهين : إما إن فاتت لا بفعله بأن فاتت بآفة سماوية بأن وقعت فيها أكلة فسقطت أو قطعها إنسان ظلماً أو فاتت من جهته بأن قضى حقاً واجباً وإن أتلفه بنفسه بأن قطع يمينه، فإن فاتت بعد القطع لا بفعله فإنه يبطل حق المقطوع يده وذلك لأن حق المقطوع يده في العين فيفوت حقه بفوات العين كالعبد الجاني إذا هلك وكمال الزكاة إذا هلك ولا يضمن القاطع يده، وإذا قطع المفصل الأعلى من أصبع رجل عمداً أو اقتص منه ثم قطع أحدهما بعد ذلك يد صاحبه عمداً فلا قصاص بينهما.
Difference between [something]? with qisas, so he has the choice. And if it was cut unjustly or by a divine affliction, then he has no choice. This is when the cutter's hand is present at the time of cutting. But if it was missing at the time of cutting, such as he cut the right hand of a man and the cutter has no right hand, then the right of the one whose hand was cut is in the diya from his property, because he does not find the exact object of his right, and he has a substitute for his right. And if the cutter's hand was present at the time of cutting and then it was lost afterwards, then this has two aspects: either it was lost not by his action, such as it was lost by a divine affliction like a disease that caused it to fall, or a person cut it unjustly, or it was lost by his own doing, such as he fulfilled a necessary right, or he destroyed it himself by cutting his own right hand. If it was lost after the cutting not by his action, then the right of the one whose hand was cut becomes void. That is because the right of the one whose hand was cut is in the specific limb, so his right is lost with the loss of the specific limb, like the slave who committed an offense if he dies, or like the complete zakat if it is destroyed. And the cutter is not liable for his hand. And if someone cuts the upper joint of a man's finger intentionally, or qisas was executed on him, then one of them afterwards cuts the hand of his companion intentionally, then there is no qisas between them.
Source pages p. 43

Commentary
This passage presents a series of rulings on qisas for cutting limbs, focusing on whether the cutter's hand is present or missing at the time of cutting, and what happens if it is lost afterwards. The author distinguishes between intentional cutting (where the victim has the option of qisas or diya) and accidental or divine affliction (where only diya is due). If the cutter lacks the corresponding limb, the victim can only claim diya. If the cutter's hand is later lost without his direct action (e.g., by disease or another person), the victim's right to qisas is lost, analogous to a criminal slave dying before retaliation. If the cutter destroys his own hand, the victim still has the option. The final part states that if after qisas is executed on a finger joint, one of the parties cuts the other's hand, no further qisas is due between them.

Key Terms
قصاص (qisas): Retaliation in kind for a crime against the body; the victim or guardian has the right to exact the same harm on the perpetrator.
أرش (arsh): Monetary compensation for a bodily injury, also called diya when for whole limb; here used synonymously with diya.
دية (diya): Blood money; monetary compensation paid for killing or causing loss of a limb.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person cuts off the right hand of another, but the cutter himself has no right hand, what is the victim entitled to?
A) Qisas on the cutter's left hand
B) Only the diya (arsh) from the cutter's property
C) Both qisas and diya
D) Nothing because equivalent limb is missing

Key Takeaway
The existence of the cutter's corresponding limb at the time of retaliation is essential for qisas; if lost without his action, the right shifts to diya.

Executing Qisas with Multiple Victims and Cuts
Scenarios of qisas with multiple victims and multiple cuts on a limb.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rules for prioritizing qisas when there are multiple victims or multiple cuts on a single limb, and state the options given to each victim.

Core Idea
When multiple victims have claims on one limb, the qadi executes qisas for the higher-level joint first, and later victims face a choice between cutting or taking diya.

This passage from al-Nawazil presents several intricate scenarios where qisas involves multiple victims or multiple cuts on the same limb. Understanding the sequence of execution and the options given to each victim is crucial for correctly applying qisas in complex cases. The Hanafi school has detailed rules to ensure justice is done for each claimant while avoiding excessive punishment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first scenario: missing thumb cuts forearm
Read the initial sentence: 'If a person whose thumb is missing cuts a forearm similar to it, there is no qisas.' Understand that because the cutter already lacks a thumb, his forearm is not equivalent to the victim's forearm, so qisas is not possible.
Equality of limbs is a condition for qisas.
2
Analyze the second scenario: finger cut and hand cut on separate victims
Focus on: 'If a man cuts the finger of one man, then cuts the hand of another...' The qadi is to first cut the cutter's finger for the finger victim, then give the hand victim the option: either have the cutter's hand cut (forgoing any claim to the finger's arsh) or take the diya of the hand.
The order is determined by the priority of the injury? No, the finger victim gets qisas first because his right is over a specific joint; the hand victim's claim is over the entire hand, which includes the finger. After the finger is cut, the hand victim may still have a claim on the remaining part.
3
Examine the third scenario: both hands of two victims cut
Look at: 'If he cuts the right hands of two men...' The qadi exacts qisas for one victim's right hand and awards diya from the cutter's property for the other. The cutter cannot lose both hands, so one victim receives blood money.
This illustrates the principle that qisas cannot exceed the injury in severity or number.
4
Consider the fourth scenario: one victim present, one absent
Read: 'If one is present and the other absent...' If the present victim is the hand owner, qisas is executed immediately; the finger owner later claims arsh. If the present victim is the finger owner, qisas is delayed until the hand owner appears.
The presence of the hand owner is prioritized because his claim is larger and his absence could complicate matters.
5
Analyze the fifth scenario: three cuts on same finger at different joints
Focus on the detailed case where three different persons cut the same finger at upper, middle, and lower joints. The qadi first cuts the upper joint for the upper joint victim. The middle joint victim is then given an option: either cut the middle joint of the cutter (and forgo diya) or take one-third of the finger's diya. The lower joint victim's right is subsumed because his joint is below the others.
The option for the middle joint victim arises because his right was in two joints (middle and lower), but the upper joint cut already eliminated one.
6
Evaluate the final scenario: palm and elbow cuts
Read: 'If a man cuts the palm from the wrist, then another cuts the elbow...' The qadi begins with the palm victim's qisas.
The palm is considered a more severe loss than the elbow, so it is prioritized.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي النوازل : مقطوع الإبهام من يده اليمنى إذا قطع ساعد مثله لا قصاص وقال محمد: إذا قطع الرجل أصبع رجل من المفصل ثم قطع يد آخر وبدأ باليد ثم قطع الأصبع وذلك كله في يد واحد بأن كان في اليمنى وفي اليسرى وحضر صاحب الأصبع والمقطوعة يده وطلبا من القاضي القصاص فإن القاضي يقطع أولاً لصاحب الأصبع ثم يخير صاحب اليد، فإن شاء قطع الثاني لجهته ولا شيء له من أرش الأصبع، وإن شاء لم يقطع يده وكان له دية اليد في ماله، هذا وبين ما إذا قطع يمنى رجلين ثم جاءا أو طلبا حقهما من القاضي فإن القاضي يبدأ بأحدهما بل يقضي لهما بالقصاص في يمينه ودية في ماله هذا الذي ذكرنا إذا كان صاحب الأصبع وصاحب اليد حاضرين، فأما إذا كان أحدهما حاضراً والآخر غائباً، فإن كان الحاضر صاحب الأصبع فلا يقطع الأصبع له وإن كان الحاضر صاحب اليد فإنه يقطع له، وإذا جاء صاحب الأصبع بعد ذلك فإنه يأخذ أرش الأصبع من ماله. ولو قطع رجل أصبع رجل من المفصل الأعلى ثم آخر قطع من المفصل الأوسط ثم آخر قطع أصبعاً أخرى من المفصل السفلى وذلك كله في أصبع واحد هذا على وجهين : إما أن يكون صاحب الأصابع حضوراً أو بعضهم غائباً، فإن كان الكل حضوراً وطلبوا من القاضي حقهم فإن القاضي يقطع من المفصل الأعلى لصاحب المفصل الأعلى، وإن كان صاحب الأسفل والأوسط ثابتاً في الأعلى لأنهما لا حق لهما في قطع المفصل الأعلى إلا على سبيل الشركة لأن القاطع لم يضع السكين على المفصل من أصابعهما وإنما وضع على صاحب المفصل الأعلى حق صاحب الأعلى من كل وجه، ثم خير صاحب المفصل الأوسط، وإنما وضع على صاحب المفصل الأوسط من كل وجه لأن حقه كان في مفصلين لأن الفائت منفصلان فبفوات أحدهما يتخير كما خير صاحب اليد بعدما قطعنا الأصبع لصاحب الأصبع، فإن شاء قطع من القاطع مفصله الوسطى ولا شيء له من دية الأصبع، وإن شاء لم يقطع وضمنه ثلث دية الأصبع لأنه فوت عليه من أصبع مفصلين فيضمن ثلث دية الأصبع. وإن حضر أحدهم وغاب الآخران، فإن كان الحاضر صاحب المفصل الأعلى فإن قطع المفصل الأعلى له ثم حضر الآخران فإنهما يخيران على الوجه الذي ذكرنا، فإن اختار القطع لم يضمن لأحد منهما شيئاً، وإن قطع كف رجل من مفصل ثم قطع الآخر مرفقة وكانا حاضرين فإنه يبدأ بحق صاحب الكف .
And in al-Nawazil: A person whose thumb of his right hand is cut, if he cuts a forearm similar to it, there is no qisas. And Muhammad said: If a man cuts the finger of a man from the joint, then he cuts the hand of another, and he started with the hand and then cut the finger, and all that is in one hand, whether it be in the right or left, and the owner of the finger and the one whose hand was cut are present and ask the qadi for qisas, then the qadi first cuts for the owner of the finger, then gives option to the owner of the hand: if he wishes, he cuts the second for his own sake and nothing for him from the arsh of the finger; and if he wishes, he does not cut his hand and he has the diya of the hand from his property. This and the case where he cuts the right hands of two men and then they come or ask the qadi for their rights, then the qadi begins with one of them, but he decrees qisas for them on his right hand and diya from his property. This is what we mentioned when the owner of the finger and the owner of the hand are present. But if one of them is present and the other absent, then if the present is the owner of the finger, he does not cut the finger for him; and if the present is the owner of the hand, he cuts for him, and when the owner of the finger comes afterwards, he takes the arsh of the finger from his property. And if a man cuts the finger of a man from the upper joint, then another cuts from the middle joint, then another cuts another finger from the lower joint, and all that is in one finger, then this has two aspects: either the owners of the fingers are present or some of them are absent. If all are present and they ask the qadi for their right, then the qadi cuts from the upper joint for the owner of the upper joint, and the owner of the lower and middle are fixed in the upper because they have no right to cut the upper joint except by way of partnership, because the cutter did not place the knife on the joint from their fingers; he only placed it on the owner of the upper joint. The right of the owner of the upper is from every aspect, then he gives option to the owner of the middle joint. He placed it on the owner of the middle joint from every aspect because his right was in two joints, because what is lost are two separate things, so with the loss of one, he has option, just as the owner of the hand was given option after we cut the finger for the owner of the finger. So if he wishes, he cuts from the cutter his middle joint and nothing for him from the diya of the finger; and if he wishes, he does not cut and he is liable for one third of the diya of the finger, because he caused him to lose two joints of a finger, so he is liable for one third of the diya of the finger. And if one of them is present and the other two are absent, then if the present is the owner of the upper joint, he cuts the upper joint for him. Then when the other two come, they are given option in the manner we mentioned. If they choose cutting, they are not liable for anything to either of them. And if a man cuts the palm of a man from the wrist, then another cuts the elbow, and they are both present, then he begins with the right of the owner of the palm.
Source pages p. 43

Commentary
This passage presents several interconnected scenarios from al-Nawazil and the statements of Imam Muhammad. First, if a person with a missing thumb cuts another's forearm, no qisas applies. Second, if a person cuts a finger of one victim and the hand of another, and both victims seek qisas, the qadi first executes qisas for the finger, then gives the hand victim a choice: either have the cutter's hand cut (and forgo any finger compensation) or take diya for the hand. Third, if two victims have their right hands cut, the qadi executes qisas for one and gives diya for the other. Fourth, if one victim is present and the other absent, the present hand victim gets qisas immediately, and the finger victim later takes arsh. Fifth, if three different persons cut the same finger at different joints, the qadi cuts the top joint for the top joint victim first, then gives the middle joint victim the option to cut the middle joint or take diya for two joints. The lower joint victim's right is subsumed. Finally, if a palm is cut and then the elbow is cut, the qadi prioritizes the palm victim's qisas.

Key Terms
نوازل (nawazil): A collection of jurisprudential issues and fatwas; here referring to a specific work of Hanafi fiqh.
مفصل (mafsil): Joint of a finger or limb; the point of amputation for qisas.
أرش (arsh): Compensation for injury less than full diya, determined by the value of the part lost.
دية (diya): Blood money; compensation paid to the victim or heirs for injury or death.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) He cuts the hand first
B) He cuts the finger first
C) He gives both victims the option to take diya
D) He delays until both agree

Key Takeaway
In cases of multiple qisas claims on the same limb, the qadi prioritizes the higher joint or the first injury, and later claimants are given the choice between executing qisas on the remaining part or taking diya.

Diyah Distribution and Rulings on Multiple Cuts
Collection of diyah rulings from al-Kafi and al-Jami' al-Saghir.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate diyah amounts for multiple limb injuries and distinguish between scenarios affecting distribution according to Hanafi fiqh.

Core Idea
Diyah for multiple cuts distributes proportionally: the thumb receives the highest share, and the palm itself has no separate value.

This lesson examines a collection of rulings from two key Hanafi texts, al-Kafi and al-Jami' al-Saghir, on how diyah (blood money) is calculated and distributed when multiple cuts affect different parts of the hand. You will learn the specific values assigned to the thumb, fingers, and palm, and how these amounts interact when multiple claimants are involved. The passage also includes an important intra-Hanafi disagreement on whether qisas can be carried out for death after a hand has already been cut.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Each ruling in the passage presents a specific set of injuries. Read the scenario carefully to determine which limbs are cut and whether the injury is intentional or mistaken.
The first scenario involves two victims with right hands cut, one losing the thumb and the other the palm.
2
Extract the diyah amounts
For each scenario, note the explicit diyah value given in dirhams or as a fraction of the full diya (10,000 dirhams). Pay attention to the proportions: the thumb is 4,000 dirhams, the palm with no fingers is 1,000 dirhams, etc.
From al-Jami' al-Saghir: a hand with one finger gets 1/10 diya (1,000 dirhams); with two fingers, 1/5 (2,000 dirhams).
3
Analyze distribution among claimants
In complex scenarios with multiple cutters or claimants, the total diyah is divided according to the shares specified. The 'qadi' divides the diyah of the cutter's two hands: the palm taker gets one quarter, the finger cutter gets three quarters.
The text emphasizes that a finger cut by a stranger before a qisas claimant's action is not considered as existing for the distribution.
4
Handle the disagreement on qisas
The final ruling presents a difference of opinion between the general view (from al-Jami' al-Saghir al-Husami) that qisas for death can be carried out even after the hand was already cut, and Abu Yusuf's view that the cutter is not killed for the death.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf; the mufta bihi position is not explicitly stated here.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مع وفي الكافي : قطع يمين رجلين فقطع أحدهما إبهامه وقطع الآخر كفه فعلى قاطع اليدين خمسة آلاف درهم لقاطع الإبهام أربعة آلاف ولقاطع الكف ألف درهم، وإن بدأ الأجنبي فقطع أصبعاً من أصابع القاطع ثم قطع أحد صاحبي القصاص بعد ذلك أصبعاً من أصابع اليدين ثم عاد الأجنبي فقطع أصبعاً من أصابع القاطع، ثم أن الذي لم يقطع شيئاً من أصابع القاطع قطع الكف وعليها أصبع فإن القاضي يقضي على القاطع بدية يديه وأخذ ربعها للذي أخذ الكف وثلاثة أرباع للذي قطع الأصبع ولا يجعل الأصبع الذي قطعه الأجنبي قبل قطع أحد صاحبي القصاص قائماً حكماً، فإن اجتمع صاحب القصاص على قطع الكف الأصبعين فالدية المأخوذة تقسم بينهم لقاطع الأصبع والآخر الخمسة إتمامها. وفي الجامع الصغير : رجل قطع يد رجل من المفصل وليس في الكف إلا أصبع واحد ففيه عشر الدين، فإن كان فيه أصبعان فالخمس ولا شيء في الكف. وقالا : ينظر إلى أرش الأصبع بالكف فيكون عليه الأكثر ويدخل القليل في الكثير . سئل أبو يوسف ومحمد عن رجل قطع يد رجل خطأ ثم قطع رجله من خلاف خطأ ماذا يجب عليه؟ فقالا: يجب عليه دية كاملة لكل عضو نصفها. وفي الجامع الصغير الحسامي رجل قطعت يده فاقتص له من اليد ثم مات يقتل المقتص منه وعن أبي يوسف أنه لا يقتص .
And in al-Kafi: One who cuts the right hands of two men, and one of them cut his thumb and the other cut his palm, so the cutter of the two hands owes five thousand dirhams: for the thumb cutter four thousand, and for the palm cutter one thousand. And if a stranger started and cut one finger of the cutter's fingers, then one of the two qisas claimants afterwards cut a finger from the fingers of the two hands, then the stranger returned and cut a finger from the cutter's fingers, then the one who did not cut anything from the cutter's fingers cut the palm while it had a finger on it, then the qadi decrees on the cutter the diya of his two hands, and the one who took the palm takes a quarter, and the one who cut the finger takes three quarters, and he does not consider the finger that the stranger cut before the cutting of one of the two qisas claimants as existent by legal fiction. If the qisas claimants agree on cutting the palm along with the two fingers, then the taken diya is divided among them: for the finger cutter and the other the five completing it. And in al-Jami' al-Saghir: A man cut the hand of a man from the wrist and there is only one finger in the palm, so there is one-tenth of the diya. If there are two fingers, then one-fifth, and nothing for the palm. And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: Look to the arsh of the fingers with the palm, so the greater is upon him and the lesser enters into the greater. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad were asked about a man who cut a man's hand by mistake and then cut his leg from the opposite side by mistake: what is due upon him? They said: A complete diya is due, for each limb half of it. And in al-Jami' al-Saghir al-Husami: A man whose hand was cut, so qisas was executed for him on the hand, then he dies, then the one upon whom qisas was executed is killed (for the death)? And from Abu Yusuf that he is not executed.
Source pages p. 44

Commentary
This passage collects multiple rulings from authoritative Hanafi texts. From al-Kafi: if two victims lose their right hands, one losing the thumb and the other the palm, the total diya is 5000 dirhams: 4000 for the thumb (since it has most of the hand's value) and 1000 for the palm. A complex scenario follows involving a stranger cutting fingers, then qisas claimants, and distribution of diya. From al-Jami' al-Saghir: if a hand has only one finger, the diya is 1/10 of full diya; with two fingers, 1/5; the palm itself has no separate value. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad rule that for a mistaken cut of hand and leg, full diya is due, each limb having half. Finally, from al-Jami' al-Saghir al-Husami: if a victim's hand was cut, qisas executed on the cutter's hand, then the victim dies, there is a difference of opinion: the cutter is not killed for the death according to Abu Yusuf.

Key Terms
دية (diya): Blood money, here calculated in dirhams for specific limbs.
إبهام (ibham): Thumb; its diya is 4,000 dirhams (two-fifths of full diya for a hand).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Jami' al-Saghir, what is the diya for a hand that has only one finger?
A) One-tenth of the full diya
B) One-fifth of the full diya
C) Half of the full diya
D) The full diya

Key Takeaway
Diyah amounts for hand injuries in the Hanafi school are precisely defined: the thumb carries the highest value, and the palm alone has no diyah.

Qisas — Retaliation

Compromise (Sulh) in Qisas Cases
Ruling on compromise for money in qisas, with evidence and distinctions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on sulh in qisas and explain why the monetary compensation is due immediately.

Core Idea
Compromise for money in qisas drops retaliation and creates an immediate debt, unless the amount exceeds diya.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq explains the Hanafi ruling on compromise (sulh) in qisas cases. The key point: if the killer and heirs agree on monetary compensation, qisas is dropped and the money is due immediately, with evidence from Quran and Sunnah. The author also distinguishes this from the right of qadhf and addresses the limit of compensation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
Determine what happens when the killer compromises with the heirs for money. The text states: qisas falls and the money is wajib (obligatory) immediately.
2
Locate the Proofs
Find the dalil cited: Quran 2:178 and the hadith giving heirs the choice between money or execution. These prove the validity of accepting money.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but its meaning (dalala) is clear.
3
Note the Exceptions
Identify two exceptions: (1) qadhf (false accusation) – a right of Allah, so no compromise; (2) if the agreed amount exceeds diya, it is riba and not permissible.
4
Understand Immediacy
Explain why the money is due immediately: it arises from a contract (sulh), which by default imposes immediate obligation, unlike diya which arises from the dropping of qisas.
Analogy: the price (thaman) in a sale and mahr in marriage are also due immediately.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل: لما كان تصور الصلح بعد تصور الجناية أتبع الصلح ذلك في فصل على حدة. قال رحمه الله : (وإن صولح على مال وجب حالاً وسقط القود) يعني إذا صالح القاتل أولياء المقتول على مال عن القصاص سقط القصاص ووجب المال حالاً قليلاً كان المال أو كثيراً لقوله تعالى فمن عفى له من أخيه شيء [البقرة : ۱۷۸] الآية. ولقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام «أولياء المقتول بين خيرتين أن يأخذوا المال أو يقتلوا القاتل» بخلاف حق القذف فإنه حق الله تعالى فلا يجري فيه العفو ولا التعويض وبخلاف ما إذا كان القليل خطأ لا يجوز بأكثر من الدية لأنه دين ثابت في الذمة فيكون أخذ أكثر منها رباً. وإنما حالاً لأنه دين وجب بالعقد والأصل في مثله الحلول كالثمن والمهر بخلاف الدية لأنها لم تجب بالعقد وإنما وجبت بسقوط القود، ولأنه موجب العقد ولأنه لم يرض ببذل
Section: Since the concept of compromise (sulh) comes after the concept of the crime, he followed that with a separate section. He (the author) said: "And if a compromise is made for money, it is due immediately and qisas falls." Meaning, if the killer compromises with the heirs of the slain for money in exchange for qisas, then qisas falls and the money is due immediately, whether the money is little or much, due to the saying of Allah the Exalted: "But whoever forgives his brother anything..." [al-Baqarah 2:178] and due to his saying, peace be upon him: "The heirs of the slain have two choices: to take the money or to kill the killer." Contrary to the right of slander (qadhf), for it is a right of Allah, so neither forgiveness nor compensation applies. And contrary to the case where the little (compensation) is mistaken; it is not permissible to take more than the diya, because it is a debt established in the liability, so taking more would be usury. And it is due immediately because it is a debt that arises from a contract, and the original in such cases is immediacy, like the price (thaman) and dowry (mahr), contrary to diya because it does not arise from a contract but rather arises from the dropping of qisas, and because it is the requirement of the contract, and because he did not consent to payment...
Source pages p. 44

Commentary
This passage introduces a new section on compromise (sulh) in qisas cases. The author states that if the killer and the heirs agree on monetary compensation instead of qisas, the money is due immediately and qisas is dropped. This ruling is supported by the Quranic verse (2:178) which implies accepting compensation, and by a hadith giving the heirs two choices: either take the money or execute qisas. The author distinguishes this from the right of qadhf (false accusation), which is a right of Allah and cannot be compromised for money. Also, if the compensation is less than the diya, it is valid; but if it is more, it is not permissible because it would be akin to usury (riba), since the diya is a fixed debt. The money is due immediately because it arises from a contract (the compromise), unlike the original diya which becomes due only after qisas is dropped. The text ends abruptly, but the reasoning continues.

Key Terms
صلح (sulh): Compromise agreement between the killer and the heirs to accept monetary compensation in lieu of qisas.
قود (qawd): Qisas; retaliation in kind for murder or bodily harm.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the money due immediately in a sulh agreement for qisas, unlike the original diya?
A) Because the Quran commands immediacy
B) Because it arises from a contract, which implies immediate obligation
C) Because the heirs need quick compensation
D) Because qisas is more urgent

Key Takeaway
Compromise (sulh) for money in qisas is valid, drops qisas, and creates an immediately due debt, with the condition that the amount does not exceed diya to avoid riba.

Qisas — Retaliation

6 min
Qisas for Bodily Injuries: Conditions and Priority
Rulings on qisas conditions and priority.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which qisas for bodily injuries is wajib, when it drops, and how priority among multiple victims is determined.

Core Idea
A bodily injury warrants qisas, but if the wound is larger than the attacker's, qisas drops and is halved; settlement converts to obligatory payment.

This lesson covers the foundational rulings on qisas for injuries that do not cause death. The text from Al-Bahr al-Raiq explains when qisas applies, when it falls away, and how priority among multiple victims is determined. These rules ensure precise retaliation or fair compensation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is a bodily injury below the soul (e.g., cutting a limb). The ruling is that qisas is wajib if the injury was intentional and equivalent. If the wound is larger than the attacker's, qisas drops and is halved.
The text begins: 'حالا وسقط القود وتنصف أن أو كان رأس الشاج أكبر' – immediately qisas drops and is halved if the head of the wound is larger.
2
Determine the effect of settlement
If the parties settle for property (مال), then cutting (i.e., qisas) becomes obligatory (وجب يقطع). This means that upon settlement, the right to qisas is replaced by a monetary obligation due immediately.
The phrase 'وإن صولح على مال وجب يقطع' indicates that settlement converts the right to qisas into a wajib payment.
3
Apply priority among multiple victims
When two victims have injuries on different limbs of the same offender, priority is given to the one with the lesser injury (palm owner over elbow cutter). The palm owner's right is executed first, and no guarantee is owed to the other.
The text: 'يبدأ بحق صاحب الكف' – the right of the palm owner is started first.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل كتاب الجنايات باب القصاص فيما دون النفس حالا وسقط القود وتنصف أن أو كان رأس الشاج أكبر وإن صولح على مال وجب يقطع، فإن قطع المفصل الأعلى له ثم حضر الآخران فإنهما يخيران على الوجه الذي ذكرنا، فإن اختار القطع لم يضمن لأحد منهما شيئاً، وإن قطع كف رجل من مفصل ثم قطع الآخر مرفقة وكانا حاضرين فإنه يبدأ بحق صاحب الكف . مع وفي الكافي : قطع يمين رجلين فقطع أحدهما إبهامه وقطع الآخر كفه فعلى قاطع اليدين خمسة آلاف درهم لقاطع الإبهام أربعة آلاف ولقاطع الكف ألف درهم، وإن بدأ الأجنبي فقطع أصبعاً من أصابع القاطع ثم قطع أحد صاحبي القصاص بعد ذلك أصبعاً من أصابع اليدين ثم عاد الأجنبي فقطع أصبعاً من أصابع القاطع، ثم أن الذي لم يقطع شيئاً من أصابع القاطع قطع الكف وعليها أصبع فإن القاضي يقضي على القاطع بدية يديه وأخذ ربعها للذي أخذ الكف وثلاثة أرباع للذي قطع الأصبع ولا يجعل الأصبع الذي قطعه الأجنبي قبل قطع أحد صاحبي القصاص قائماً حكماً، فإن اجتمع صاحب القصاص على قطع الكف الأصبعين فالدية المأخوذة تقسم بينهم لقاطع الأصبع والآخر الخمسة إتمامها. وفي الجامع الصغير : رجل قطع يد رجل من المفصل وليس في الكف إلا أصبع واحد ففيه عشر الدين، فإن كان فيه أصبعان فالخمس ولا شيء في الكف. وقالا : ينظر إلى أرش الأصبع بالكف فيكون عليه الأكثر ويدخل القليل في الكثير . سئل أبو يوسف ومحمد عن رجل قطع يد رجل خطأ ثم قطع رجله من خلاف خطأ ماذا يجب عليه؟ فقالا: يجب عليه دية كاملة لكل عضو نصفها. وفي الجامع الصغير الحسامي رجل قطعت يده فاقتص له من اليد ثم مات يقتل المقتص منه وعن أبي يوسف أنه لا يقتص .
Chapter: Book of Injuries, Section: Qisas for Below the Soul. Immediately, and qisas drops, and it is halved if the head of the wound is larger. And if he settles for property, cutting becomes obligatory. Then if he cuts the upper joint for him, then the other two come, they choose in the manner we mentioned. If they choose cutting, he does not guarantee anything to either. And if a man's palm is cut from a joint, then another cuts his elbow while they are present, then the right of the palm owner is given priority. Also, in Al-Kafi: Two men's right hands are cut, one cut his thumb and the other cut his palm; the one who cut both hands owes five thousand dirhams: four thousand to the thumb-cutter and one thousand to the palm-cutter. And if a stranger begins by cutting a finger from the cutter's fingers, then one of the two qisas companions cuts a finger from the fingers of the hands, then the stranger cuts a finger from the cutter's fingers, then the one who had not cut anything from the cutter's fingers cuts the palm with a finger on it, then the judge rules that the cutter pays the diya of his two hands, one quarter to the one who took the palm and three quarters to the one who cut the finger. And the finger cut by the stranger before one of the qisas companions cut is not considered as existing legally. If the qisas companion joins in cutting the palm of the two fingers, the taken diya is divided among them: for the finger-cutter and the other the fifth, completing it. And in Al-Jami' al-Saghir: A man cuts a man's hand from the joint and there is only one finger in the palm, then it contains one-tenth of the diya. If there are two fingers, then one-fifth, and nothing for the palm. The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: Consider the arsh of the finger with the palm, so the greater is upon him, and the small is included in the large. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad were asked about a man who cuts a man's hand by mistake, then cuts his leg from a different mistake, what is obligatory upon him? They said: A full diya is obligatory for each limb, half of it. In Al-Jami' al-Saghir al-Husami: A man's hand is cut, then qisas is taken from the hand, then he dies; the one from whom qisas was taken is killed. From Abu Yusuf: He does not execute qisas.
Source pages p. 44

Commentary
This passage presents a series of rulings on qisas for injuries below the soul, drawn from authoritative Hanafi sources like Al-Kafi and Al-Jami' al-Saghir. It covers cases of multiple offenders, partial injuries, and the distribution of diyat. The rulings emphasize that qisas may drop in certain situations, and when compromise is made, the settlement amount becomes due immediately. The text also discusses scenarios where multiple victims or perpetrators are involved, detailing how diyat is apportioned. The mention of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad's opinion indicates intra-Hanafi discussion, but the main ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah. The final point about the person from whom qisas was taken dying and whether he is killed reflects a difference between Abu Yusuf and the established position.

Key Terms
القصاص (al-qisas): Retaliation in kind for bodily injury; the right of the victim or heirs to inflict equivalent harm.
الدية (al-diya): Monetary compensation paid to the victim or heirs in lieu of qisas, or for unintentional injuries.
الأرش (al-arsh): The prescribed compensation for a specific injury, varying by severity and body part.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what happens to qisas if the head of the wound is larger than the injury?
A) Qisas is still wajib.
B) Qisas drops and the penalty is halved.
C) Qisas is replaced by diyat only.
D) Qisas is doubled.

Key Takeaway
Qisas for bodily injuries is wajib but drops if the wound is larger than the injury; settlement converts the right to immediate payment.

Multiple Victims and Distribution of Diyat
Rulings on diyat distribution for multiple injuries.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the distribution of diyat when a single offender injures multiple victims in different ways, using the rulings from Al-Kafi and Al-Jami' al-Saghir.

Core Idea
When one person causes injuries to multiple victims, diyat is apportioned according to the severity of each injury, with the thumb considered more valuable than the palm.

This lesson examines cases where a single offender injures multiple victims, such as cutting both hands of two men. The rulings from Al-Kafi and the complex scenario demonstrate how diyat is divided based on the type of injury. These examples help students understand the Hanafi method of apportioning compensation when multiple claims arise from the same act.

Guided Path
1
Identify the injuries and victims
In the Al-Kafi case, two victims each lose a right hand. However, one loses just the thumb, the other loses the entire palm. The offender cut both hands. So we have two distinct injuries: thumb amputation and palm amputation.
The text: 'قطع يمين رجلين فقطع أحدهما إبهامه وقطع الآخر كفه'
2
Note the assigned diyat amounts
The text states that the cutter owes 5000 dirhams total: 4000 to the thumb-cutter and 1000 to the palm-cutter. This indicates the relative value: thumb is more valuable than palm.
Why 4000 and 1000? Because the thumb is considered equivalent to 4000 dirhams (4/5 of the full hand diya?), and the palm is 1000 (1/5). This reflects the Hanafi scale of arsh.
3
Analyze the complex scenario with multiple cutters
In the longer example, multiple offenders cut fingers of a cutter (someone who had cut a hand). The distribution is more intricate: the judge rules that the cutter pays diya of his two hands, with one quarter to the one who took the palm and three quarters to the one who cut the finger. The finger cut by a stranger before qisas does not count as existing.
The purpose is to show priority and how prior acts affect distribution.

Qisas — Retaliation
intermediate
6 min
Specific Rulings on Arsh and Inheritance of Qisas
Rulings on arsh for fingers and death after qisas.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to determine the arsh for a hand with one or two fingers, and explain the ruling on qisas when the victim dies after execution.

Core Idea
When a hand has only one finger, the arsh is one-tenth of diya; with two fingers, it is one-fifth; and if the victim dies after qisas is taken, the offender is killed (except according to Abu Yusuf).

This lesson covers two specific rulings from Al-Jami' al-Saghir. First, the arsh (compensation) for a hand cut from the joint depending on the number of fingers remaining. Second, a unique case where a victim's hand is cut and qisas is taken, but then the victim dies; the Hanafi view is that the offender is killed (qisas for murder), while Abu Yusuf disagrees. These rulings highlight precision in compensation and the interaction between qisas for injury and for death.

Guided Path
1
Identify the hand injury and finger count
The text describes a hand cut at the joint. If the palm has only one finger, the arsh is one-tenth of the full diya. If it has two fingers, it is one-fifth. The palm itself has no separate arsh.
The text: 'ليس في الكف إلا أصبع واحد ففيه عشر الدين... فإن كان فيه أصبعان فالخمس ولا شيء في الكف'
2
Apply the principle of the Sahibayn
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: Look at the arsh of the finger with the palm, so the greater amount is upon him, and the small is included in the large. This means if there are multiple injuries, only the larger arsh is owed, not both.
This is an intra-Hanafi opinion that simplifies compensation.
3
Analyze the death after qisas case
A man's hand is cut, qisas is executed on the offender by cutting his hand. Then the victim dies. The majority view (Zahir al-Riwayah) is that the offender is killed (qisas for death). Abu Yusuf held that he is not executed because the qisas for the hand already satisfied the injury.
This shows the principle that once qisas for the limb is taken, it cannot be repeated; but death introduces a new claim.

According to Abu Yusuf, if a victim dies after qisas for his hand has been taken, what is the ruling?
A) The offender is killed.
B) The offender is not executed.

Key Takeaway
Arsh for a hand depends on finger count (1/10 or 1/5 of diya); after qisas for a limb, if the victim dies, the offender is killed (majority) or not (Abu Yusuf).

Qisas — Retaliation
intermediate
6 min
Compromise on Qisas: Immediate Payment of Property
Explanation of the ruling that compromise on qisas for property makes the money due immediately.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that sulh in qisas makes the money due immediately and explain the evidence from the Quran and Hadith.

Core Idea
Compromise on qisas creates an immediate contractual debt, unlike diya.

In Hanafi fiqh, when the heirs of a murder victim agree to accept property in exchange for dropping the right to retaliation (qisas), the qisas is dropped and the agreed amount becomes due immediately. This ruling is supported by the Quranic verse on forgiveness (Al-Baqarah 2:178) and a hadith granting heirs a choice between money and execution. The commentator in this passage clarifies that the obligation is immediate because it arises from a contract, analogous to the price in a sale or the dower in marriage. This lesson unpacks the textual evidence and the legal reasoning behind the immediacy of payment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and act
What exactly is being ruled upon? It is sulh (compromise) on qisas for property. The hukm: the money is wajib immediately, and qisas drops.
The act is a contract between killer and heirs.
2
Locate the dalil
Two proofs: the Quranic verse (2:178) and the hadith giving heirs the choice. Identify the specific words used.
Quran: 'فمن عفى له من أخيه شيء'; Hadith: 'أولياء المقتول بين خيرتين أن يأخذوا المال أو يقتلوا القاتل'.
3
Analyze the dalil's applicability
How does the verse support sulh? Hanafis interpret 'شيء' as property, making compensation valid. The hadith explicitly mentions taking money.
The dalala of the verse is zanni but supported by hadith.
4
Distinguish from related cases
Contrast sulh on qisas with diya (which is deferred) and with the right of qadhf (which is a divine right not subject to sulh). Understand why the payment is immediate here.
Immediate because it's a contractual debt; diya is not contractual.
5
Consider the critique of absolute wording
The commentator notes the matn's wording is too absolute; it should be restricted to a single victim. Why? Because multiple victims involve different rules (explained later).
This is a typical Hanafi tafsir pointing out limitations in the matn.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل: لما كان تصور الصلح بعد تصور الجناية أتبع الصلح ذلك في فصل على حدة. قال رحمه الله : (وإن صولح على مال وجب حالاً وسقط القود) يعني إذا صالح القاتل أولياء المقتول على مال عن القصاص سقط القصاص ووجب المال حالاً قليلاً كان المال أو كثيراً لقوله تعالى فمن عفى له من أخيه شيء [البقرة : ۱۷۸] الآية. ولقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام «أولياء المقتول بين خيرتين أن يأخذوا المال أو يقتلوا القاتل» بخلاف حق القذف فإنه حق الله تعالى فلا يجري فيه العفو ولا التعويض وبخلاف ما إذا كان القليل خطأ لا يجوز بأكثر من الدية لأنه دين ثابت في الذمة فيكون أخذ أكثر منها رباً. وإنما حالاً لأنه دين وجب بالعقد والأصل في مثله الحلول كالثمن والمهر بخلاف الدية لأنها لم تجب بالعقد وإنما وجبت بسقوط القود، ولأنه موجب العقد ولأنه لم يرض ببذل المال إلا مقابلاً به فيوفر عليه مقصوده وهو الحال. وقوله وإن صولح الخ» أطلق في العبارة فشمل ما إذا كان المقتول متعدداً والقاتل واحداً قبل القضاء بالقصاص أو بعده والإطلاق في محل التقييد لا ينبغي، فلو قال وإن صالح في واحد قبل القضاء بالقصاص أو بعده إلى آخره كان أولى لأن في قولنا في واحد يخرج ما إذا كان المقتول متعدداً والقاتل واحداً أو حصل العفو، وبقولنا قبل القضاء أو بعده يفيد أنه إذا كان المقتول واحداً فالعفو يسقط القصاص قبل القضاء وبعده بخلاف ما إذا كان المقتول متعدداً على تفصيل يأتي بيانه .
Section: Since the concept of compromise arises after the concept of injury, he followed compromise after that in a separate section. He (the author) said: (And if he settles for property, it becomes due immediately and qisas drops) meaning: if the killer settles with the heirs of the slain for property in lieu of qisas, then qisas drops and the property becomes due immediately, whether the property is little or much, due to His words 'But whoever is granted a remission by his brother' [Al-Baqarah 2:178], and due to his (peace be upon him) statement 'The heirs of the slain are given two choices: to take the property or to kill the killer.' Unlike the right of qadhf (slander), for it is a right of Allah, so forgiveness and compensation do not apply. And unlike when the small amount is a mistake, it is not permissible to take more than the diya, because it is a debt established in the dhimmah, so taking more than it would be usury. And it is due immediately because it is a debt that became obligatory by contract, and the default in such is immediacy, like the price and the dowry, unlike the diya because it did not become obligatory by contract but rather became obligatory upon dropping of qisas. And because it is the requirement of the contract, and because he did not consent to give property except in exchange for it, so his objective is preserved, which is immediacy. And his statement 'And if he settles etc.' is absolute in expression, so it includes when the slain is multiple and the killer is one, before or after the judge's ruling on qisas. But absolute in a context that requires restriction is not proper. So if he said 'And if he settles in one case before or after the ruling on qisas etc.' it would be better, because in our saying 'in one case' excludes when the slain is multiple and the killer is one or forgiveness occurred. And by our saying 'before or after the ruling' it indicates that when the slain is one, forgiveness drops qisas before and after the ruling, unlike when the slain is multiple, according to the detail that will come.
Source pages p. 44

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn 'وإن صولح على مال وجب حالاً وسقط القود' from Kanz al-Daqaiq. The commentator explains that when the killer and the heirs agree on a monetary settlement in place of qisas, the qisas is dropped and the agreed amount becomes due immediately, regardless of amount. Two proofs are cited: the Qur'anic verse allowing remission for a price, and the hadith giving heirs the choice between money and execution. The commentator distinguishes this from the right of qadhf (slander), which is a divine right not subject to forgiveness. He also clarifies that the obligation is immediate because it arises from a contract, unlike diya which is not contracted. He then critiques the matn's absolute wording, noting that it should restrict to a single victim, as multiple victims involve different rules. This is a typical Hanafi tafsīr of a ruling, emphasizing the contractual nature of sulh.

Key Terms
الصلح (al-sulh): A compromise or settlement where the heirs accept property in exchange for dropping their right to qisas.
القود (al-qawd): The right to retaliation (qisas) itself.
حالاً (halan): Immediately; the payment is due at the time of contract, not deferred.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Because it is like diya.
B) Because it is a contractual debt akin to price and dowry.
C) Because the killer insists on prompt payment.
D) Because the heirs demand it.

Key Takeaway
Compromise on qisas creates an immediate contractual debt, not a deferred diya-like obligation.

Qisas — Retaliation
intermediate
10 min
Partial Forgiveness and Spouses' Right to Qisas
Ruling with proof and inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling when one heir forgives qisas and state the Hanafi position on spouses' right to qisas, supporting each with the school's proof.

Core Idea
Qisas is indivisible: one heir's forgiveness drops it for all, and spouses, as heirs, claim qisas and diya.

The Hanafi school holds that qisas cannot be divided among heirs; if one heir forgives, qisas drops entirely and the remaining heirs are entitled to their share of diya. This ruling leads to a key dispute: do spouses inherit the right to qisas? The Hanafis affirm it, while Malik, al-Shafi'i, and Ibn Abi Layla deny it. In this lesson, we unpack the reasoning and the proofs.

Guided Path
1
State the main ruling and its rationale
Identify the ruling: if one heir forgives or settles his share, qisas drops for all because it is indivisible. Note why indivisibility matters: qisas cannot be partially executed.
2
Distinguish from the multi-victim case
Contrast with a scenario where one killer murders two people – here, each victim's heirs have independent qisas rights, so one forgiveness does not affect the other. Understand the difference by noting that in our case there is one qisas, in the multi-victim case there are multiple qisas.
3
Identify the dispute over spouses
Recognise that the disagreement is about whether spouses are included among the 'awliya' (heirs) for qisas. The Hanafi school includes them; the opposing schools exclude them.
4
Analyse the opposing proofs
State the arguments of Malik, al-Shafi'i, and Ibn Abi Layla: inheritance is by lineage, not marriage (which ends at death); qisas aims at revenge, which is for blood relatives only.
5
Examine the Hanafi proof
The Hanafi proof is based on a hadith (mentioning spouses as heirs) and the principle that all heirs share the right. Note that the hadith is cited partially in the text; the full version supports the Hanafi view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله: (فإن صالح أحد الأولياء حظه على عوض أو عفا فلمن بقي حظه من الدية لأن كل واحد منهم متمكن من التصرف في نصيبه استيفاء وإسقاطاً بالعفو وبالصلح لأنه يتصرف في خالص حقه فينفع. عفوه وصلحه فسقط حقه من القصاص، ومن ضرورية سقوط حقه سقوط حصة الباقين أيضاً فيه لأنه لا يتجزئ، ألا ترى أنه لا يثبت إلا في محله من حيث الجملة فيتجزئ ثبوتاً فكذا سقوطاً. وفي عبارة المصنف يتجزئ قصور من وجهين : الأول أنه يقال صالح عن كذا. وذكر في الكتاب كلمة من الثاني قوله من نصيبه يوهم تجزئ القصاص وقد قدمنا أنه لا يتجزئ، قال الشارح: بخلاف ما لو قتل رجلين فعفا أولياء أحدهما حيث يكون لأولياء الآخر قتله لأن الواجب فيه قصاصان لاختلاف القاتل والمقتول فسقوط أحدهما لا يسقط الآخر ألا ترى أنهما يفترقان ثبوتاً، وكذا بقاء بخلاف ما نحن فيه فإذا سقط انقلب نصيب من لم يعف مالاً لأنه تعذر استيفاؤه فيجب المال كما في الخطأ فإن سقوط القصاص فيه لمعنى في القتل وهو كونه مخطأ ولا يجب للعافي شيء لأنه أسقط حقه المتعين بفعله ورضاه بلا عوض بخلاف شركائه لعدم ذلك منهم فينقلب نصيبهم مالاً والورثة في ذلك كلهم سواء. وقال مالك والشافعي: لا حق للزوجين في القصاص ولا في الدية لأن في الوراثة خلافه وهي بالنسب دون السبب لانقطاعه بالموت. وقال ابن أبي ليلى لا يثبت حقهما في القصاص لأن سبب استحقاقهما العقد والقصاص لا يستحق بالعقد ألا ترى أن الوصي لا يثبت له حق في القصاص لأن المقصود في القصاص التشفي والانتفاع وذلك يختص به الأقارب الذين ينصر بعضهم بعضاً ولهذا لا يكون أحدهما عاقلة الآخر لعدم التناصر . ولنا قوله عليه الصلاة والسلام «من ...»
He (the author) said: (If one of the heirs settles his share for a consideration or forgives, then for the remaining heir is his share of the diya). Because each of them is able to dispose of his share by execution or dropping through forgiveness or compromise, since he acts in his own exclusive right, so his action is effective. His forgiveness and compromise drop his right to qisas, and necessarily from the dropping of his right, the share of the others also drops in it because it is indivisible. Do you not see that it is not established except in its place as a whole, so it is divisible in establishment? Likewise in dropping. In the author's statement, 'his share' has a deficiency in two aspects: first, he says 'settles for such and such', and second, his saying 'his share' suggests that qisas is divisible, and we have already stated that it is not divisible. The commentator said: Unlike if he kills two men and the heirs of one forgive, then the heirs of the other have the right to kill him because the obligation there is two qisas due to the difference of killer and slain, so dropping one does not drop the other. Do you not see that they differ in establishment and likewise in remaining, unlike our case. So when it drops, the share of the one who did not forgive converts to property because its execution becomes impossible, so property becomes obligatory as in mistake. It is not obligatory for the one who forgives anything because he dropped his specific right by his own action and consented without compensation, unlike his partners because they did not do that, so their share converts to property, and all heirs are equal in that. Malik and al-Shafi'i said: The spouses have no right to qisas nor to diya because inheritance is otherwise, and it is by lineage not by cause (marriage), due to its termination by death. Ibn Abi Layla said: Their right to qisas is not established because the cause of their entitlement is contract, and qisas is not entitled by contract. Do you not see that the guardian does not have a right to qisas? Because the purpose of qisas is revenge and benefit, and that is specific to relatives who support each other. For this reason, one is not the 'aqlah (blood money paying group) of the other due to lack of mutual support. Our proof is his statement (peace be upon him): 'Whoever...' (hadith incomplete).
Source pages p. 45

Commentary
This passage explains the matn: if one of the heirs (e.g., of a murdered person) settles his share for compensation or forgives, then qisas drops entirely because it is indivisible, and the remaining heirs become entitled to their share of the diya (blood money). This is contrary to a case where two separate murders occur, where forgiveness by one set of heirs does not affect the qisas of the other. The commentator also critiques the author's phrasing 'min nasibihi' (from his share) as implying divisibility of qisas. Then a major inter-madhhab dispute is presented: Malik, al-Shafi'i, and Ibn Abi Layla argue that spouses (husband and wife) have no right to qisas or even diya because their inheritance is through marriage (contract), which ends at death, and qisas is only for blood relatives. The Hanafi position, supported by a hadith (incomplete here), is that spouses do inherit the right to qisas (and diya). The Hanafi argument is that the purpose of qisas includes consolation for all heirs, and the hadith 'Whoever kills a person...' includes all heirs. This dispute has practical consequences: under Hanafi law, a spouse can demand qisas or take diya, while under Shafi'i/Maliki, the spouses get nothing from qisas or diya.

Key Terms
الأولياء (al-awliya): The heirs of the victim who have the right to demand qisas or accept diya.
العفو (al-afw): Forgiveness; dropping the right to qisas without compensation.
القصاص (al-qisas): Retaliatory punishment; the right to kill the murderer in kind.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Qisas still applies for the other heirs
B) Qisas drops and the other heirs get their share of diya
C) The forgiving heir must pay diya to the others
D) The killer goes free

Key Takeaway
Qisas is indivisible: one heir's forgiveness drops it for all, and spouses have a right to qisas and diya under Hanafi law.

Qisas — Retaliation
intermediate
6 min
Sulh for Free and Slave Killers and Effect of Heir's Forgiveness
Ruling on sulh by representative and effect of partial forgiveness

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the effect of one heir's forgiveness on qisas and explain why the remaining heirs receive diya.

Core Idea
Qisas is indivisible: forgiveness by one heir voids it for all, converting remaining shares to diya.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains a scenario where a representative is appointed to negotiate a settlement (sulh) for two killers—one free, one slave. The payment is divided equally. The crucial point is the effect of one victim's heir forgiving his share of qisas: according to the Hanafi school, qisas cannot be divided, so forgiveness by one heir drops the right entirely, and the remaining heirs receive their shares of diya. The commentator also refines the wording of the original matn to avoid ambiguity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the sulh made by a representative for two killers (one free, one slave) at the instruction of the free killer and the slave's master. The ruling: the payment is divided equally between them.
The payment substitutes for qisas, which is equally upon both.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The proof is derived from qiyas (analogical reasoning): qisas is indivisible in its establishment—it cannot be partially established—so it is also indivisible in its dropping. Therefore, forgiveness by one heir drops the entire qisas.
The analogy is based on the nature of qisas as a single right.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The legal link: if qisas cannot be partially established (e.g., one heir cannot claim half the killer's life), then it cannot be partially dropped. Hence, forgiveness by any heir extinguishes the entire right.
This is contrasted with the case of multiple victims, where each has a separate qisas right.
4
Note the ikhtilaf (disagreement) and refinement
The commentator criticizes the matn's absolute wording, which might suggest that the ruling applies even when multiple victims are killed. He restricts it to a single victim. The correct Hanafi position is that if one heir forgives, qisas drops entirely, but the remaining heirs get diya.
The refinement clarifies that the rule is for a single victim; multiple victims give separate qisas rights.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih (preferred view)
The Hanafi position is that qisas is indivisible in both establishment and dropping. This is the mufta bihi (operative ruling) for fatwa. The evidence from qiyas is considered strong (zanni in thubut but clear in dalala).
Other schools may have different views, but within Hanafi, this is settled.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أمر الحر القاتل وسيد القاتل رجلاً بالصلح عن دمهما على ألف ففعل فإن صالح أحد الأولياء من حظه على عوض أو عفا فلمن بقي حظه من الدية ويقتل الجمع بالمفرد المال إلا مقابلاً به فيوفر عليه مقصوده وهو الحال. وقوله وإن صولح الخ» أطلق في العبارة فشمل ما إذا كان المقتول متعدداً والقاتل واحداً قبل القضاء بالقصاص أو بعده والإطلاق في محل التقييد لا ينبغي، فلو قال وإن صالح في واحد قبل القضاء بالقصاص أو بعده إلى آخره كان أولى لأن في قولنا في واحد يخرج ما إذا كان المقتول متعدداً والقاتل واحداً أو حصل العفو، وبقولنا قبل القضاء أو بعده يفيد أنه إذا كان المقتول واحداً فالعفو يسقط القصاص قبل القضاء وبعده بخلاف ما إذا كان المقتول متعدداً على تفصيل يأتي بيانه . قال رحمه الله : ( وتنصف أن أمر الحر القاتل وسيد القاتل رجلاً بالصلح عن دمهما على ألف ففعل) معناه لو كان القاتل حراً وعبداً فأمر الحر القاتل ومولى العبد رجلاً بأن يصالح عن دمهما على ألف درهم ففعل المأمور فالألف على الحر والعبد نصفان لأنه مقابل بالقصاص وهو عليهما على السواء فيقسم بدله عليهما بالسواء، ولأن الألف وجبت بالعقد وهو مضاف إليهما فينصف موجبه وهو الألف عليهما. قال رحمه الله: (فإن صالح أحد الأولياء حظه على عوض أو عفا فلمن بقي حظه من الدية لأن كل واحد منهم متمكن من التصرف في نصيبه استيفاء وإسقاطاً بالعفو وبالصلح لأنه يتصرف في خالص حقه فينفذ عفوه وصلحه فسقط حقه من القصاص، ومن ضرورة سقوط حقه سقوط حقه عن الباقين أيضاً فيه لأنه لا يتجزئ، ألا ترى أنه لا يثبت بعضه فكذا سقوطاً. وفي عبارة المصنف يتجزئ قصور من وجهين : الأول أنه يقال صالح عن كذا. وذكر في الكتاب كلمة من الثاني قوله من نصيبه يوهم تجزئ القصاص وقد قدمنا أنه لا يتجزئ، قال الشارح: بخلاف ما لو قتل رجلين فعفا أولياء أحدهما حيث يكون لأولياء الآخر قتله لأن الواجب فيه قصاصان لاختلاف القاتل والمقتول فسقوط أحدهما لا يسقط الآخر ألا ترى أنهما يفترقان ثبوتاً، وكذا بقاء بخلاف ما نحن فيه فإذا سقط انقلب نصيب من لم يعف مالاً لأنه تعذر استيفاؤه فيجب المال كما في الخطأ فإن سقوط القصاص فيه لمعنى في القتل وهو كونه مخطأ ولا يجب للعافي شيء لأنه أسقط حقه المتعين بفعله ورضاه بلا عوض بخلاف شركائه لعدم ذلك منهم فينقلب نصيبهم مالاً والورثة في ذلك كلهم سواء.
He ordered the free killer and the master of the killer a man to make a settlement for their blood for a thousand, so he did. If one of the heirs settled his share for compensation or forgave, then for the remaining is his share of the blood money. And a group is killed for one individual, but not if money is taken in exchange... etc. His statement 'and if he made a settlement' is absolute in expression, so it includes whether the killed person is multiple and the killer is one before judgment of qisas or after, and absoluteness in a place requiring restriction is not proper. So if he said 'and if he made a settlement for one before or after judgment' it would be better... He said: (And he apportions equally that the free killer and master of the killer ordered a man to make a settlement for their blood for a thousand, so he did) meaning if the killer was free and a slave, so the free killer and the master of the slave ordered a man to make a settlement for their blood for a thousand dirhams, and the ordered man did, then the thousand is on the free and slave equally because it is in exchange for qisas, which is upon them equally, so its substitute is divided equally between them... He said: (If one of the heirs settled his share for compensation or forgave, then for the remaining is his share of the blood money) because each of them is able to dispose of his share by execution or dropping, and because he disposes of his exclusive right, so his forgiveness and settlement are effective, and his right to qisas drops, and necessarily the right of the remaining also drops because it is not divisible... This is unlike if he killed two men and the heirs of one forgave, because the obligation there is two qisas due to the difference of killer and killed... The text's expression has shortcomings... (Then the dispute about spouses is not included here).
Source pages p. 45

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on an arrangement where a representative is appointed to negotiate a settlement for the blood of two killers (one free, one slave). The author explains that the payment (the thousand dirhams) is divided equally between them because it is in exchange for qisas, which is equally upon both as they share the killing. Then, if one of the heirs (from the victim's side) forgives or settles his share, the remaining heirs get their portion from the blood money (diya), because qisas cannot be divided: once part of it is dropped, the whole is dropped. The author criticizes the wording of the original text (Kanz al-Daqa'iq) for being too absolute and suggests a more precise phrasing. The commentary contrasts this case with a scenario where one killer kills two victims: there, each victim's heirs have independent claims, so forgiveness by one set does not affect the other. Here, the single victim's qisas is indivisible, so forgiveness by one heir converts the remaining heirs' share to diya. All heirs are equal in this regard.

Key Terms
الصلح (al-sulh): A settlement or compromise to drop qisas in exchange for compensation.
الولي (al-wali (plural: awliya')): The heir of the victim who has the right to execute qisas or forgive.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) The killer is freed without any payment.

Key Takeaway
Qisas is indivisible: forgiveness by any heir drops the right entirely, converting the remaining heirs' claims to diya.
