Do Spouses Inherit Qisas and Diya? Hanafi Refutation of Opposing Views
Hanafi refutation of opposing views on spouses inheriting qisas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on spouses inheriting qisas and diya, identify the opposing proofs, and explain the Hanafi rebuttal.

Core Idea
Spouses inherit qisas and diya because inheritance is by marital tie, not by a contract that ends at death.

In this passage, the Hanafi school defends the right of spouses to inherit qisas (retaliation) and diya (blood money) from their murdered spouse. The opposing schools—Maliki, Shafi'i, and Ibn Abi Layla—rely on arguments based on blood relation and the nature of qisas as vengeance. The Hanafi response uses a prophetic hadith, the practice of the Prophet and Ali, and qiyas (analogical reasoning) to establish the inheritance right.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi Position
Identify that the Hanafi school holds that both husband and wife inherit qisas and diya from their murdered spouse. This is the core ruling being defended.
The ruling applies to spouses, not to other relatives by marriage.
2
Identify the Opposing Views and Their Proofs
Malik and al-Shafi'i deny any right for spouses in qisas or diya, arguing inheritance is by lineage, not cause (contract), which ends at death. Ibn Abi Layla specifically denies qisas because it is a right of vengeance for supportive relatives, and spouses do not support each other in that way (e.g., not part of 'aqila).
Note the different nuances: Malik/Shafi'i deny both; Ibn Abi Layla denies only qisas.
3
Analyze the Hanafi Dalil (Proof)
The primary Hanafi proof is the hadith: 'Whoever leaves wealth or a right, it belongs to his heirs.' Qisas is a right, so it is included. Also, the Prophet ordered the wife of Asim al-Dhababi to inherit his diya. This shows practical application.
The hadith is general, and qisas is a subset of 'right'.
4
Examine the Hanafi Rebuttal
The Hanafi response argues that inheritance is based on the marital tie, which persists after death in a legal sense. The objection about lack of 'aqila support is irrelevant because women relative (like mothers) also inherit qisas without being 'aqila. Thus, the analogy with other heirs is sound.
The rebuttal uses qiyas and the principle that inheritance follows the legal relationship, not physical strength.
5
Identify the Practical Consequence (Thamarah al-Khilaf)
In Hanafi practice, if a married person is killed, the spouse gets a share in qisas or diya. In Maliki/Shafi'i, the spouse gets nothing from qisas or diya. This affects the distribution of blood money and retaliation rights.
This difference impacts estate planning and criminal proceedings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال مالك والشافعي: لا حق للزوجين في القصاص ولا في الدية لأن في الوراثة خلافه وهي بالنسب دون السبب لانقطاعه بالموت. وقال ابن أبي ليلى لا يثبت حقهما في القصاص لأن سبب استحقاقهما العقد والقصاص لا يستحق بالعقد ألا ترى أن الوصي لا يثبت له حق في القصاص لأن المقصود في القصاص التشفي والانتفاع وذلك يختص به الأقارب الذين ينصر بعضهم بعضاً ولهذا لا يكون أحدهما عاقلة الآخر لعدم التناصر . ولنا قوله عليه الصلاة والسلام «من ترك مالاً أو حقاً فلورثته» الحديث والقصاص حقه فيكون الجميعهم كالمال، وأمر عليه الصلاة والسلام بتوريث امرأة أسيم الضبابي من دية زوجها أسيم، ولأن القصاص حق يجري فيه الإرث حتى إذا قتل وله ابنان فمات أحدهما عن ابن كان القصاص بين الابن وبين ابن الابن فيثبت كسائر الورثة والزوجية تبقى بعد الموت حكماً كما في حق الإرث أو يثبت الإرث مستنداً إلى سببه وهو الجرح، وكان على رضي الله عنه يقسم الدية على من أحرز الميراث. والدية حكمها حكم سائر الأموال ولهذا لو أوصى بثلث ماله تدخل الدية فيه والقصاص بدل النفس كالدية فيورث كسائر أمواله ولهذا لو انقلبت مالا يقضى به دینه وتنفذ به وصاياه واستحقاق الإرث بالزوجية كاستحقاقه بالقرابة لا بالعقد ألا أنه لا يرتد بالرد بخلاف الوصية ولهذا يتبين أن الاستحقاق ليس بالعقد بل بالعقد ولا يلزم من عدم التناصر وعدم العقل عدم الإرث للقصاص ألا تری أن النساء من الأقارب لا يعقلن ويرثن القصاص والدية أقرب منه إذا المرأة لا تعقل عنها أبناؤها الكبار ويرثونها.
Malik and al-Shafi'i said: The spouses have no right in qisas nor in diya because inheritance is otherwise (i.e., based on lineage, not cause) and it is by lineage, not by cause, as it ends at death. Ibn Abi Layla said: Their right in qisas is not established because the cause of their entitlement is contract (marriage), and qisas is not entitled by contract. Do you not see that the guardian (executor) has no right in qisas? Because the purpose of qisas is vengeance and benefit, and that is specific to relatives who support one another... Our proof: The Prophet's saying 'Whoever leaves wealth or a right, it is for his heirs' and qisas is a right, so it is for them like wealth. And he ordered the inheritance of the wife of Asim al-Dhababi from her husband's blood money. And because qisas is a right in which inheritance applies... Ali (RA) used to divide the blood money among those who inherited. And diya is like other wealth...
Source pages p. 45

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute about whether spouses (husband and wife) inherit the right to qisas and diya. Malik and al-Shafi'i deny it, arguing inheritance is by blood relation not by marriage contract that ends at death. Ibn Abi Layla also denies it for qisas, saying qisas is for vengeance which is for supportive relatives, not for spouses who do not act as 'aqila (blood money payers). The Hanafi response uses the hadith 'Whoever leaves wealth or a right, it is for his heirs' to include qisas as a right. Also, the Prophet (SAW) ordered the wife of Asim al-Dhababi to inherit his diya. Furthermore, qisas involves inheritance, as seen when a son predeceases his father, his son inherits qisas. Ali (RA) distributed diya among all inheritors. The Hanafi position is that spouses inherit qisas and diya because they are heirs; the inheritance is based on marital tie which persists after death, not like a contract. The objection about lack of 'aqila support is irrelevant because women do not pay 'aqila but still inherit qisas.

Key Terms
الزوجان (al-zawjan): The married couple: husband and wife.
العاقلة (al-'aqila): The male relatives who pay blood money on behalf of the killer.
القصاص (al-qisas): Retaliation in kind for murder or injury.
الدية (al-diya): Blood money compensation paid to the heirs of a murder victim.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, do spouses inherit the right to qisas (retaliation) from their murdered spouse?
A) Only the husband inherits, not the wife.
B) Only the wife inherits, not the husband.
C) Both husband and wife inherit qisas and diya.
D) Neither inherits; it goes only to blood relatives.

Key Takeaway
Spouses inherit qisas and diya because the marital bond is a basis for inheritance that persists after death, and qisas is a right included in the general hadith.

Group Executed for Killing One Person: Istihsan Over Qiyas
Ruling that multiple killers can be collectively executed for one victim

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on collective qisas and explain why istihsan overrides the qiyas based on equality.

Core Idea
Hanafi qisas applies to all participants in a group killing – deterrence overrides the qiyas of one-for-one equality.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents the Hanafi position on qisas when a group kills a single victim. The default qiyas (analogy) would suggest that only one life can be taken for one life, but the Hanafi school adopts istihsan (juristic preference) based on the action of Caliph Umar (RA), allowing execution of all participants to deter gang violence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
State the ruling as given at the beginning: 'A group is killed for one individual.'
This is the mufta bihi position.
2
Locate the primary proof
Find the report of Umar executing seven from San'a. Note that this is a companion action used as evidence.
The proof is a sunna (fi'li) with a statement.
3
Understand the counter-argument (qiyas)
The qiyas argument: equality (musawat) required in qisas, so ten lives cannot be taken for one. This is supported by Quran 5:45.
Qiyas jali: one-to-one correspondence.
4
Analyze the istihsan reasoning
Istihsan overrides qiyas because otherwise the door of qisas would be closed and gang killing would increase. Each participant is considered as if alone killed.
The purpose of deterrence (zajr) is achieved.
5
Note the unresolved discussion
The author (Ibn Nujaym) questions setting aside a Quranic verse on the basis of a single companion's action, but the passage cuts off.
This shows the critical attitude within the Hanafi tradition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : ( ويقتل الجمع بالمفرد) لما روي أن سبعة من أهل صنعاء قتلوا واحداً فقتلهم عمر به وقال : لو تمالاً عليه أهل صنعاء لقتلتهم. ولأن القتل بطريق التغالب والقصاص شرع حكمه للزجر فيجعل كل واحد منهم كالمنفرد به فيجري القصاص عليهم جميعاً تحقيقاً لمعنى الإحياء، ولولا ذلك لسد باب القصاص وفتح باب التغالب إذ لا يوجد القتل من واحد غالباً لأنه يقاومه الواحد فلم يقدر عليه فلم يحصل إلا نادراً والنادر يشرع فيما يغلب لا فيما يندر . قال صاحب النهاية : هذا جواب الاستحسان. وفي القياس لا يلزمهم القصاص لأن المعتبر في القصاص المساواة لما في الزيادة من الظلم على المتعدي وفي النقصان من النجس بحق المتعدي عليه ولا مساواة بين العشرة والواحد في شيء هذا يعلم ببداهة العقل فالواحد من العشرة يكون مثلاً للواحد فكيف تكون العشرة مثلاً للواحد؟ وأيد هذا القياس قوله تعالى وكتبنا عليهم فيها أن النفس بالنفس ﴾ [المائدة : ٤٥] وذلك ينفي مقابلة النفوس بنفس ولكن ترك هذا القياس بما روي أن سبعة من أهل صنعاء قتلوا رجلاً فقضى عمر رضي الله عنه بالقصاص عليهم وقال : لو تمالاً عليه أهل صنعاء لقتلتهم به انتهى كلامه. أقول : فيه بحث لأنه بأن هذا القياس مقيد بقوله تعالى وكتبنا عليهم فيها أن النفس بالنفس ﴾ [المائدة: ٤٥] وقال في بيانه : وذلك ينفي مقابلة النفوس بنفس فعلى ذلك يلزم من ترك هذا القياس ترك العمل بمدلول الآية المذكورة وذا لا يجوز بما روي عن عمر رضي الله عنه لأن عمر إن كان منفرداً في قضائه
He said: (And a group is killed for one individual) because it is narrated that seven people from San'a killed one man, so Umar executed them all and said: 'If all the people of San'a had conspired against him, I would have killed them all.' And because killing is by way of overpowering, and qisas is legislated for deterrence, so each one is considered as if he alone killed, and qisas applies to all, achieving the meaning of giving life. Otherwise, the door of qisas would be closed and the door of overpowering opened... The author of al-Nihaya said: This is the answer of istihsan. By qiyas, qisas is not required because equality is considered in qisas... Qiyas is supported by the verse 'a life for a life' which negates multiple lives for one life. But this qiyas is abandoned due to the report that seven from San'a killed a man and Umar executed them... I say: There is a discussion here...
Source pages p. 46

Commentary
This passage states the ruling that multiple killers may all be executed in retaliation for a single victim. The proof is the historical incident of Umar ibn al-Khattab (RA) executing seven men who collectively killed one person, and his statement that he would kill all the people of San'a if they conspired. The rationale (istihsan) is that qisas serves as a deterrent against gang violence; if only one could be executed, people would kill through groups to avoid punishment. The text contrasts this with qiyas (analogy) which would argue that executing ten for one is not equal, and is supported by the Quranic verse 'an eye for an eye' implying one-to-one equality. However, the qiyas is overridden by the sunna of Umar and istihsan. The author (Ibn Nujaym) raises a discussion about the validity of setting aside the Quranic verse based on a single companion's action, but the passage does not resolve it fully as it cuts off.

Key Terms
الاستحسان (al-istihsan): Preferring a ruling that deviates from qiyas due to a stronger evidence, such as a companion's action or public interest.
التغالب (al-taghalub): Overpowering through collective action; killing by a group.
المساواة (al-musawat): Equality required in qisas: one life for one life.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary evidence that the Hanafi school uses to support the ruling that a group can be executed for one victim?
A) The Quranic verse 'a life for a life' (5:45).
B) The consistent practice of the four Rightly Guided Caliphs.
C) The incident of Umar executing seven men from San'a who killed one person.
D) A hadith directly from the Prophet (PBUH) stating 'kill the group for the one'.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school rules that all participants in a collective killing are liable for qisas, applying istihsan to override the qiyas of one-to-one equality.

One Person Killed for a Group: Qisas for Multiple Victims
Commentary on the ruling that one execution suffices for multiple victims, with proof and refutation of Shafi'i.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on executing a single killer for multiple victims, explain the Hanafi proof from the Quran, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
One execution suffices for all victims — the killer's life is forfeit for each right to life.

This lesson examines a distinctive Hanafi principle in qisas: if one person kills multiple victims, he is executed once for all. The passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq defends this against the Shafi'i view that only the first victim's right is fulfilled. We will unpack the Hanafi proof, the Quranic interpretation, and practical applications.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling
Identify the act (single killer, multiple victims) and the Hanafi position: one execution suffices for all victims.
The matn says 'al-fardu bil-jam'i iktifa'.
2
Examine the proof
Analyze how the Hanafi school derives this from Quran 5:45. The verse 'an-nafsu bin-nafs' establishes equivalence of life for life, but does not specify numerical matching. Hanafi usul interprets it as genus equivalence.
The dalil_block in the toolbox provides details.
3
Contrast with Shafi'i
State the Shafi'i view: the killer is executed only for the first victim. Their proof is the apparent one-to-one correspondence in the verse.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The commentary rebuts the Shafi'i argument by noting that the verse does not specify 'one life for one life' but rather 'life for life' generically. Also, the act of killing each victim is complete, so execution for all is just.
The text uses analogy with limb injuries to show that specificity is derived elsewhere.
5
Apply to sub-rulings
Consider scenarios: if some heirs are absent, if forgiveness occurs, or if there are also limb injuries. This shows the practical effect of the principle.
The passage discusses these in detail.

بالنفس لا ينافيه لأنهم في إزهاق الروح الغير المتجزئ عن مجموعهم وجعلهم كشخص واحد . اهـ كلامه أقول : فيه نظر لأن جعل الأشخاص المتعددة الذوات في الحقيقة شخصاً واحداً بمجرد صدور إزهاق الروح الغير المتجزيء من مجموعهم وجعلهم متساوين كشخص واحد بحيث يتحقق بين ذلك الشخص الواحد وبين ؤلاء الجماعة مماثلة معتبرة في القصاص بعيد جداً عن مساعدة العقل والنقل، وأيضاً ينافي هذا ما سيأتي في تعليل المسألة الآتية من أن الأصل أن كل واحد منهم قاتل بوصف الكمال الصادر منهم بهذا الاعتبار فثلاث متعددة على عدد رؤوسهم فحصلت المماثلة المعتبرة في القصاص والحق عندي ههنا أن يقال : إن قوله تعالى أن النفس بالنفس لا ينافي ما قالوا تعالى والعين بالعين لا يدل عليه نظراً إلى ظاهر إطلاقه بل إنما يستفاد ذلك من دليل آخر فكذا هنا تبصر . قال رحمه الله : والفرد بالجمع اكتفاء) يعني إذا قتل واحد جماعة يقتل بهم يعني إذا حضر الأولياء وطلبوا وقال الإمام الشافعي رحمه الله تعالى : يقتل بالأول فقط . ولنا أنه لو قتل كل واحد بهم . منهم بوصف الكمال فيقتل بهم الحصول التماثل. وفي الحاوي: قتل رجلاً فقيل له لم قتلت فلاناً فقال قد كان ذلك كله مكتوباً في اللوح المحفوظ، ثم قال آخر لم قتلت غلامي فقال يقتل. وفي المحيط : وإذا قتل واحد رجلين يقتص بهما ولا يغرم الدية لأن بقتله صار كل واحد منهما مستوفياً حقه على الكمال لأن حق كل واحد منهما في عدم الحياة وبقتل الواحد حصل لهما إعدام الحياة معنى لما بينا. وإن حضر أحدهما والآخر غائب كان للحاصر أن يستوفي القصاص لأن كل واحد في إتلاف كل النفس واستيفاء البعض لمكان المزاحمة ولا مزاحمة هنا لأن حق الحاضر قد ظهر عند القاضي وحق الغائب لم يظهر وصار كأحد الشفيعين إذا حضر فقضى له بالجميع فكذا هذا ولو كان قطع اليدين لهما فقطع لأحدهما والمسألة بحالها فللآخر دية يده بخلاف القصاص بالنفس إذا قضى لأحدهما وقتله لم يجب للآخر شيء لأن فوات حقه في الاستيفاء يكون سبباً لقصور في المحل فإنهما إذا اجتمعا واستوفيا صار كل واحد منهما مستوفياً حقه على الكمال فلا تجب معه الدية، وإما في الطرف فوات حقه بسبب قصور في المحل لا يضر عن إيفاء حق كل واحد منهما فيجب الضمان . ولو عفا أحدهما قبل القضاء بالقصاص أو الدية بطل حقه واقتص للآخر لأن المزاحمة قد انقطعت بالعفو فبقي حق الآخر في الكل، وإن عفا بعد القضاء بالقصاص وصالح ولي المقتول فالدية بينهما، فلو قتل وقطع اليد من آخر وأخذ الدية فللساكت دية اليد عند محمد. وقالا : للساكت أن يقطع اليد على أن لهما حق استيفاء القصاص في يد واحدة واستيفاء دية واحدة ولا قصاص مع وجود الموافقة والملائمة وانعدام المنازعة والمشاجرة ولكنه أقصى ما يجب لهما وهو أن يجتمعا على القطع وأخذ الدية بينهما فصار الحال بعد القضاء كالحال قبله . ولو أخذ الدية عن اليد ثم عفا أحدهما يكون للآخر نصف الدية لأنهما لما قبضا الدية فقد ملكاها، ومن ضرورة ثبوت الملك في المستوفي أن لا يبقى الحق في اليد فسقط حق كل واحد منهما في نصف اليد كيلا يجتمع البدل والمبدل في ملك واحد فلا يتمكن من استيفاء كل اليد بدون نصيب العافي فبطل حقه في القصاص فامتنع القطع لأن من موجبه الدية في نصيبه كما إذا كان خطأ، ولو أخذ الدية كفيلاً ثم عفا أحدهما فللآخر القصاص لأن الكفالة توقيف . قال رحمه الله : (فإن حضر واحد قتل وسقط حق البقية كموت القاتل حتف أنفه لفوات محل الاستيفاء فصار كموت العبد الجاني وفيه خلاف الإمام الشافعي لأن الواجب عنده أحدهما على ما بينا، فإن فات أحدهما قضى الآخر لفوات المحل وقد قدمناه.
Book of Crimes, Chapter of Retaliation for Injuries Short of Homicide. And one person [is killed] for a group is sufficient. If one [heir] appears, he kills and the right of the rest falls. And the hand of two men is not cut for a hand, as a preference. ... He (the author) said: 'And one person for a group is sufficient' meaning if one person kills a group, he is killed for them, meaning if the heirs appear and demand. Imam al-Shafi'i said: He is killed only for the first. Our proof: If he killed each one of them completely, then he is killed for them to achieve equivalence. In al-Hawi: A man killed, and it was said to him 'Why did you kill so-and-so?' He replied 'All that was written in the Preserved Tablet.' Then another said 'Why did you kill my slave?' He replied 'He is killed.' In al-Muhit: If one kills two men, he is executed for both and does not owe blood money because by killing him each of them fully obtains his right, since each one's right is in removing life, and by killing the one, removal of life is achieved for both in meaning as we explained. If one heir is present and the other absent, the present one may execute the retaliation because each one is entitled to destroy the entire life, but partial execution is due to competition; here there is no competition because the right of the present one has appeared before the judge and the right of the absent one has not appeared, and it is like one of two co-shafis when he appears and is awarded the whole. Similarly this. And if he had cut off the hands of two and cut off for one, the other gets the blood money for his hand, unlike retaliation for life if he awards to one and kills him, nothing is due to the other because the loss of his right to execution is due to deficiency in the locus; when both gather and execute, each becomes fully satisfied, so no blood money is due. But in the limb, the loss of his right due to deficiency in the locus does not prevent fulfilling each one's right, so compensation is obligatory. And if one forgives before judgment of retaliation or blood money, his right becomes void and the other retaliates because competition has ended by forgiveness, so the other's right remains in the whole. If he forgives after judgment of retaliation and settles with the heir of the victim, the blood money is between them. If he killed and cut off the hand of another and took blood money, the silent one has the blood money of the hand according to Muhammad. They (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: The silent one may cut the hand, but both have the right to execute retaliation on one hand and take one blood money, and there is no retaliation with agreement and harmony and absence of dispute and quarrel, but the utmost due to them is that they gather on the cutting and take the blood money between them, so the situation after judgment is like before. And if he took the blood money for the hand then one forgives, the other has half the blood money because when they received the blood money they owned it, and from the necessity of establishing ownership in the received is that the right in the hand does not remain, so each one's right in half the hand falls so that the substitute and the substituted are not combined in one ownership; so he cannot execute the whole hand without the share of the one who forgave, so his right to retaliation becomes void, so cutting is prevented because its consequence is blood money in his share, as if it were accidental. And if he took the blood money as a surety then one forgives, the other has retaliation because suretyship is temporary. He (the author) said: If one appears, he kills and the right of the rest falls, like the death of the killer naturally, due to the loss of the locus of execution; it becomes like the death of the slave who perpetrated the crime, and there is a disagreement with Imam al-Shafi'i because according to him the obligation is one of two things as we explained; if one is lost, the other takes its place due to the loss of the locus, and we have already mentioned this.
Source pages p. 47

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq is a commentary on the matn of Kanz al-Daqaiq regarding the ruling that a single killer is executed for multiple victims. The passage begins with a refutation of an objection against the Hanafi position. Some had argued that the Quranic verse 'an-nafsu bin-nafs' (the soul for the soul) implies a one-to-one correspondence, so a single killer should only be executed for one victim. The author responds by analyzing the verse's intent, stating that it merely establishes the principle of equivalence of life for life, not that the killer's life is equal to only one victim's life. He further uses analogy with other Quranic verses like 'al-aynu bil-ayn' (eye for eye) which do not specify exact matching of right eye with right eye, etc. The matn then states 'Wal-fardu bil-jam'i iktifa' (one person is sufficient for a group), meaning if one person kills a group, he is executed for all of them when the heirs demand. The commentary explains the Hanafi view that each victim's right is to remove the killer's life, and by executing him once, all victims' rights are satisfied. Imam al-Shafi'i holds he is only executed for the first victim. The Hanafi proof relies on the concept that the killer killed each victim completely, so execution for all achieves equivalence. Further sub-rulings discuss scenarios where only some heirs are present or some forgive, detailing the distribution of blood money and rights to execution. The passage also includes an important distinction between cases of life and limb: for life, one execution satisfies all, but for limbs, if multiple victims have a right to the same limb, compensation may be due to the others. The commentary concludes by analogizing the absence of some heirs to the death of the killer, where the right falls due to loss of locus.

Key Terms
الفرد بالجمع اكتفاء (al-fardu bil-jam'i iktifa'): A maximal principle that a single killer is sufficiently punished by execution for a group of victims; one execution covers all.
المماثلة (al-mumathala): The equivalence required for qisas; in homicide, the killer's life must be equivalent to the victim's life in terms of sanctity, not number.
مزاحمة (muzahama): Competition between multiple claimants for the same right of execution; here, the right of each heir to execute the killer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi madhhab, if a single person kills a group, what is the ruling when the heirs of all victims demand qisas?
A) The killer is executed only for the first victim.
B) The killer is executed for all victims, and this suffices.
C) The killer is executed for each victim separately (multiple executions).
D) The killer pays blood money for all victims.

Key Takeaway
One execution of a single killer suffices for all victims, because the killer's life is forfeit for each victim's right to life.

No Qisas for Two Offenders in a Single Hand Cutting
Commentary on the ruling that no qisas applies when two cut one hand

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when two men cut one hand and explain the proof against qisas.

Core Idea
No qisas when two cut one hand because the hand cannot be divided.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq clarifies a specific qisas scenario: two offenders cut off a single hand. The Hanafi school rules that neither loses his hand, contrary to the Shafi'i analogy with homicide. We will examine the textual basis, the reasoning, and the practical consequence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act is two men cutting one person's hand. The ruling stated is that neither man's hand is cut (no qisas). This is the mufta bihi Hanafi position.
2
Note the opposing view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that both should lose their hands, analogizing to homicide where two killers are both executed.
Shafi'i uses the principle 'al-atraf tabi'ah lil-anfus'.
3
Analyze the Hanafi proof
The Hanafi proof: qisas requires equivalence; a hand is indivisible, so each offender only partially contributed and full qisas cannot be applied. The analogy to homicide is rejected because life is indivisible whereas limbs are not.
The text distinguishes two factual scenarios: joint action with one knife vs. separate knives meeting in the middle.
4
Identify the practical consequence
Under Hanafi, neither loses a hand; they must pay diyah (blood money). Under Shafi'i, both lose a hand. This is the thamarah al-khilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (ولا يقطع يد رجلين بيد معناه إذا قطع رجلان يد رجل فلا قصاص على واحد منهما. وقال الإمام الشافعي: تقطع أيديهما ومحل الخلاف فيما أخذ سكيناً واحداً من جانب وأمراها على يده حتى انقطعت هو يعتبرها بالأنفس لأن الأطراف تابعة لها وملحقة بها فأخذت حكمها بخلاف ما إذا أمر أحدهما السكين من جانب والآخر من جانب حتى التقت السكينان في الوسط وبانت اليد حيث لا يجب القصاص فيه على واحد منهما لأنه لم يوجد من كل واحد منهما إمرار السلاح على بعض العضو. ولنا أن كل واحد منهما قاطع للبعض لأن ما أثم
He (the author) said: 'And the hand of two men is not cut for a hand' meaning if two men cut the hand of a man, there is no qisas upon either of them. Imam al-Shafi'i said: Their hands are cut. The locus of disagreement is when they took one knife from one side and passed it over his hand until it was cut off; he (al-Shafi'i) analogizes it to homicides because limbs are dependent upon and annexed to lives, so they take their ruling, unlike if one passed the knife from one side and the other from the other side until the two knives met in the middle and the hand separated, where qisas is not obligatory upon either one because from each one there was not passing the blade over some part of the organ. Our proof: Each one of them is a cutter of part, because what ...
Source pages p. 48

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq addresses the ruling for qisas in injuries: when two people cut off one person's hand, neither is subject to qisas (their hands are not cut). The commentary explains the matn from Kanz al-Daqaiq. There is a disagreement with Imam al-Shafi'i, who holds that both should have their hands cut (qisas). The Hanafi position distinguishes between two scenarios: (1) if both acted together using a single knife from one side to cut the hand, then the Shafi'i analogy to homicide is rejected because limbs are not equivalent to life in divisibility; (2) if each used his own knife from opposite sides meeting in the middle, then clearly no qisas because each only partially cut. The Hanafi proof is that each is a cutter of part, but the hand is one organ, so qisas cannot be divided. The text is cut off, but the argument is that since qisas requires perfect equivalence and the hand cannot be split, neither can have their hand cut.

Key Terms
يد رجلين بيد (yadu rajulayni bi-yad): Ruling that two men's hands are not cut off for the single hand they cut off.
الأطراف تابعة للأنفس (al-atraf tabi'ah lil-anfus): Limbs are dependent on lives; Shafi'i uses this to analogize, Hanafi rejects it for qisas in joints.
قصاص (qisas): Retaliation punishment for homicide or bodily injury; here for cutting a hand.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi madhhab, if two people together cut off one person's hand, what is the ruling?
A) Each of the two has his hand cut off.
B) Neither loses his hand; they pay blood money.
C) Only one loses his hand, chosen by lottery.
D) The victim chooses which offender's hand to cut.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that qisas in limbs cannot be divided, so when multiple offenders cut one hand, none suffers amputation; diyah is the remedy.

Equality in Limb Qisas: Two Offenders and One Hand
Explains why qisas for limbs requires equality in benefit and value, and rules for two offenders

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Hanafi fiqh requires equality in benefit and value for limb qisas, and apply the ruling to multiple offenders.

Core Idea
Limb qisas requires equality in benefit and value; multiple offenders for one limb cannot be retaliated.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra’iq clarifies a key difference between qisas for life and for limbs. For life, only equality in protection (isma) is needed; for limbs, equality in benefit and value is required. This directly affects the ruling when two or more offenders cut a single limb: they cannot all be subjected to qisas but instead pay diya.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core distinction
Recognize that the passage distinguishes between qisas for life and qisas for limbs. For life, equality in protection is sufficient; for limbs, equality in benefit and value is required.
This is the foundational principle of the ruling.
2
Locate the condition of musāwāh
Find where the author states that for limbs, musāwāh (equality) is considered in manfa‘a (benefit) and qīma (value). This is why a healthy hand is not cut for a paralyzed one.
The term musāwāh appears in the text in connection with the impossibility of cutting 'the whole for the part'.
3
Understand the proof: divisibility of limbs
Examine the author’s reasoning: limb cutting is divisible – you can cut part and leave the rest – whereas the soul is indivisible. Hence, for homicide, two can be killed for one; for limbs, two cannot be retaliated for one.
Compare the author's mention of the knife on nape and throat example for homicide.
4
Apply to two offenders
Apply the principle to the case of two men cutting one hand: qisas is not possible because equality in cutting cannot be achieved – each would need to lose a hand but only one hand was cut. Instead, diya is wajib on both.
The text explicitly says 'no qisas on them, and diya is due from them.'
5
Generalize to multiple offenders
Note that the ruling is not restricted to two offenders; any number of offenders share the diya without qisas. The phrase 'two men' is an example.
The author cites al-Tajrid to confirm that the same ruling applies for any number.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فلا انقطع بقوة أحدهما أن يقطع بقوة الآخر فلا يجوز أن يقطع الكل بالبعض والأثنين بالواحد لانعدام المساواة فصار كما إذا أمرها كل واحد من جانب الآخر بخلاف النفس فإن شرط فيه المساواة في العصمة لا غير وفي الطرق يعتبر المساواة في النفع والقيمة ولهذا لا تقطع الصحيحة بالشلاء النفس السالمة من العيوب تقتل بالمفلوج والمسلول، وكذا الاثنان بالواحد يصح القياس على النفس، ولأن زهوق الروح لا يتجزئ فأضيف إلى كل واحد كلاً وقطع العضو يتجزئ ألا ترى أنه يمكن أن يقطع البعض ويترك الباقي، وفي القتل لا يمكن ذلك ولهذا لو أمر أحدهما السكين على قفاه والآخر على حلقه حتى التقتا في الوسط ومات منهما يجب القصاص وفي اليد لا يجب، ولأن القتل بطريق الاجماع غالب مخالفة الغوث لا في القطع لأنه يحتاج إلى مقدمات بطيئة فيلحقه الغوث بسببها كالنداء ونقول ثبت وجوب القصاص في النفس والاجتماع على خلاف القياس والطرف ليس مثلها فلا يحلق بها. وقوله رجلان مثال وليس بقيد قال في التجريد : إذا قطع رجلان يدي رجل فلا قصاص عليهما وعليهما الدية، وكذا ما زاد على هذا العدد في هذا الحكم سواء.
So if the force of one is broken for cutting with the force of another, it is not permissible to cut the whole for the part, nor two for one due to lack of equality. It becomes as if each one commanded from the other's side, unlike the soul, for equality in protection alone is required there, while in limbs equality in benefit and value is considered. For this reason, a healthy (hand) is not cut for a paralyzed one, but a soul free from defects is killed for a paralyzed and consumptive one. Likewise, two for one is valid by analogy to the soul. Because the departure of the soul is indivisible, so it is attributed to each one wholly, while cutting a limb is divisible; do you not see that it is possible to cut part and leave the rest? In killing, this is not possible. For this reason, if one placed the knife on his nape and the other on his throat until they met in the middle and he died from both, qisas is obligatory, but in a hand it is not obligatory. And because killing by consensus is usually contrary to rescue, unlike cutting because it requires slow preliminaries, so rescue overtakes due to them, like calling out. And we say: the obligation of qisas in homicide and assembly is established contrary to analogy, and a limb is not like it, so it is not annexed to it. His saying 'two men' is an example, not a restriction. In al-Tajrid: if two men cut off a man's hand, there is no qisas on them, and diya is due from them. Likewise, any number beyond this in this ruling is equal.
Source pages p. 49

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof explaining the principle of equality (musawa) in qisas for limbs. The author distinguishes between qisas for life and qisas for limbs. For life, the only condition for equality is that both parties are protected (ma‘sum) — thus a healthy person can be killed for a disabled one, and two can be killed for one because the soul is indivisible. For limbs, equality in benefit and value (manfa‘a wa qima) is required; hence a healthy hand is not cut for a paralyzed one, and two cannot be retaliated against for cutting one hand. The proof is that limb cutting is divisible — one could cut part and leave the rest — unlike homicide. This is supported by analogy and the impossibility of rescue in sudden killing versus limb cutting. The author then clarifies that the ruling is not restricted to two offenders; any number of offenders share the diya without qisas.

Key Terms
مساواة (musāwāh): Equality in benefit and value required for limb qisas, unlike life where only equality in protection is needed.
قصاص (qiṣāṣ): Retaliation in kind for intentional injury to a limb or life.
دية (diya): Financial compensation for injury or homicide when qisas is not applicable.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why can two people not be subjected to qisas for cutting one man's hand in the Hanafi school?
A) Because the hand cannot be divided equally between them
B) Because the victim is not protected
C) Because the cutting is considered one act
D) Because the two offenders are not equal in strength

Key Takeaway
For limb qisas, equality in benefit and value is essential; due to divisibility, multiple offenders for one limb incur diya, not qisas.

Successive Cuts and Healing: When Does Qisas Apply?
Rulings on qisas when cuts are made sequentially with intervals of healing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the Hanafi positions on qisas for successive cuts with healing and apply the principle of equality at the time of each injury.

Core Idea
Healing between cuts can break equality, leading to compensation instead of qisas.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explores a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute: what happens when someone repeatedly cuts a limb, with healing in between? The key variable is whether the victim's limb remains equal to the cutter's after each act. Understanding this helps you see how qisas is not a blanket rule but balanced with compensation (arsh or hukuma) when equality is lost.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main scenario
Read the first scenario: a man cuts the upper joint of a finger, it heals, then he cuts the second joint. Focus on how Muhammad (in al-Ziyadat) rules: the cutter's finger is cut from the lower joint, treating both cuts as one.
Note the assumption: no qisas was already executed for the first cut.
2
Trace the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Identify that some mashayikh attribute this view to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the two), whereas others say it is the position of all, including Abu Hanifa. Then note Abu Hanifa's alternative: the victim may cut only the upper joint.
This difference arises from whether healing breaks the unity of the act.
3
Analyze the condition of equality
The principle is that qisas requires equality (musawat) at the time of retaliation. After a cut heals, the victim's limb may be deficient (e.g., missing a joint), making the cutter's intact limb not equal. Explain how this leads to compensation instead.
Consider the distinction between a healed cut and a cut that has not healed.
4
Apply to subsequent scenarios
Work through the cases: cutting half a joint with healing, cutting fingers then palm, cutting glans then remainder. For each, determine whether qisas or compensation applies based on presence or absence of healing interval.
Healing after the first cut creates a deficiency in the victim's limb.
5
Evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf
State the practical consequence: whether the cutter loses a finger from the lower joint or only the upper joint, and whether qisas is possible for later cuts. The relied-upon view (mufta bihi) is that if healing intervenes, qisas is possible only if equality remains; otherwise compensation.
The tarjih leans toward the view of the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) as it is more practical.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال محمد رحمه الله في الزيادات : رجل قطع المفصل الأعلى من أصبع رجل وبرأ منه ثم عاد وقطع الثاني أيضاً ثم اختصما إلى القاضي فالقاضي يقضي على القاطع بالقصاص في المفصل الثاني. هذا الذي ذكرنا إذا قطع المفصل الأعلى وبرئ ثم عاد وقطع المفصل الثاني فإنه يقطع أصبع القاطع من المفصل الأسفل ويجعل كأنه قطع المفصلين بدفعة واحدة، فمن مشايخنا من قال ما ذكر ههنا قولهما، أما على قول أبي حنيفة رحمه الله للمقطوع مفصلاه أن يقطع المفصل الأعلى ثم قال هذا قول الكل، ولو قطع المفصل الأعلى واقتص من القاطع ثم وقطع المفصل الثاني وبرئ يجب لوجود المساواة، فرق بين . هذا وبين ر رجلين مقطوعي الأصابع قطع أحدهما كف صاحبه لا يقطع كف القاطع. أقول : فيه نظر لأن المساواة ممكنة فينبغي يقطع لإمكانها فتدبره، وكذا إذا كان مقطوع الكف قطع أحدهما زند صاحبه لا يقطع زند القاطع. ولو قطع من أصبع رجل نصف مفصل وكسر وبرئ ثم قطع ما بقي من المفصل وبرئ فلا قصاص عليه في شيء من ذلك، أما في النصف الأول فلحلول الجناية في العظم، وأما في النصف الثاني فلعدم المساواة لأن أصبع القاطع حال ما قطع الثاني من المفصل صحيحة والأصبع المقطوعة من نصف المفصل ناقصة ولو لم يحل بينهما برئ يجب القصاص في المفصل وجعل كأنه قطع المفصل بدفعه واحدة وكذلك لو قطع الأصابع من رجل وعاد وقطع الكف إن لم يحل بينهما برء يجب القصاص في يد كأنه قطع الكل دفعة واحدة وإن حال بينهما برء يجب القصاص في الأصابع وحكومة عدل في الكف، وكذا إذا قطع حشفة إنسان ثم عاد وقطع باقي الذكر إن كان قبل تخلل البرء تجب دية واحدة، وإن كان تخلل بينهما برء يجب كمال الدية في الحشفة وحكومة عدل في الباقي. ولو قطع المفصل الأعلى من أصبع رجل فقبل البرء قطع النصف من المفصل الثاني ثم برئ القصاص وجعل كأنه من الابتداء قطع النصف من المفصل الثاني وهناك لا يجب القصاص بل يجب الأرش فهذا ذلك، ولو برأ من القطع الأول ثم قطع النصف من المفصل الثاني يجب القصاص في المفصل الأعلى لوجود الشرط ويجب نصف الأرش في الثاني.
Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him) said in al-Ziyadat: A man cut the upper joint of another man's finger, and it healed, then he again cut the second joint, then both came to the judge. The judge rules qisas on the cutter for the second joint. In what we have mentioned, if he cut the upper joint and it healed, then again cut the second joint, then he cuts the cutter's finger from the lower joint and treats it as if he cut both joints at once. Some of our mashayikh said what is mentioned here is the position of the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). As for the position of Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him): the one whose two joints were cut may cut the upper joint. Then he (Muhammad) said: this is the position of all. If he cut the upper joint and qisas was executed on the cutter, then he cut the second joint and it healed, qisas is wajib due to the existence of equality. A distinction is made between this and two men with missing fingers: if one cuts the palm of the other, the cutter's palm is not cut. I say: there is consideration because equality is possible, so it should be cut due to possibility, so ponder this. Likewise, if a person with a missing hand cuts the forearm of another, the cutter's forearm is not cut. If a man cuts half a joint of another's finger, breaks it, and it heals, then cuts the remainder of the joint and it heals, there is no qisas on him for any of that. As for the first half, because the injury enters the bone; as for the second half, due to lack of equality because at the time of cutting the second joint, the cutter's finger is healthy while the cut finger is deficient from half a joint. If healing did not intervene between them, qisas is wajib for the joint and it is treated as if he cut the joint at once. Similarly, if he cut fingers of a man and then cut the palm, if healing did not intervene between them, qisas is wajib for the hand as if he cut the whole at once; if healing intervened, qisas is wajib for the fingers and a just compensation (hukuma) for the palm. Likewise, if he cuts a man's glans then cuts the remainder of the penis, if before healing, one diya is due; if healing intervened, complete diya for the glans and hukuma for the remainder. If he cut the upper joint of a man's finger, and before healing cut half of the second joint, then it healed, qisas is due and it is treated as if from the beginning he cut half of the second joint, and there no qisas is due but only arsh; so this is similar. If he healed from the first cut then cut half of the second joint, qisas is wajib for the upper joint due to the existence of the condition, and half arsh is due for the second.
Source pages p. 49

Commentary
This passage presents intra-Hanafi disputes regarding successive cuts on the same limb with intervals of healing. Imam Muhammad in al-Ziyadat rules that if the upper joint of a finger is cut and heals, then the second joint is cut, the cutter's finger is cut from the lower joint — treating both cuts as one. Some mashayikh attribute this to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the two), while others say it is the position of all, including Abu Hanifa. However, a distinction is made if the cutter had already been retaliated upon for the first cut: then if the second cut occurs after healing, qisas is possible because equality exists (the victim's remaining part is now comparable). The passage then discusses various scenarios: cutting a healthy hand when the cutter has a missing hand, cutting half a joint, cutting fingers then palm, and cutting the glans then remainder. In each case, if healing intervenes, the later injury may not allow full qisas due to deficiency of the victim's limb. The principle is that qisas requires equality at the time of each cut; if healing makes the victim's limb deficient (due to prior loss), qisas is not possible, and compensation (arsh/hukuma) is due instead.

Key Terms
برء (bur'): Healing of a wound after an injury, which may change the status of the limb for future qisas.
حكومة عدل (ḥukūmat 'adl): A fair monetary compensation assessed by a judge for injuries where no fixed arsh is prescribed.
أرش (arsh): Compensation for a specific injury, often a fixed portion of diya.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person cuts the upper joint of someone's finger, it heals, then he cuts the second joint, what is the ruling according to Muhammad in al-Ziyadat?
A) The cutter's finger is cut from the lower joint as if both cuts were one
B) No qisas because of healing
C) The cutter's upper joint is cut only
D) Full diya is due

Key Takeaway
Healing between successive cuts can break equality, leading to compensation instead of qisas, unless the cutter's limb has also been reduced by prior qisas, restoring equality.

Multiple Offenders and the Status of the Victim in Homicide Rulings
Rulings on multiple offenders causing death and special cases involving apostates and dar al-harb.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on liability when multiple offenders cause death, and apply the rule of direct causation to scenarios involving apostasy and joining dar al-harb.

Core Idea
Liability for death follows the direct cause; the victim's status at injury determines qisas or diya.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses complex homicide scenarios. It demonstrates the Hanafi principle that when multiple injuries lead to death, only the injury that is the direct cause of death triggers qisas for life, while other injuries warrant diya for the limb. The passage also examines cases where the victim is an apostate or joins dar al-harb, showing that the protected status of the victim at the time of injury is critical. These examples sharpen our understanding of causation and liability in Islamic criminal law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key scenarios
The passage presents several scenarios: multiple offenders cutting limbs (hand then elbow, finger then hand), causing paralysis, and apostate/victim status changes. Break down each scenario into the acts and their nature (intentional/accidental).
Focus on the sequence of acts and the victim's status at each point.
2
Determine causal link to death
In each multiple-offender case, identify which act directly caused the death. In the hand/elbow case, the elbow cut is the direct cause; in the finger/hand case, the intentional finger cut is direct. The direct intentional act that leads to death is treated as homicide.
Consider the principle of direct causation.
3
Apply the ruling: qisas vs diya
The Hanafi school rules that the person whose direct intentional act causes death faces qisas; others pay diya for their respective injuries. If the act is accidental, diya is on the 'aqila.
Note the difference from Zufar who imposes diya of life on both in some cases.
4
Examine apostate and dar al-harb cases
If the victim was an apostate at the time of injury, no liability for his later death. If he was a Muslim when injured, then apostatized and died, only diya of the limb is due. If he returned to Islam and died, Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold diya of life; Muhammad holds diya of hand. Similarly for joining dar al-harb.
Key: the victim's protected status at the time of injury governs the liability, not at death.
5
Compare and contrast the ikhtilaf
Zufar's view makes both offenders equally liable for diya of life in certain cases. Abu Yusuf differs from Abu Hanifa in the accidental finger/intentional hand case. Identify the thamarah al-khilaf: whether qisas is applicable or only diya.
The relied-upon position is that of the three (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) as stated in the text.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي الظهيرية : ولو قطع آخر كفه ثم قطع آخر مرفقه فمات، فإن كان عمداً فقصاص النفس على الثاني ودية القاطع على الأول وهذا قول علمائنا الثلاثة وقال زفر : إن كان عمداً وإن كان خطأ ولم يتخلل البرء فدية النفس عليهما. وإن قطع أصبع رجل عمداً ثم قطع آخر كفه خطأ فمات يقتص من قاطع الأصبع وعلى عاقلة الآخر. دية النفس وقال :زفر لا يقتص ولكل واحد منهما نصف الدية وإذا ضرب رجل على يد رجل فشلت اليد فعليه دية كاملة وفي النوازل: وسئل شداد عن رجل قطع رأس أصبع رجل من مفصله قال : يقتص منه فإن اقتص منه ثم قطع أحدهما يد صاحبه فقال ليس بينهما قصاص. وفي العيون رجل قطع أصبع رجل خطأ فجاء آخر وقطع كفه عمداً فمات منها جميعاً في قول الإمام لا يجب القصاص وعلى كل واحد منهما نصف الدية وبه قال الإمام الشافعي رحمه الله تعالى : وقال أبو يوسف رحمه الله : يقطع من الكف وعلى عاقلة الذي قطع الأصبع دية الأصبع. وفي شرح الطحاوي ومن قطع يد مرتد فأسلم فمات فلا شيء على القاطع. ولو قطع يده وهو مسلم فارتد فمات فعليه دية اليد لا غير، ولو رجع إلى الإسلام ثم مات فعلى قول أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف عليه دية النفس، وفي قول محمد عليه دية اليد. وكذلك لو لحق بدار الحرب ولم يقض القاضي بلحوقه ثم عاد مسلماً فمات تجب دية اليد لا غير.
In al-Zahiriyya: If one cuts his hand, then another cuts his elbow, and he dies: if it was intentional, qisas of life is on the second, and diya of the cutter (hand) is on the first — this is the statement of our three scholars. Zufar said: if it was intentional, and if it was accidental and healing did not intervene, then diya of life is on both. If a man cut another's finger intentionally, then another cut his hand accidentally, and he died: qisas is executed from the finger-cutter, and diya of life is on the 'aqila of the other. Zufar said: no qisas, and each owes half diya. If a man strikes another's hand making it paralyzed, full diya is due. In al-Nawazil: Shaddad was asked about a man who cut off the tip of another's finger from its joint; he said: qisas is taken from him. If qisas was taken from him, then one of them cuts the other's hand, he said: there is no qisas between them. In al-'Uyun: a man cut another's finger accidentally, then another came and cut his hand intentionally, and he died from both; according to the Imam (Abu Hanifa), qisas is not obligatory, and each owes half diya — Imam al-Shafi'i (may Allah have mercy on him) also said this. Abu Yusuf said: qisas is taken from the hand-cutter, and the 'aqila of the finger-cutter owes diya of the finger. In Sharh al-Tahawi: if one cuts the hand of an apostate, then the apostate becomes Muslim and dies, there is nothing on the cutter. If he cut his hand while he was Muslim, then he apostatized and died, then only diya of the hand is due. If he returned to Islam and then died, according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, diya of life is due; according to Muhammad, diya of the hand. Similarly, if he joined dar al-harb and the judge did not pronounce his joining, then he returned as a Muslim and died, diya of the hand only is due.
Source pages p. 50

Commentary
This passage presents several rulings on complex cases involving multiple offenders causing death, and on the status of apostates. The first case: two offenders — one cuts the hand, another cuts the elbow, and the victim dies. The Hanafi consensus (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) is that if both acts are intentional, the elbow-cutter (whose direct act caused death) is subject to qisas for life, while the hand-cutter owes diya for the hand. Zufar disagrees, making them both liable for diya of life if accidental and no healing. The second case: intentional finger cut and accidental hand cut leading to death — the finger-cutter faces qisas (since his act was intentional and directly led to death?), but Abu Yusuf's view (in al-'Uyun) is that the hand-cutter faces qisas for the hand, and the finger-cutter's 'aqila pays diya for the finger. The third case: paralysis of hand — full diya due. The fourth case: tip of finger — qisas is taken, but after execution, if one cuts the other's hand, no qisas (due to prior injury?). The fifth case: apostate — if the victim was an apostate at the time of cutting, no liability if he later dies. If he was Muslim when cut but apostatized before death, only diya for the hand is due. If he returned to Islam and then died, Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold that diya of life is due (since he died as a Muslim), while Muhammad holds diya of hand only. The same applies if he joined dar al-harb and returned.

Key Terms
مرتد (murtadd): An apostate from Islam, whose blood may not be protected depending on the ruling.
دار الحرب (dār al-ḥarb): Territory of war; joining it may affect one's protected status.
قصاص (qiṣāṣ): Retaliatory punishment for intentional homicide or bodily harm, equivalent to the injury inflicted.
دية (diya): Monetary compensation paid to the victim's heirs for homicide or bodily harm.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person cuts the hand of an apostate, then the apostate becomes Muslim and later dies from the wound, what is the ruling according to the text?
A) Qisas of life on the cutter
B) Diya of the hand only
C) Nothing on the cutter
D) Diya of life on the cutter

Key Takeaway
In homicide by multiple offenders, liability for qisas falls on the one whose deliberate act directly caused death; for apostate victims, liability is determined by their protected status at the time of the injury.

Conditions for Qisas on Limbs in Hanafi Fiqh
Conditions for qisas between different categories of persons

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for qisas on limbs and identify when qisas is not applicable.

Core Idea
Qisas requires equality in freedom, religion, and gender; otherwise only diya.

This passage from Sharh al-Tahawi outlines the conditions under which qisas (retaliatory amputation) is obligatory for intentional limb cutting. Understanding these conditions is crucial because many cases involve mixed categories where qisas is impossible and only financial compensation applies.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is intentional cutting of a limb. The ruling is qisas, but deferred until after the wound has healed to ensure proportionality.
2
List the conditions for qisas
Equality in freedom (both free or both slave), religion (both Muslim, both Kitabi, or one Muslim one Kitabi), and gender (both male or both female).
Kitabi refers to Jews and Christians (People of the Book).
3
Determine when qisas is not applicable
If any condition is not met—e.g., free vs slave, male vs female—qisas is not possible. Instead, diya is due immediately from the offender's property.
'Halān' means immediately, without deferment.
4
Note the consequence of non-application
When qisas falls, the obligation shifts to financial compensation (diya), which is wajib on the offender's property at once.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي شرح الطحاوي : ومن قطع من رجل يداً أو رجلاً أو أصبعاً أو نملة من أصبع أو ما سوى ذلك مفصلاً من المفصل عمداً فعليه القصاص بعد البرء من الجناية ولا قصاص عليه قبل ذلك، وإذا قطع رجل يد آخر عمداً فإن كان القاطع والمقطوع حرين مسلمين أو كتابيين أو أحدهما مسلم والآخر كتابي يجري القصاص بينهما أو كانا امرأتين حرتين مسلمتين أو أحدهما مسلمة والأخرى كتابية أو كانتا ذميتين يجب القصاص. ولو كانا عبدين أو أحدهما عبد والآخر حر أو أحدهما ذكر والآخر أنثى فلا قصاص بينهما والأرض في ماله حالاً. وهذا كله بيان حكم العمد . رجعنا إلى بيان حكم الخطأ فنقول وبالله التوفيق : اليدين إذا قطعتا خطأ الدية لفوات جنس المنفعة على الكمال وفي أحدهما نصف الدية ولا تفضل اليمن على الشمال وإن كانت اليمين أكثر بطشاً من الشمال لأن العبرة في الجنايات لجنس المنفعة لا للزيادة، وفي اليد إذا قطعت من نصف الساعد دية اليد وحكومة عدل فيما وراء الكف وهو قول الحنفي والشافعي ؛ روى صاحب الأمالي عن أبي يوسف أنه لا يجب في الساعد شيء وهو قول زفر ومالك وسفيان والثوري، وكذلك على هذا الاختلاف إذا قطع اليد من المرفق أو المنكب فإنه يجب في الكف دية
In Sharh al-Tahawi: Whoever cuts a hand, foot, finger, or a segment of a finger, or any other joint from a joint intentionally, qisas is upon him after healing from the injury, but no qisas before that. When a man cuts another's hand intentionally, if the cutter and the victim are both free, both Muslim or both Kitabi, or one Muslim and the other Kitabi, qisas is executed between them. Or if both are free Muslim women, or one Muslim woman and the other Kitabi woman, or both dhimmis, qisas is obligatory. If both are slaves, or one slave and the other free, or one male and the other female, then no qisas between them, and compensation is due from his property immediately. This is all the ruling of intentional injury. We return to the ruling of error: we say, and with Allah is success: if both hands are cut in error, full diya is due for loss of the entire type of benefit; for one hand, half diya. The right hand is not preferred over the left, even if the right is more powerful, because consideration in injuries is for the type of benefit, not for excess. If a hand is cut from the middle of the forearm, diya of the hand is due plus a just compensation for what is beyond the hand. This is the statement of the Hanafi and Shafi'i. The author of al-Amali narrated from Abu Yusuf that nothing is due for the forearm — this is the statement of Zufar, Malik, Sufyan al-Thawri. Likewise, based on this difference, if the hand is cut from the elbow or shoulder, diya for the hand is due.
Source pages p. 50

Commentary
This passage covers the conditions for qisas on limbs and the diya for hands cut in error. It states that qisas for intentional limb cutting is only applicable after the wound has healed (to ensure equality and avoid further injury). The conditions for qisas are equality in freedom (both free or both slave), religion (both Muslim, both Kitabi, or one Muslim one Kitabi), and gender (both male or both female; but if one male and one female, no qisas). For mixed categories like free and slave, or male and female, no qisas is possible; only financial compensation is due immediately from the offender's property. The text then shifts to accidental (khata') cutting of hands: full diya for both hands (10,000 dirhams or 1000 dinars?), half for one. There is no distinction between right and left hand in diya, because the criterion is the type of benefit (jins al-manfa'a), not increased strength. The description then discusses where the cut occurs: if from the mid-forearm, diya for the hand plus hukuma for the extra part (forearm). This is the Hanafi and Shafi'i view. Abu Yusuf, however, reported that nothing is due for the forearm (i.e., only diya for the hand, no extra for forearm), which is also the view of Zufar, Malik, Sufyan al-Thawri. The same difference applies if the cut is at the elbow or shoulder.

Key Terms
قصاص (qisas): Retaliatory punishment equal to the injury inflicted.
دية (diya): Financial compensation paid for injury or homicide when qisas is not applicable.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a free Muslim man cuts the hand of a free Muslim woman intentionally and the wound has healed, what is the ruling?
A) Qisas by cutting the man's hand
B) Diya only
C) Both qisas and diya
D) No penalty because she is a woman

Key Takeaway
Qisas requires complete equality between cutter and victim; otherwise only financial compensation is due.

Qisas — Retaliation
intermediate

Diya for Hands and the Forearm Dispute in Hanafi Fiqh
Diya for hands in accidental injury and the dispute on forearm compensation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the diya for hands in accidental injury and identify the intra-madhhab dispute regarding compensation for the forearm.

Core Idea
The right and left hand have equal diya; the forearm requires additional hukuma according to the majority Hanafi view.

After covering intentional injury, the passage turns to accidental (khata') cutting of hands. It establishes the principle that diya is based on the type of benefit (jins al-manfa'a), not on functional superiority, so right and left hands have equal diya. A key dispute arises when the cut extends beyond the hand to the forearm: the majority Hanafi (and Shafi'i) rule that diya for the hand plus a fair compensation (hukuma) for the forearm is due, while Abu Yusuf and others hold that nothing extra is owed. This lesson unpacks that ruling and its underlying reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling for accidental cutting of hands
For both hands cut accidentally, full diya is due. For one hand, half diya. No distinction between right and left regardless of strength.
The diya for a hand is 5,000 dirhams (half of full diya for a person).
2
Understand the rationale: jins al-manfa'a
The criterion is the type of benefit (e.g., grasping), not the degree of function. The right hand may be stronger, but both share the same type of benefit, so diya is equal.
This principle prevents subjective assessments of value.
3
Examine the dispute on forearm cutting
If the cut is from the middle of the forearm, the hand diya is due, plus a hukuma (just compensation) for the forearm part. This is the view of the majority Hanafis (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) and Shafi'i.
4
Contrast the opposing position
Abu Yusuf, Zufar, Malik, and Sufyan al-Thawri hold that only the hand diya is due, and nothing extra for the forearm. They consider the forearm as part of the hand for compensation.
The same dispute applies if cut from elbow or shoulder.
5
Identify the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
The difference is whether additional financial compensation (hukuma) is paid for the forearm portion or not. The mufta bihi (relied-upon) view in the Hanafi school is the majority view with hukuma.
The passage mentions that the author of al-Amali narrated Abu Yusuf's view, but the text likely favors the majority.

Source Text

وفي شرح الطحاوي : ومن قطع من رجل يداً أو رجلاً أو أصبعاً أو نملة من أصبع أو ما سوى ذلك مفصلاً من المفصل عمداً فعليه القصاص بعد البرء من الجناية ولا قصاص عليه قبل ذلك، وإذا قطع رجل يد آخر عمداً فإن كان القاطع والمقطوع حرين مسلمين أو كتابيين أو أحدهما مسلم والآخر كتابي يجري القصاص بينهما أو كانا امرأتين حرتين مسلمتين أو أحدهما مسلمة والأخرى كتابية أو كانتا ذميتين يجب القصاص. ولو كانا عبدين أو أحدهما عبد والآخر حر أو أحدهما ذكر والآخر أنثى فلا قصاص بينهما والأرض في ماله حالاً. وهذا كله بيان حكم العمد . رجعنا إلى بيان حكم الخطأ فنقول وبالله التوفيق : اليدين إذا قطعتا خطأ الدية لفوات جنس المنفعة على الكمال وفي أحدهما نصف الدية ولا تفضل اليمن على الشمال وإن كانت اليمين أكثر بطشاً من الشمال لأن العبرة في الجنايات لجنس المنفعة لا للزيادة، وفي اليد إذا قطعت من نصف الساعد دية اليد وحكومة عدل فيما وراء الكف وهو قول الحنفي والشافعي ؛ روى صاحب الأمالي عن أبي يوسف أنه لا يجب في الساعد شيء وهو قول زفر ومالك وسفيان والثوري، وكذلك على هذا الاختلاف إذا قطع اليد من المرفق أو المنكب فإنه يجب في الكف دية
In Sharh al-Tahawi: Whoever cuts a hand, foot, finger, or a segment of a finger, or any other joint from a joint intentionally, qisas is upon him after healing from the injury, but no qisas before that. When a man cuts another's hand intentionally, if the cutter and the victim are both free, both Muslim or both Kitabi, or one Muslim and the other Kitabi, qisas is executed between them. Or if both are free Muslim women, or one Muslim woman and the other Kitabi woman, or both dhimmis, qisas is obligatory. If both are slaves, or one slave and the other free, or one male and the other female, then no qisas between them, and compensation is due from his property immediately. This is all the ruling of intentional injury. We return to the ruling of error: we say, and with Allah is success: if both hands are cut in error, full diya is due for loss of the entire type of benefit; for one hand, half diya. The right hand is not preferred over the left, even if the right is more powerful, because consideration in injuries is for the type of benefit, not for excess. If a hand is cut from the middle of the forearm, diya of the hand is due plus a just compensation for what is beyond the hand. This is the statement of the Hanafi and Shafi'i. The author of al-Amali narrated from Abu Yusuf that nothing is due for the forearm — this is the statement of Zufar, Malik, Sufyan al-Thawri. Likewise, based on this difference, if the hand is cut from the elbow or shoulder, diya for the hand is due.
Source pages p. 50

Commentary
This passage covers the conditions for qisas on limbs and the diya for hands cut in error. It states that qisas for intentional limb cutting is only applicable after the wound has healed (to ensure equality and avoid further injury). The conditions for qisas are equality in freedom (both free or both slave), religion (both Muslim, both Kitabi, or one Muslim one Kitabi), and gender (both male or both female; but if one male and one female, no qisas). For mixed categories like free and slave, or male and female, no qisas is possible; only financial compensation is due immediately from the offender's property. The text then shifts to accidental (khata') cutting of hands: full diya for both hands (10,000 dirhams or 1000 dinars?), half for one. There is no distinction between right and left hand in diya, because the criterion is the type of benefit (jins al-manfa'a), not increased strength. The description then discusses where the cut occurs: if from the mid-forearm, diya for the hand plus hukuma for the extra part (forearm). This is the Hanafi and Shafi'i view. Abu Yusuf, however, reported that nothing is due for the forearm (i.e., only diya for the hand, no extra for forearm), which is also the view of Zufar, Malik, Sufyan al-Thawri. The same difference applies if the cut is at the elbow or shoulder.

Key Terms
جنس المنفعة (jins al-manfa'a): The type of benefit provided by a limb; diya is based on loss of this type, not on individual functional variations.
حكومة عدل (ḥukūmat 'adl): A fair compensation assessed by judges for injuries without fixed arsh.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In an accidental injury, a man loses his left hand. What diya is due?
A) Half diya, same as if he lost his right hand
B) Full diya because it is a hand
C) Half diya for the left, less than for the right
D) Only a hukuma, no fixed diya

Key Takeaway
The right and left hand have equal diya in accidental injury; the forearm requires additional hukuma according to the majority Hanafi view.

Qisas for Limb Cuts: Only After Healing
General rule stating condition for qisas on limbs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rule that qisas for intentional limb cutting requires healing of the wound and identify the condition that delays qisas.

Core Idea
Qisas for limb cuts is wajib only after the victim's wound heals.

This lesson presents a clear rule from Sharh al-Tahawi: for any intentional cutting of a limb, qisas (retaliation in kind) is not immediate. It must wait until the wound has fully healed. This condition ensures proportionality and prevents additional harm. Let's understand why and how this rule applies.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is intentionally cutting a limb (hand, foot, finger, etc.). The ruling is that qisas is wajib but subject to conditions.
2
Note the condition
The key condition is healing (bar') of the victim's wound. Without healing, qisas cannot be executed.
This is a shart for execution, not for the obligation itself.
3
Apply to examples
The rule covers hand, foot, finger, fingertip, or any joint cut. In each case, qisas is after healing.
4
Consequence of ignoring condition
If qisas is attempted before healing, it is invalid and the cutter may be liable for additional damages.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي شرح الطحاوي : ومن قطع من رجل يداً أو رجلاً أو أصبعاً أو نملة من أصبع أو ما سوى ذلك مفصلاً من المفصل عمداً فعليه القصاص بعد البرء من الجناية ولا قصاص عليه قبل ذلك
And in Sharh al-Tahawi: Whoever cuts from a man a hand, or a foot, or a finger, or the tip of a finger, or anything else joint by joint intentionally, then upon him is qisas after healing from the injury, and there is no qisas upon him before that.
Source pages p. 50

Commentary
This is a clear general rule: for any deliberate cutting of a limb or part thereof, qisas (retaliation in kind) is only carried out after the victim's wound has healed. Until healing, qisas is not permitted. The wisdom is to ensure proportionality and to avoid additional harm. This applies to hands, feet, fingers, and even the tip of a finger (anmala). The condition of healing is essential for the execution of qisas.

Key Terms
البرء من الجناية (al-bar' min al-jinaya): Complete healing of the wound inflicted by the assault.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When is qisas for an intentional cut of a hand executed?
A) Immediately after the cut
B) After the wound heals
C) Only if the victim dies
D) At the judge's discretion

Key Takeaway
Qisas for limb cuts is never immediate; it requires the victim's wound to heal completely.

Conditions for Qisas Between Different Statuses
Rulings on qisas applicability based on status differences.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which qisas is obligatory or replaced by arsh between individuals of different legal statuses according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Qisas requires equality in freedom, religion, and gender; inequality mandates arsh.

This lesson examines the Hanafi rules for qisas (retaliation) when a person intentionally cuts off another's limb. The key factor is the legal status of the parties: free vs slave, Muslim vs dhimmi, male vs female. The text states clear conditions for when qisas applies and when it is replaced by arsh (compensation). Mastering these conditions is essential for correctly applying Islamic criminal law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and general principle
The act is intentional cutting of a hand. Determine the default: qisas is the right of the victim unless a bar exists.
The passage classifies pairs where qisas runs vs. where it is replaced by arsh.
2
List pairs where qisas is obligatory
From the text: free Muslim/free Muslim, free kitabi/free kitabi, free Muslim/free kitabi (any combination), free Muslim woman/free Muslim woman, free kitabiyya/free kitabiyya, free Muslim woman/free kitabiyya, and both dhimmis.
Kitabis are Jews and Christians under dhimma.
3
List pairs where qisas is not obligatory
From the text: slave/slave, free/slave, and male/female (when one is male and the other female regardless of other statuses).
Note that if both are slaves, no qisas; if one is free and the other slave, no qisas; if one is male and the other female, no qisas.
4
State the alternative ruling
Where qisas does not apply, the remedy is arsh (financial compensation) payable immediately from the cutter's wealth.
Arsh is a fixed sum of money.
5
Understand the rationale
The underlying principle is kafa'a (equality). Qisas requires equality of status in freedom, religion, and gender. Inequality breaks the symmetry required for retaliation in kind.
This distinguishes the Hanafi position from the Shafi'i school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا قطع رجل يد آخر عمداً فإن كان القاطع والمقطوع حرين مسلمين أو كتابيين أو أحدهما مسلم والآخر كتابي يجري القصاص بينهما أو كانا امرأتين حرتين مسلمتين أو أحدهما مسلمة والأخرى كتابية أو كانتا ذميتين يجب القصاص. ولو كانا عبدين أو أحدهما عبد والآخر حر أو أحدهما ذكر والآخر أنثى فلا قصاص بينهما والأرش في ماله حالاً.
And if a man cuts the hand of another intentionally: if the cutter and the cut are both free Muslims, or both kitabis, or one Muslim and the other kitabi, qisas runs between them; or if they are both free Muslim women, or one Muslim woman and the other kitabiyya, or both dhimmis, qisas is obligatory. And if they are both slaves, or one is a slave and the other free, or one is male and the other female, then there is no qisas between them, and the arsh is in his wealth immediately.
Source pages p. 50

Commentary
This passage outlines the conditions for qisas between individuals of different legal statuses. Qisas is obligatory between free Muslims, free dhimmis (Jews/Christians), or between a Muslim and a dhimmi, as well as between free women of these categories. However, qisas does not apply when one party is a slave (even if the other is free), or when one is male and the other female. In such cases, the remedy is financial compensation (arsh) payable from the cutter's wealth immediately. The reasoning is based on the principle of equality (kafa'a) in qisas: the parties must be equal in legal status for retaliation in kind to be just.

Key Terms
كتابي (kitabi): A follower of a revealed scripture (Jew or Christian) under dhimma.
ذمي (dhimmi): A non-Muslim permanently residing in Islamic state with protected status.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Qisas applies because both are female.
B) No qisas, arsh from the woman's wealth.
C) No penalty because the victim is a slave.
D) Qisas on the woman's hand and arsh to the owner.

Key Takeaway
Qisas is obligatory only when both parties are equal in freedom, religion, and gender; otherwise, the penalty is financial compensation (arsh).
